	\section{First Order Logic}

	\section{von Neumann–Bernays–Gödel (NBG) Set Theory}
	
	\tcr{maybe just use iterated extensions to not worry about if stuff is well defined or small, etc}, see \href{https://mathoverflow.net/questions/51257/can-zfc-%E2%86%92-nbg-be-iterated}{iterated NBG math overflow}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{11001} 
		Let $x$ be a class. Then $x$ is said to be a set iff there exists a class $A$ such that $x \in A$. 
	\end{defn}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $x$ and $y$ be classes. Then $x$ is said to be a \tbf{subclass} of $y$, denoted $x \subset y$, if for each set $a$, $a \in x$ implies that $a \in y$. 
	\end{defn}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $x$ and $y$ be classes. Then $x$ is said to be \tbf{equal} to $y$ if $x \subset y$ and $y \subset x$. 
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ax} \lax{11001.1a} \textbf{Axiom of Extensionality:}  \\
		Let $x$ and $y$ be classes. If for each set $a$, $a \in x$ iff $a \in y$, then $x = y$.
	\end{ax}
	
	\begin{ax} \lax{11001.1b} \textbf{Axiom of Pairing:}  \\
		Let $a$, $b$ be sets. Then there exists a set $p$ such that for each for each set $x$, $x \in p$ iff $x = a$ or $x = b$. 
	\end{ax}

	\begin{defn}
		product of two classes
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $A$, $B$ be classes and $R \subset A \times B$. elation from $A$ to $B$.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		We can define cartesion products, relations, and functions for classes just like for sets. 
	\end{note}

	\begin{ex}
		Let $a$, $b$ be sets. Then there exists a unique set $p$ such that for each for each set $x$, $x \in p$ iff $x = a$ or $x = b$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		By \rax{11001.1b} implies that there exists a set $p$ such that for each for each set $x$, $x \in p$ iff $x = a$ or $x = b$. Let $q$ be a set. Suppose that for each for each set $x$, $x \in q$ iff $x = a$ or $x = b$. Then  
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $x$ and $y$ be sets. We define $(x,y) = \{\}$, denoted 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ax} \lax{11001.1} \textbf{Axiom of Replacement:}  \\
		Let $A$, $B$ be classes and $f:A \rightarrow B$. If $A$ is a set, then $f(A)$ is a set. 
	\end{ax}

	\begin{ax} \lax{11002} \textbf{Schema of Specification:}  \lax{11002}\\
		Let $\phi$ a propositional function on sets. Then there exists a class $A$ such that for each set $x$, $x \in A$ iff $\phi(x)$. 
	\end{ax}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{11003}
		There exists a class $A$ such that for each class $x$, $x \in A$ iff $x$ is a set.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Define $\phi$ by $$\phi(x) : x = x$$ 
		\rax{11002} implies that there exists a class $A$ such that for each set $x$, $x \in A$ iff $x = x$. Let $x$ be a class. If $x \in A$, then by definition, $x$ is a set. \\
		Conversely, if $x$ is a set, then by construction, $x \in A$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{11004}
		There exists a class $A$ such that for each class $G$ and $*: G \times G \rightarrow G$, $(G, *) \in A$ iff $(G, *)$ is a group.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Define $\phi_1$, $\phi_2$ and $\phi_3$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\phi_1(G, *): *:G \times G \rightarrow G$ is associative
			\item $\phi_2(G, *):$ there exists $e \in G$ such that for each $g \in G$, $e * g = g * e = g$
			\item $\phi_3(G, *):$ for each $g \in G$ there exists $h \in G$ such that $g * h = h * g = e$
		\end{itemize}
		Define $\phi$ by 
		$$\phi(G, *) : \phi_1(G, *) \text{ and } \phi_2(G, *) \text{ and } \phi_3(G, *)$$
		Then there exists a class $A$ such that for each set $G$ and  $*: G \times G \rightarrow G$, $(G, *) \in A$ iff $\phi(G, *)$ $(G, *) \text{ ``is a group"}$. Therefore, for each group $(G, *)$, $(G, *) \in A$.
		\textbf{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}

	\subsection{Relations}
	
	\tcr{can I define relations on classes instead of just sets? do i need to move this stuff before to prelim material since we need class functions which I guess are class relations?} \\
	\tcr{apparently yes } \href{https://arxiv.org/abs/2006.01613}{class,set theory notes (link, but already downloaded)}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $A, B$ be classes and $R \subset A \times B$. Then $R$ is said to be a \tbf{relation between $A$ and $B$}. 
		\tcr{write out 1st order logic definition like in notes} \href{https://arxiv.org/abs/2006.01613}{class,set theory notes (link, but already downloaded)}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $A,B,C$ be classes, $R$ a relation between $A$ and $B$, $S$ a relation between $B$ and $C$. We define the \tbf{composition relation of $R$ with $S$ between $A$ and $C$}, denoted $R \circ S$, by $R \circ S \defeq \{(a,c) \in A \times C: \text{there exists $b \in B$ such that $(a,b) \in R$ and $(b,c) \in S$}\}$.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{show composition of class relations exists}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $A,B, C, D$ be classes, $R$ a relation between $A$ and $B$, $S$ relation between $B$ and $C$ and $T$ relation between $C$ and $D$. Then $(T \circ S) \circ R = T \circ (S \circ R)$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $(a,d) \in (T \circ S) \circ R$. Then there exists $b \in B$ such that $(a,b) \in R$ and $(b,d) \in T \circ S$. Since $(b,d) \in T \circ S$, there exists $c \in C$ such that $(b,c) \in S$ and $(c,d) \in T$. Since $(a,b) \in R$ and $(b,c) \in S$, $(a,c) \in S \circ R$. Since $(a,c) \in S \circ R$ and $(c,d) \in T$, we have that $(a,d) \in T \circ (S \circ R)$. Since $(a,d) \in (T \circ S) \circ R$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $(a,d) \in (T \circ S) \circ R$, $(a,d) \in T \circ (S \circ R)$. Hence $(T \circ S) \circ R \subset T \circ (S \circ R)$.
			\item Similarly, $T \circ (S \circ R) \subset (T \circ S) \circ R$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Since $(T \circ S) \circ R \subset T \circ (S \circ R)$ and $T \circ (S \circ R) \subset (T \circ S) \circ R$, we have that $(T \circ S) \circ R = T \circ (S \circ R)$.
		
		\tcr{review, input any necessary axioms for classes}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $A$ be a class. We define the \tbf{diagonal relation on $A$}, denoted $\Del_A$, by $\Del_A \defeq \{(a,a): a \in A\}$. \tcr{make and show exists in a previous ex}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $A, B$ be classes and $R$ a relation between $A$ and $B$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $R \circ \Del_A = R$
			\item $\Del_B \circ R = R$
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $(a,b) \in R \circ \Del_A$. Then there exists $a' \in A$ such that $(a, a') \in \Del_A$ and $(a',b) \in R$. By definition of $\Del_A$, $a = a'$. Therefore $(a,b) \in R$. Since $(a,b) \in R \circ \Del_A$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $(a,b) \in R \circ \Del_A$, $(a,b) \in R$. Hence $ R \circ \Del_A \subset R$. 
				\item Let $(a,b) \in R$. Then $a \in A$. Therefore $(a,a) \in \Del_A$. Since $(a,a) \in \Del_A$ and $(a,b) \in R$, we have that $(a, b) \in R \circ \Del_A$. Since $(a,b) \in R$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $(a,b) \in R$, $(a,b) \in R \circ \Del_A$. Hence $R \circ \Del_A \subset R$.  
			\end{itemize}
			Since $R \circ \Del_A \subset R$ and $R \circ \Del_A \subset R$, we have that $R \circ \Del_A = R$.
			\item Similar to $(1)$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}

	\chapter{Basic Concepts}
	
	\section{Categories}
	
	\subsection{Introduction}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{12001}
		Let $\MC_0$, $\MC_1$ be classes and $\dom, \cod : \MC_1 \rightarrow \MC_0$. Define $\MC_1^{(2)}\subset \MC_1 \times \MC_1$ by $\MC_1^{(2)} \defeq \{(g,f) \in \MC_1 \times \MC_1 : \dom(g) = \cod(f) \}$. Let $\circ: \MC_1^{(2)} \rightarrow \MC_1$. Then $(\MC_0, \MC_1, \dom, \cod, \circ)$ is said to be a \textbf{category} if 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \tbf{(Composition):} \\ 
			for each $(g,f) \in \MC_1^{(2)}$, $\dom(g \circ f) = \dom(f)$ and $\cod(g \circ f) = \cod(g)$
			\item \tbf{(Associativity):} \\ 
			for each $f,g,h \in \MC_1$, if $(g,f), (h,g) \in \MC_1^{(2)}$, then 
			$$(h \circ g) \circ f = h \circ (g \circ f)$$  
			\item \tbf{(Identity):} \\ 
			for each $X \in \MC_0$, there exists $e \in \MC_1$ such that $\dom(e) = X$, $\cod(e) = X$ and for each $f, g \in \MC_1$, if $\dom(f) = X$ and $\cod(g) = X$, then 
			$$f \circ e = f \text{ and } e \circ g = g$$ 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Write $\MC = (\MC_0, \MC_1, \dom, \cod, \circ)$.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item We define the
			\begin{itemize}
				\item \textbf{objects of $\MC$}, denoted $\Obj(\MC)$, by $\Obj(\MC) \defeq \MC_0$
				\item \textbf{morphisms of $\MC$}, denoted $\Hom$, by $\Hom_{\MC} \defeq \MC_1$ 
				\item \textbf{domain function of $\MC$}, denoted $\dom_{\MC}$, by $\dom_{\MC} \defeq \dom$
				\item \textbf{codomain function of $\MC$}, denoted $\cod_{\MC}$, by $\cod_{\MC} \defeq \cod$
				\item \textbf{composition operator of $\MC$}, denoted $\circ_{\MC}$, by $\circ_{\MC} \defeq \circ$
			\end{itemize}
			\item For $X, Y \in \Obj(\MC)$, we define the \textbf{Morphisms of $\MC$ from $X$ to $Y$}, denoted $\Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$, by $\Hom_{\MC}(X, Y) \defeq \{f \in \Hom(\MC): \dom_{\MC}(f) = X \text{ and } \cod_{\MC}(f) = Y\}$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we write $\dom$, $\cod$ and $g \circ f$ in place of $\dom_{\MC}$, $\cod_{\MC}$ and $g \circ_{\MC} f$ respectively.
	\end{note}

	\begin{note} 
		We typically define a category $\MC$ by specifying 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\MC)$
			\item for $X,Y \in \Obj(\MC)$, the class $\Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$
			\item for $X,Y,Z \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(Y, Z)$, the composite morphism $g \circ f \in \Hom_{\MC}(X,Z)$.
		\end{itemize}
		and then show 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item well-definedness of composition
			\item associativity of composition 
			\item existence of identities 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15001} \textbf{Uniqueness of Identities:} \\
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, there exists a unique $e \in \Endo_{\MC}(A)$ such that for each $B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$, $f \circ e = f$ and $e \circ g = g$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{Existence:} \\
			Since $\MC$ is a category, by definition there exists $e \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, A)$ such that for each $B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$, $f \circ e = f$ and $e \circ g = g$. 
			\item \tbf{Uniqueness: } \\
			Let $e_1, e_2 \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, A)$. Suppose that for each $B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$, $f \circ e_1 = f$, $f \circ e_2 = f$, $e_1 \circ g = g$ and $e_2 \circ g = g$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				e_1
				& = e_2 \circ e_1 \\
				& = e_2.
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define the \tbf{identity morphism on $A$}, denoted $\id_A^{\MC} \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, A)$, to be the unique $e \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, A)$ such that for each $B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$, $f \circ e = f$ and $e \circ g = g$.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we write $\id_A$ in place of $\id_A^{\MC}$.
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{12002}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\MC$ is said to be 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \textbf{small} if $\Obj(\MC)$ and $\Hom_{\MC}$ are sets
			\item \textbf{locally small} if for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ is a set 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{12003}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. If $\MC$ is small, then $\MC$ is a set. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Then $\Obj(\MC)$ and $\Hom_{\MC}$ are sets. Then $\MP(\Obj(\MC))$, $\MP(\Hom_{\MC})$ and $\Obj(\MC)^{\Hom_{\MC}}$ are sets. Hence $\Obj(\MC) \times \Hom_{\MC} \times \Obj(\MC)^{\Hom_{\MC}} \times \Obj(\MC)^{\Hom_{\MC}}$ is a set. By definition, $\MC = (\Obj(\MC), \Hom_{\MC}, \dom, \cod) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \Hom_{\MC} \times \Obj(\MC)^{\Hom_{\MC}} \times \Obj(\MC)^{\Hom_{\MC}}$. By definition, $\MC$ is a set. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{12004}
		There exists a class $A$ such that $\MC \in A$ iff $\MC$ is a small category. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\rex{12003} implies that for each category $\MC$, $\MC$ is small implies that $\MC$ is a set. Define $\phi$ by $$\phi(\MC): \MC \text{ is a small category} $$ 
		Then \rax{11002} implies that there exists a class $A$ such that $\MC \in A$ iff $\MC$ is a small category.  
	\end{proof}
	
	\tcr{prosets}
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MP$ be a category. Then $\MP$ is said to be a 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \tbf{proset category} if for each $a, b \in \Obj(\MP)$, $\# \Hom_{\MP}(a,b) \leq 1$
			\item \tbf{poset category} if $\MP$ is a proset category and for each $a,b \in \Obj(\MP)$, $\# \Hom_{\MP}(a,b) = 1$ and $\# \Hom_{\MP}(b,a) = 1$ implies that $a = b$.  
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MP$ be a proset. Set $P \defeq \Obj(\MP)$. We define the \tbf{less-than-or-equal-to relation} on $P$, denoted ${\leq} \subset P \times P$, by 
		$${\leq} \defeq \{(a,b) \in P \times P: \Hom_{\MP}(a,b) \neq \varnothing\}.$$
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}  
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\MC$ is said to be \tbf{discrete} if $\Hom_{\MC} = \{\id_X: X \in \Obj(\MC)\}$. 
	\end{defn}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Fundamental Examples}

	\begin{defn} \ld{12001.1}
		We define the \textbf{empty category}, denoted $\0$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\0) = \varnothing$
			\item $\Hom_{\0} = \varnothing$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex} \lex{12001.2}
		We have that $\0$ is a category.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Vacuously true.
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn} \ld{12001.}
		We define the \textbf{trivial category}, denoted $\1$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\1) = \{*\}$
			\item $\Hom_{\1} = \{\id_*\}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex} \lex{12001.}
		We have that $\1$ is a category.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Clear.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{12001.}
		We define $\bSet$ by  
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\bSet) = \{A: A \text{ is a set}\}$ 
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\bSet)$, $\Hom_{\bSet}(A,B) = \{f: f:A \rightarrow B\}$
			\item for $A, B, C \in \bSet$, $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\bSet}(B, C)$, $g \circ_{\bSet} f = g \circ f$. 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex} \lex{12001.}
		We have that $\bSet$ is a category.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{well-definedness of composition:}
			\item \tbf{associativity of composition:} 
			\item \tbf{existence of identities:} 
		\end{itemize}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{Let $A,B \in \Obj(\bSet)$, show $\MR(A, B)$ is a category, (category of relations)}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{preordered set is a category}
	\end{ex}
	
	
	

	
	\tcr{FIX!!!! need to decide what to do about relations, on the one hand, we can define relations as classes like in the previous section, on another hand, we can define the category of relations based on $\bSet$, on the third hand, looking at `Elementary categories, elementary toposes` by mcLarty who shows you cand define relations in terms of subobjects, i.e. morphisms, does this more general idea also form a category, of which the category of relations based on set can be considered a subobject(i.e. a subcategory)?}
	\begin{defn}
		We define the \tbf{category of relations}, denoted $\bRel$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\bRel) \defeq \Obj(\bSet)$
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\bRel)$, $\Hom_{\bRel}(A, B) \defeq \MP(A \times B)$
			\item for each $A,B, C \in \Obj(\bRel)$, $R \in \Hom_{\bRel}(A, B)$ and $\Hom_{\bRel}(B, C)$, we define $S \circ_{\bRel} R \defeq \{(a,c) \in A \times C: \text{there exists $b \in B$ such that $(a,b) \in R$ and $(b,c) \in S$}\}$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{well-definedness of composition:} \\
			By definition, for each $A,B, C \in \Obj(\bRel)$, $R \in \Hom_{\bRel}(A, B)$ and $S \in \Hom_{\bRel}(B, C)$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				S \circ_{\bRel} R 
				& \in \MP (A \times C) \\
				& = \Hom_{\bRel}(A, C).
			\end{align*}
			So $\circ_{\bRel}$ is well-defined.
			\item \tbf{associativity of composition:} \\
			\tcr{ref ex in basic concepts chapter}
			\item \tbf{existence of identities:} \\
			\tcr{ref ex in basic concepts chapter}
		\end{itemize}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	

	
	
	\tcr{maybe discuss a quiver as a category whos objects are vertices and morphisms are  and composition is given by concatenation (i.e. I guess a quiver equipped with the path algebra), maybe this is not appropriate}
	\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quiver_(mathematics)#Path_algebra}{quiver wikipedia} 
	
	\begin{defn}
		We define the \tbf{category of quivers}, denoted $\bQuiv$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\bQuiv) \def \{\MQ: \text{$\MQ$ is a quiver}\}$
			\item for $\MQ$, $\ML \in \Obj(\bQuiv)$, 
			$$\Hom_{\bQuiv}(\MQ, \ML) \defeq \{\phi: \text{$\phi$ is a quiver} \}$$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	


















	













































	
	
	\subsection{Opposite Categories}

	\begin{defn}  \ld{12004}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, we define the \text{dual of $\MC$} or the \textbf{opposite of $\MC$}, denoted $\op{\MC}$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\op{\MC}) \defeq \Obj(\MC)$
			\item for $X,Y \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X,Y) \defeq \Hom_{\MC}(Y,X)$
			\item for $X, Y, Z \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, Y), g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(Y,Z)$, $g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f \defeq f \circ_{\MC} g$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex}  \lex{12005}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\op{\MC}$ is a category.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item for $W,X,Y,Z \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(W, X)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, Y)$ and $h \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(Y, Z)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				(h \circ_{\op{\MC}} g) \circ_{\op{\MC}} f 
				&= f \circ_{\MC}( h \circ_{\op{\MC}} g) \\
				&= f \circ_{\MC} (g \circ_{\MC} h) \\
				&= (f \circ_{\MC} g) \circ_{\MC} h \\
				&= h \circ_{\op{\MC}} (f \circ_{\MC} g) \\
				&= h \circ_{\op{\MC}} (g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f)
			\end{align*}
			So composition is associative.
			\item Let $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}$. Suppose that $\dom(f) = X$ and $\cod(g) = X$ 
			Then 
			\begin{align*}
				f  \circ_{\op{\MC}} \id_X
				&= \id_X  \circ_{\MC} f \\
				&= f
			\end{align*}
			and 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_X  \circ_{\op{\MC}} g 
				&= g \circ_{\MC} \id_X \\
				&= g
			\end{align*}
		So $(\id_X)_{\op{\MC}} =  (\id_X)_{\MC}$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{12005.1}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\op{(\op{\MC})}  = \MC$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Set $\MD \defeq \op{\MC}$.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item We have that
			\begin{align*}
				\Obj(\op{(\op{\MC})} )
				& = \Obj(\op{\MD}) \\
				& = \Obj(\MD), \quad \text{(by definition)} \\
				& = \Obj(\op{\MC}) \\
				& = \Obj(\MC), \quad \text{(by definition)}. 
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $X,Y \in \Obj(\op{(\op{\MC})} )$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\op{(\op{\MC})} }(X, Y) 
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MD}}(X, Y) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MD}(Y, X), \quad \text{(by definition)} \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(Y, X) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y), \quad \text{(by definition)}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MP$ be a category. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\MP$ is a proset iff $\op{\MP}$ is a proset
			\item $\MP$ is a poset iff $\op{\MP}$ is a poset
		\end{enumerate} 
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MP$ be a proset. Set $P \defeq \Obj(\MP)$. We define the \tbf{less-than-or-equal-to relation} on $P$, denoted ${\leq} \subset P \times P$, by 
		$${\leq} \defeq \{(a,b) \in P \times P: \Hom_{\op{\MP}}(a,b) \neq \varnothing\}.$$
	\end{defn}





































	
	
	
	























































	
	
	

	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Functors}
	
	
	\subsection{Introduction}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:intro:0001}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories and $F_0 : \Obj(\MC) \rightarrow \Obj(\MD)$, $F_1: \Hom_{\MC} \rightarrow \Hom_{\MD}$ class functions. Set $F = (F_0, F_1)$. Then $F$ is said to be a \text{$(\MC, \MD)$-functor}, denoted  $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$, if 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$, $F_1(f) \in \Hom_{\MD}(F_0(A), F_0(B))$
			\item for each $A,B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$, $F_1(g \circ f) = F_1(g) \circ F_1(f)$
			\item for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$,  $F_1(\id_A) = \id_{F_0(A)}$
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we may say ``functor" instead of ``$(\MC, \MD)$-functor".
	\end{note}

	\begin{note}
		For $A \in \Obj(C)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}$, we typically write $F(A)$ and $F(f)$ instead of $F_0(A)$ and $F_1(f)$ respectively.
		\tcr{maybe discuss how this is just a quiver homomorphism}
	\end{note}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:intro:0002}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. We define the \textbf{empty functor} from $\0$ to $\MC$, denoted $E_{\MC}: \0 \rightarrow \MC$ by $(E_{\MC})_0 \defeq \varnothing$ and = $(E_{\MC})_1 \defeq \varnothing$. 
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:intro:0003}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $E_{\MC}: \0 \rightarrow \MC$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Since $\Obj(\0) = \varnothing$ and $\Hom_{\0} = \varnothing$, this is vacuously true. 
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:intro:0004}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be categories and $X \in \Obj(\MD)$. We define the \textbf{constant functor} from $\MC$ onto $X$, denoted $\Del^{\MC}_X: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Del^{\MC}_X (A) = X$
			\item $\Del^{\MC}_X (f) = \id_X$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:intro:0005}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be categories and $X \in \Obj(\MD)$. Then $\Del^{\MC}_X : \MC \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\Del^{\MC}_X (f)
				& = \id_X \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, X) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MD}(\Del^{\MC}_X (A), \Del^{\MC}_X (B))
			\end{align*}  
			\item Let $A,B,C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\Del^{\MC}_X (g \circ f) 
				& = \id_X \\
				& = \id_X \circ \id_X \\
				& = \Del^{\MC}_X (g) \circ \Del^{\MC}_X (f)
			\end{align*} 
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\Del^{\MC}_X (\id_A)
				& = \id_X \\
				& = \id_{\Del^{\MC}_X (A)}
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		So $\Del^{\MC}_X : \MC \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}

	
	
	
	
	
	















































\subsection{Fundamental Examples}

\tcr{discuss a quiver as a functor from the free quiver (a category) to $\bSet$ or other category}
\href{https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quiver_(mathematics)#Path_algebra}{quiver wikipedia} 


\begin{note}
	We recall for $X,Y \in \Obj(\bSet)$, $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(X,Y)$, the image and preimage maps induced by $f$, denoted $f_* \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\MP(X), \MP(Y))$ and $f^* \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\MP(Y), \MP(X))$ are defined by $f_*(A) \defeq f(A)$ and $f^*(B) \defeq f^{-1}(B)$. \tcr{make exercise in set theory notes showing $(g \circ f)_* = g+* \circ f_*$ and similar for contravariant version}
\end{note}

\begin{defn}
	We define the 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item \tbf{image power set functor on $\bSet$}, denoted $\MP_*: \bSet \rightarrow \bSet$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\MP_*(X) \defeq \MP(X), \quad X \in \Obj(\bSet)$
			\item $\MP_*(f) \defeq f_*, \quad f \in \Hom_{\bSet}$
		\end{itemize}
		\item 
		\tbf{preimage power set functor on $\bSet$}, denoted $\MP^*: \op{\bSet} \rightarrow \bSet$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\MP^*(X) \defeq \MP(X), \quad X \in \Obj(\bSet)$
			\item $\MP^*(f) \defeq f^*, \quad f \in \Hom_{\bSet}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}

\begin{ex}
	We have that 
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item $\MP_*: \bSet \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor.
		\item $\MP^*: \op{\bSet} \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor.
	\end{enumerate}
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}\
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item For each $X,Y \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(X,Y)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\MP_*(f)
				& = f_* \\
				& \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\MP(X), \MP(Y)) \quad \tcr{(ref ex in set theory section intro to math notes)}\\
				& = \Hom_{\bSet}(\MP_*(X), \MP_*(Y)).
			\end{align*}
			\item 
			For each $X,Y,Z \in \Obj(\bSet)$, $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(X,Y)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\bSet}(Y,Z)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\MP_*(g \circ_{\bSet} f)
				& = (g \circ_{\bSet} f)_* \\
				& = g_* \circ_{\bSet} f_* \quad \text{(ref ex in set theory section intro to math notes)} \\
				& = \MP_*(g) \circ_{\bSet} \MP_*(f).
			\end{align*}
			\item 
			For each $X \in \Obj(\bSet)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\MP_*(\id_X^{\bSet})
				& = \id_{\MP(X)}^{\bSet} \quad \text{(ref ex in set theory section intro to math notes)} \\
				& = \id_{\MP_*(X)}^{\bSet}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $\MP_*: \bSet \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor.
		\item 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $X,Y \in \Obj(\op{\bSet})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\bSet}}(X,Y)$. Then $X \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(Y, X)$. Therefore
			\begin{align*}
				\MP^*(f)
				& = f^* \\
				& \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\MP(X), \MP(Y)) \quad \tcr{(ref ex in set theory section intro to math notes)} \\
				& = \Hom_{\bSet}(\MP^*(X), \MP^*(Y)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $X,Y \in \Obj(\op{\bSet})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\bSet}}(X,Y)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $X,Y \in \Obj(\op{\bSet})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\bSet}}(X,Y)$, $\MP^*(f) \in \Hom_{\op{\bSet}}(\MP^*(X), \MP^*(Y))$.
			\item 
			Let $X,Y,Z \in \Obj(\op{\bSet})$, $f \in \Hom_{\op{\bSet}}(X,Y)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\op{\bSet}}(Y,Z)$. Then $X,Y,Z \in \Obj(\bSet)$, $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(Y,X)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\bSet}(Z,Y)$. Therefore
			\begin{align*}
				\MP^*(g \circ_{\op{\bSet}} f)
				& = (g \circ_{\op{\bSet}} f)^* \\
				& = (f \circ_{\bSet} g)^* \\
				& = g^* \circ_{\bSet} f^* \quad \text{(ref ex in set theory section intro to math notes)} \\
				& = \MP^*(g) \circ_{\bSet} \MP^*(f).
			\end{align*}
			\item 
			For each $X \in \Obj(\op{\bSet})$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\MP^*(\id_X^{\op{\bSet}})
				& = (\id_X^{\op{\bSet}})^* \\
				& = (\id_X^{\bSet}) \\
				& = \id_{\MP(X)}^{\op{\bSet}} \quad \text{(ref ex in set theory section intro to math notes)} \\
				& = \id_{\MP^*(X)}^{\op{\bSet}}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $\MP^*: \op{\bSet} \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor.
	\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

%\begin{defn}
%	We define the \tbf{Boolean exponential functor on $\bSet$}, denoted $\Exp((-, \{0,1\})): \op{\bSet} \rightarrow \bSet$ by 
%	\begin{itemize}
%		\item $\Exp((-, \{0,1\}))(X) \defeq \{0,1\}^X, \quad X \in \Obj(\bSet)$
%		\item $\Exp((-, \{0,1\}))(f) \defeq (-) \circ_{\bSet} f, \quad f \in \Hom_{\bSet}$
%	\end{itemize}
%\end{defn}
%
%\begin{ex}
%	We have that $\Exp_{\bSet}(-, \{0,1\}) \op{\bSet} \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor. 
%\end{ex}

	\subsection{Category of Small Categories}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:small_cat:0001}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ and $\ME$ be categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$, $G: \MD \rightarrow \ME$ functors. We define the \textbf{composition of $G$ with $F$}, denoted $G \circ F: \MC \rightarrow \ME$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $G \circ F (A) \defeq G(F(A))$
			\item $G \circ F (f) \defeq G(F(f))$
		\end{itemize} 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		Writing $G \circ F = (H_0, H_1)$, we have that $H_0 = G_0 \circ F_0$ and $H_1 = G_1 \circ F_1$. 
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0002}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ and $\ME$ be categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$, $G: \MD \rightarrow \ME$ functors. Then  $G \circ F: \MC \rightarrow \ME$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
				\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Since $F(f) \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), F(B))$, we have that $G(F(f)) \in \Hom_{\ME}(G(F(A)), G(F(B)))$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				G \circ F (f) 
				& = G(F(f)) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\ME}(G(F(A)), G(F(B))) \\
				& =  \Hom_{\ME}(G \circ F(A), G \circ F (B)) \\
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A,B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				G \circ F(g \circ f) 
				& = G (F (g \circ f)) \\
				& = G(F(g) \circ F(f)) \\
				& = G(F(g)) \circ G(F(f)) \\
				& = G \circ F (g) \circ G \circ F (f) \\
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				G \circ F(\id_{A})
				& = G(F(\id_A) )\\
				& = G(\id_{F(A)}) \\
				& = \id_{G(F(A))} \\
				& = \id_{G \circ F(A)} 
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		So $G \circ F: \MC \rightarrow \ME$ is a functor. 
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0003}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$, $\ME$, $\MF$ be categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$, $G : \MD \rightarrow \ME$, $H: \ME \rightarrow \MF$ functors. Then $(H \circ G) \circ F = H \circ (G \circ F)$.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then 
		\begin{itemize}
				\item 
				\begin{align*}
					(H \circ G) \circ F(A) 
					& = H \circ G (F(A)) \\
					& = H (G(F(A))) \\
					& = H( G \circ F (A)) \\
					& = H \circ (G \circ F) (A)
				\end{align*}
				\item  
				\begin{align*}
					(H \circ G) \circ F(f) 
					& = H \circ G (F(f)) \\
					& = H (G(F(f))) \\
					& = H( G \circ F (f)) \\
					& = H \circ (G \circ F) (f)
				\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
		Hence $(H \circ G) \circ F = H \circ (G \circ F)$.
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:small_cat:0004}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. We define the \textbf{identity functor from $\MC$ to $\MC$}, denoted $\id_{\MC}: \MC \rightarrow \MC$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\id_{\MC}(A) \defeq A, \quad (A \in \Obj(\MC))$
			\item $\id_{\MC}(f) \defeq f, \quad (f \in \Hom_{\MC})$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0005}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\id_{\MC}: \MC \rightarrow \MC$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MC}(f) 
				& = f \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\id_{\MC}(A), \id_{\MC}(B)) \\
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A,B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MC}(g \circ f) 
				& = g \circ f \\
				& = \id_{\MC}(g) \circ \id_{\MC} (f)
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MC}(\id_{A})
				& = \id_A \\
				& = \id_{\id_{\MC}(A)}
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0006}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\id_{\MD} \circ F = F$
			\item $F \circ \id_{\MC} = F$
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MD} \circ F(A) 
				& = \id_{\MD}(F(A)) \\
				& = F(A)
			\end{align*}
			and 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MD} \circ F(f) 
				& = \id_{\MD}(F(f)) \\
				& = F(f)
			\end{align*} 
			Since $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ are arbitrary, $\id_{\MD} \circ F = F$.
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				F \circ \id_{\MC}(A) 
				& = F(\id_{\MC}(A)) \\
				& = F(A) 
			\end{align*}
			and 
			\begin{align*}
				F \circ \id_{\MC}(f) 
				& = F (\id_{\MC}(f)) \\
				& = F(f)
			\end{align*} 
			Since $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$ are arbitrary, $ F \circ \id_{\MC} = F$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0007}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$. If $\MC$ is small, then $F$ is a set.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Then $\Obj(\MC)$ and $\Hom_{\MC}$ are sets. By definition, there exist $F_0: \Obj(\MC) \rightarrow \Obj(\MD)$ and $F_1: \Hom_{\MC} \rightarrow \Hom_{\MD}$ such that $F = (F_0, F_1)$. \rax{11001.1} implies that $F_0(\Obj(\MC))$ and $F_1(\Hom_{\MC})$ are sets. Therefore, $\Obj(\MC) \times F_0(\Obj(C))$ and $\Hom_{\MC} \times F_1(\Hom_{\MC})$ are sets. Hence $\MP(\Obj(\MC) \times F_0(\Obj(C)))$ and $\MP(\Hom_{\MC} \times F_1(\Hom_{\MC}))$ are sets. Since $F_0 \subset \Obj(\MC) \times F_0(\Obj(C))$ and $F_1 \subset \Hom_{\MC} \times F_1(\Hom_{\MC})$, we have that $F_0 \in \MP(\Obj(\MC) \times F_0(\Obj(C)))$ and $F_1 \in \MP(\Hom_{\MC} \times F_1(\Hom_{\MC}))$. Hence $F_0$ and $F_1$ are sets. Thus $F = (F_0, F_1)$ is a set. 
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0008}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Then there exists a class $A$ such that for each class $F$, $F \in A$ iff $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$.   
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof} 
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Define $\phi$ by 
		$$\phi(F) : F : \MC \rightarrow \MD$$ 
		Then there exists a class $A$ such that for each set $F$, $F \in A$ iff $\phi(F)$. Let $F$ be a class. Suppose that $F \in A$. By \rd{11001}, $F$ is a set. Since $F$ is a set and $F \in A$, we have that $\phi(F)$. Hence $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. \\
		Conversely, suppose that $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0007} implies that $F$ is a set. Since $F$ is a set and $\phi(F)$ is true, we have that $F \in A$. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:small_cat:0009}
		We define $\tbf{Cat}$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\tbf{Cat}) = \{\MC: \MC \text{ is a small category}\}$.
			\item for $\MC,\MD \in \Obj(\tbf{Cat})$, 
			$$\Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC,\MD) = \{F : F: \MC \rightarrow \MD \}$$
			\item for $\MC,\MD, \ME \in \Obj(\tbf{Cat})$, $F \in \Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC,\MD)$ and $G \in \Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MD, \ME)$, $$G \circ_{\tbf{Cat}} F = G \circ F$$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}


	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0010}
		We have that \tbf{Cat} is 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item a category
			\item locally small
		\end{enumerate} 
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0002} implies that composition is well defined. \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0003} implies that composition is associative. \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0005} and \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0006} imply the existence of identities.
			\item Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\tbf{Cat})$ and $F \in \Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC, \MD)$. \rd{12002} implies that $\Obj(\MC)$, $\Obj(\MD)$, $\Hom_{\MC}$ and $\Hom_{\MD}$ are sets. Then $\Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)}$ and $\Hom_{\MD}^{ \Hom_{\MC}}$ are sets. Hence $ \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)} \times  \Hom_{\MD}^{ \Hom_{\MC}}$ is a set. Let $F \in \Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC, \MD)$. Then there exist $F_0 \in \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)} $ and $F_1 \in \Hom_{\MD}^{ \Hom_{\MC}}$ such that $F = (F_0, F_1)$. Therefore $F \in  \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)} \times  \Hom_{\MD}^{ \Hom_{\MC}}$. Since $F \in \Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC, \MD)$ is arbitrary, 
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC, \MD) 
				& \subset \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)} \times  \Hom_{\MD}^{ \Hom_{\MC}}
			\end{align*}
			which implies that $\Hom_{\tbf{Cat}}(\MC, \MD)$ is a set. Therefore, $\tbf{Cat}$ is locally small.
		\end{enumerate} 
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	















	\subsection{Comma Categories}

	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:comma_cat:0001}
		Let $\MA$, $\MB$, $\MC$ be a categories and $S: \MA \rightarrow \MC$, $T: \MB \rightarrow \MC$ functors. We define the \textbf{comma category of $S$ to $T$}, denoted $(S \doar T)$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(S \doar T) = \{(A, B, h): A \in \Obj(\MA), B \in \Obj(\MB) \text{, and } h \in \Hom_{\MC}(S(A), T(B))\}$
			\item For $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2) \in \Obj(S \doar T)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				& \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2)) = \\
				& \quad \quad \{(\al, \be): \al \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2) \text{, } \be \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2) \text{ and } T(\be) \circ_{\MC} h_1 = h_2 \circ_{\MC} S(\al)\}
			\end{align*}
			i.e. for $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2) \in \Obj(S \doar T)$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$, $(\al, \be) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$ iff the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				S(A_1) \arrow[r, "S(\al)"] \arrow[d, "h_1"'] & S(A_2)  \arrow[d, "h_2"] \\
				T(B_1) \arrow[r, "T(\be)"']                 & T(B_2)
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item For 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_3, B_3, h_3) \in \Obj(S \doar T)$
				\item $(\al_{12}, \be_{12}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$
				\item $(\al_{23}, \be_{23}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_3, B_3, h_3))$
			\end{itemize}
			we define 
			$$(\al_{23}, \be_{23}) \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\al_{12}, \be_{12}) = (\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12}, \be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12})$$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:comma_cat:0002}
		Let $\MA$, $\MB$, $\MC$ be a categories and $S: \MA \rightarrow \MC$, $T: \MB \rightarrow \MC$ functors. Then $(S \doar T)$ is a category.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \textbf{well-definedness of composition:} \\
			Let 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_3, B_3, h_3) \in \Obj(S \doar T)$
				\item $(\al_{12}, \be_{12}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$ 
				\item $(\al_{23}, \be_{23}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_3, B_3, h_3))$
			\end{itemize}
			By definition, $\al_{12} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $\al_{23} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_2, A_3)$, $\be_{12} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$, $\be_{23} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_2, B_3)$, $T(\be_{12}) \circ_{\MC} h_1 = h_2 \circ S(\al_{12})$ and $T(\be_{23}) \circ_{\MC} h_2 = h_3 \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{23})$, \\
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				S(A_1) \arrow[r, "S(\al_{12})"] \arrow[d, "h_1"'] & S(A_2)  \arrow[d, "h_2"] \arrow[r, "S(\al_{23})"] 
				& S(A_3) \arrow[d, "h_3"]\\
				T(B_1) \arrow[r, "T(\be_{12})"']                  & T(B_2)                   \arrow[r, "T(\be_{23})"'] 
				& T(B_3) 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Then $\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_3)$, $\be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_3)$ and 
			\begin{align*}
				T(\be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12}) \circ_{\MC} h_1
				& = (T(\be_{23}) \circ_{\MC} T(\be_{12})) \circ_{\MC} h_1 \\
				& = T(\be_{23}) \circ_{\MC} (T(\be_{12}) \circ_{\MC} h_1) \\
				& = T(\be_{23}) \circ_{\MC} (h_2 \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{12})) \\
				& = (T(\be_{23}) \circ_{\MC} h_2) \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{12}) \\
				& = (h_3 \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{23})) \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{12}) \\
				& = h_3 \circ_{\MC} (S(\al_{23}) \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{12})) \\
				& = h_3 \circ_{\MC} S(\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12})
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				S(A_1) \arrow[rr, "S(\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12})"] \arrow[d, "h_1"']&  & S(A_3)  \arrow[d, "h_3"] \\
				T(B_1) \arrow[rr, "T(\be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12})"']                       &  & T(B_3)
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Hence $(\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12}, \be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_3, B_3, h_3))$ and composition is well defined. \\
			\item \textbf{associativity of composition:} \\
			Let 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_3, B_3, h_3), (A_4, B_4, h_4) \in \Obj(S \doar T)$
				\item $(\al_{12}, \be_{12}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$ 
				\item $(\al_{23}, \be_{23}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_3, B_3, h_3))$
				\item $(\al_{34}, \be_{34}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_3, B_3, h_3), (A_4, B_4, h_4))$
			\end{itemize}
			Then 
			\begin{align*}
				[ (\al_{34}, \be_{34}) \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\al_{23}, \be_{23}) ] \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\al_{12}, \be_{12})
				& = (\al_{34} \circ_{\MA} \al_{23}, \be_{34} \circ_{\MB} \be_{23}) \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\al_{12}, \be_{12}) \\
				& = ([\al_{34} \circ_{\MA} \al_{23}] \circ_{\MA} \al_{12}, [\be_{34} \circ_{\MB} \be_{23}] \circ_{\MB} \be_{12}) \\
				& =  (\al_{34} \circ_{\MA} [\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12}], \be_{34} \circ_{\MB} [\be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12}]) \\
				& = (\al_{34}, \be_{34}) \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\al_{23} \circ_{\MA} \al_{12}, \be_{23} \circ_{\MB} \be_{12}) \\
				& = (\al_{34}, \be_{34}) \circ_{(S \doar T)} [(\al_{23}, \be_{23}) \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\al_{12}, \be_{12})]
			\end{align*}
			So composition is associative. \\
			\item \textbf{existence of identities:} \\
			Let
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2), \in \Obj(S \doar T)$
				\item $(\al, \be) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$ 
			\end{itemize}
			By definition, 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\al \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $\be \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$
				\item $h_1 \in \Hom_{\MC}(S(A_1), T(B_1))$, $h_2 \in \Hom_{\MC}(S(A_2), T(B_2))$ 
				\item $T(\be) \circ h_1 = h_2 \circ S(\al)$
			\end{itemize}
			Since $\id_{A_1} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_1)$, $\id_{B_1} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_1)$, and
			\begin{align*}
				T(\id_{B_1}) \circ_{\MC}  h_1 
				& = \id_{T(B_1)} \circ_{\MC} h_1 \\
				& = h_1 \\
				& = h_1 \circ_{\MC} \id_{S(A_1)} \\
				& = h_1 \circ_{\MC} S(\id_{A_1}) 
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				S(A_1) \arrow[r, "S(\id_{A_1})"] \arrow[d, "h_1"']  & S(A_1)  \arrow[d, "h_1"] \\
				T(B_1) \arrow[r, "T(\id_{B_1})"']                   & T(B_1)
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			we have that $(\id_{A_1}, \id_{B_1}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_1, B_1, h_1))$. Similarly $(\id_{A_2}, \id_{B_2}) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_2, B_2, h_2), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$. Therefore
			\begin{align*}
				(\al, \be) \circ_{(S \doar T)} (\id_{A_1}, \id_{B_1}) 
				& = (\al \circ_{\MA} \id_{A_1}, \be \circ_{\MB} \id_{B_1}) \\
				& = (\al, \be)
			\end{align*}
			and 
			\begin{align*}
				(\id_{A_2}, \id_{B_2}) \circ_{(S\doar T)} (\al, \be) 
				& = (\id_{A_2} \circ_{\MA} \al ,  \id_{B_2} \circ_{\MB} \be ) \\
				& = (\al, \be)
			\end{align*}
			Since $(A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2), \in \Obj(S \doar T)$ and\\ $(\al, \be) \in \Hom_{(S \doar T)}((A_1, B_1, h_1), (A_2, B_2, h_2))$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $(A, B, h) \in \Obj(S \doar T)$, $\id_{(A, B, h)} = (\id_A, \id_B)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		\tcr{define the arrow category of $\MC$} \href{URL}{text}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{note}
		\tcr{explain with diagram how in the case $\al = \Del^{\1}_X$ and how we can contract one edge of the rectangle diagram to get a triangle}
	\end{note}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:comma_cat:0003}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be a categories, $X \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. We define the \textbf{comma category from $X$ to $F$}, denoted $(X \doar F)$, by $(X \doar F) \defeq (\Del^{\1}_X \doar F)$. \\
		We may make the following identification:
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(X \doar F) = \{(A, f): A \in \Obj(\MC) \text{ and } f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, F(A))\}$ 
			\item For $(A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2) \in \Obj(X \doar F)$, 
			$$\Hom_{(X \doar F)}((A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2)) = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2) \text{ and } F(\al) \circ f_1 = f_2\}$$
			i.e. for $(A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2) \in \Obj(X \doar F)$ and $\al \in \Hom_{A_1, A_2}$, $\al \in \Hom_{(X \doar F)}((A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2))$ iff the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				&  X \arrow[dl, "f_1"']  \arrow[dr, "f_2"] & \\
				F(A_1)  \arrow[rr, "F(\al)"'] &&  F(A_2) \\ 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item For 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2), (A_3, f_3) \in \Obj(X \doar F)$
				\item $\al \in \Hom_{(X \doar F)}((A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2))$
				\item $\be \in \Hom_{(X \doar F)}((A_2, f_2), (A_3, f_3))$
			\end{itemize}
			we define 
			$$\be \circ_{(X \doar F)} \al = \be \circ_{\MC} \al $$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		\tcr{note that the coslice category under $X$ is a comma categroy from $X$ to $\id_{\MC}$}
	\end{note}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:comma_cat:0004}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be a categories, $X \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. We define the \textbf{comma category from $F$ to $X$}, denoted $(F \doar X)$, by $(F \doar X) \defeq (F \doar \Del^{\1}_X)$.\\
		We may make the following identification:
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(F \doar X) = \{(A, f): A \in \Obj(\MC) \text{ and } f \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), X)\}$ 
			\item For $(A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2) \in \Obj(F \doar X)$, 
			$$\Hom_{(X \doar F)}((A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2)) = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2) \text{ and } f_2 \circ F(\al)  = f_1\}$$
			i.e. for $(A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2) \in \Obj(F \doar X)$ and $\al \in \Hom_{A_1, A_2}$, $\al \in \Hom_{(F \doar X)}((A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2))$ iff the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(A_1) \arrow[dr, "f_1"'] \arrow[rr, "F(\al)"] &&  F(A_2) \arrow[dl, "f_2"]\\
				& X  & 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item For 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2), (A_3, f_3) \in \Obj(F \doar X)$
				\item $\al \in \Hom_{(F \doar X)}((A_1, f_1), (A_2, f_2))$
				\item $\be \in \Hom_{(F \doar X)}((A_2, f_2), (A_3, f_3))$
			\end{itemize}
			we define 
			$$\be \circ_{(F \doar X)} \al = \be \circ_{\MC} \al $$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{12006}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define the \textbf{arrow category of $\MC$}, denoted $\Arr(\MC)$, by $\Arr(\MC) \defeq (\id_{\MC} \downarrow \id_{\MC})$.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{12007}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define the \textbf{slice category of $\MC$ over $X$} or the \textbf{over category of $\MC$ over $X$}, denoted $\MC \downarrow X$, by $\MC \downarrow X \defeq (\id_{\MC} \downarrow X)$.
	\end{defn}
	
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{12008}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define the \textbf{coslice category of $\MC$ over $X$} or the \textbf{under category of $\MC$ under $X$}, denoted $X \downarrow \MC$, by $X \downarrow \MC \defeq (X \downarrow \id_{\MC})$.
	\end{defn}

	\tcr{give examples in posets, and other}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Natural Transformations}
	
	\subsection{Introduction}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:intro:0001}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories, $F, G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $ \al : \Obj(\MC) \rightarrow  \Hom_{\MD}$. Then $\al$ is said to be a \textbf{natural transformation from $F$ to $G$}, denoted $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, if
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\al_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$
			\item for each $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$, $G(f) \circ \al_A = \al_B \circ F(f)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(A)  \arrow[r, "\al_A"]  \arrow[d, "F(f)"']  & G(A)   \arrow[d, "G(f)"]\\
				F(B) \arrow[r, "\al_B"'] &  G(B) 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:intro:0002} \tbf{Horizontal Composition:} \\
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories, $F, G:\MA \rightarrow \MB$, $F', G': \MB \rightarrow \MC$ functors and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, $\al' : F' \Rightarrow G'$ natural transformations. We define the \textbf{horizontal composition of $\be$ with $\al$}, denoted $\be * \al: F' \circ F \Rightarrow G' \circ G$, by  
		$$(\al' * \al)_A = \al'_{G(A)} \circ F' (\al_A)$$ 
	\end{defn}
	
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0003}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories, $F, G:\MA \rightarrow \MB$, $F', G': \MB \rightarrow \MC$ functors and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, $\al' : F' \Rightarrow G'$ natural transformations. Then $ \al' \circ \al: F' \circ F \Rightarrow G' \circ G$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MA)$. Since $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, we have that $\al_A \in \Hom_{\MB}(F(A), G(A))$. Since $F':\MB \rightarrow \MC$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				F'(\al_A) 
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F'(F(A)), F'(G(A))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ F(A), F' \circ G(A)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $G:\MA \rightarrow \MB$, we have that $G(A) \in \Obj(\MB)$. Since $\al':F' \Rightarrow G'$, we have that  
			\begin{align*}
				\al'_{G(A)} 
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F'(G(A)), G'(G(A))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ G(A), G' \circ G(A)). 
			\end{align*}
			Therefore 
			\begin{align*}
				(\al' * \al)_A 
				& = \al'_{G(A)} \circ F' (\al_A) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ F(A), G' \circ G(A)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $A \in \Obj(\MA)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$, $(\al' * \al)_A \in \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ F(A), G' \circ G(A))$.
			\item Let $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$. Since $F,G:\MA \rightarrow \MB$, we have that $F(f) \in \Hom_{\MB}(F(A_1), F(A_2))$ and $G(f) \in \Hom_{\MB}(G(A_1), G(A_2))$. Since $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, we have that for each $k \in [2]$, $\al_{A_k} \in \Hom_{\MB}(F(A_k), G(A_k))$ and $G(f) \circ \al_{A_1} = \al_{A_2} \circ F(f)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(A_1)  \arrow[r, "\al_{A_1}"]  \arrow[d, "F(f)"']  & G(A_1)   \arrow[d, "G(f)"]\\
				F(A_2) \arrow[r, "\al_{A_2}"'] &  G(A_2) 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Since $F',G': \MB \rightarrow \MC$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				F' \circ F(f)
				& = F'(F(f)) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F'(F(A_1)), F'(F(A_2))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ F(A_1), F' \circ F(A_2)),
			\end{align*}
			\begin{align*}
				F' \circ G(f)
				& = F'(G(f)) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F'(G(A_1)), F'(G(A_2))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ G(A_1), F' \circ G(A_2)),
			\end{align*}
			\begin{align*}
				G' \circ G(f)
				& = G'(G(f)) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(G'(G(A_1)), G'(G(A_2))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(G' \circ G(A_1), G' \circ G(A_2)),
			\end{align*}
			and for each $k \in [2]$, 
			\begin{align*}
				F'(\al_{A_k}) 
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F'(F(A_k)), F'(G(A_k))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ F(A_k), F' \circ G(A_k)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $\al': F' \Rightarrow G'$, we have that for each $k \in [2]$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\al'_{G(A_k)}
				& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F'(G(A_k)), G'(G(A_k))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(F' \circ G(A_k), G' \circ G(A_k)).
			\end{align*}
			Therefore 
			\begin{align*}
				[F' \circ G (f)] \circ F'(\al_{A_1})
				& = F'(G(f)) \circ F'(\al_{A_1}) \\
				& = F'(G(f) \circ \al_{A_1}) \\
				& = F'(\al_{A_2} \circ F(f)) \\
				& = F'(\al_{A_2}) \circ F'(F(f)) \\
				& = F'(\al_{A_2}) \circ [F' \circ F(f)],
			\end{align*}
			and 
			\begin{align*}
				[G' \circ G(f)] \circ \al'_{G(A_1)}
				& = G'(G(f)) \circ \al'_{G(A_1)} \\
				& = \al'_{G(A_2)} \circ F'(G(f)) \\
				& =  \al'_{G(A_2)} \circ [F' \circ G(f)],
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F' \circ F(A_1)  \arrow[r, "F'(\al_{A_1})"]  \arrow[d, "F' \circ F(f)"']  & F' \circ G(A_1)   \arrow[d, "F' \circ G(f)"] \arrow[r, "\al'_{G(A_1)}"]    & G' \circ G(A_1)   \arrow[d, "G' \circ G(f)"] \\
				F' \circ F(A_2) \arrow[r, "F'(\al_{A_2})"'] &  F' \circ G(A_2) \arrow[r, "\al'_{G(A_2)}"'] &  G' \circ G(A_2) 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\] 
			Hence 
			\begin{align*}
				[G' \circ G(f)] \circ (\al' * \al)_{A_1}
				& = [G' \circ G(f)] \circ [\al'_{G(A_1)} \circ F'(\al_{A_1})] \\
				& = ([G' \circ G(f)] \circ \al'_{G(A_1)}) \circ F'(\al_{A_1}) \\
				& = (\al'_{G(A_2)} \circ [F' \circ G(f)]) \circ F'(\al_{A_1}) \\
				& = \al'_{G(A_2)} \circ ([F' \circ G(f)] \circ F'(\al_{A_1})) \\
				& = \al'_{G(A_2)} \circ (F'(\al_{A_2}) \circ [F' \circ F(f)]) \\
				& = [\al'_{G(A_2)} \circ F'(\al_{A_2})] \circ [F' \circ F(f)] \\
				& = (\al' * \al)_{A_2} \circ [F' \circ F(f)],
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F' \circ F(A_1)  \arrow[r, "(\al' * \al)_{A_1}"]  \arrow[d, "F' \circ F(f)"']  & G' \circ G(A_1)   \arrow[d, "G' \circ G(f)"]\\
				F' \circ F(A_2) \arrow[r, "(\al' * \al)_{A_2}"'] &  G' \circ G(A_2) 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Since $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $[G' \circ G(f)] \circ (\al' * \al)_{A_1} = (\al' * \al)_{A_2} \circ [F' \circ F(f)]$.
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $\al' * \al: F' \circ F \Rightarrow G' \circ G$.
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:intro:0004} \tbf{Whiskering:}
		\begin{itemize}
			\item 
			\item 
		\end{itemize}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{defn}
	
	
	

	\tcr{talk about following example}
	\href{https://pseudonium.github.io/2026/01/20/Preimages_Preserve_Subset_operations.html}{preimages and set comprehension vs post composition and predicates}
	\tcr{will need to talk about contravariant functors from $\text{preim}, \text{pred}$, denoted $F,G:\bSet \rightarrow \bSet$ respectively given by $F(X) \defeq \MP(X)$, $F(f) \defeq f^{-1}$ and $G(X) \defeq \{0,1\}^X$, $G(f) \defeq - \circ f$.}	
	This post/functor is interesting because it highlights the associativity of $(\text{NOT} \circ \phi) \circ f = \text{NOT} \circ (\phi \circ f)$ as a commutativity $f^{-1}(A^c) = (f^{-1}(A))^c$. That is if $X = f^{-1}$ and $Y = -^c$, then $XYA = YXA$ so that $XY = YX$. It begs the question whether or not commutativity can always be recast as associativity in some other context. 
	
	
	\tcr{below is wild speculation and off topic question}
	The author writes that associativity shows you that for any appropriate $f, \phi$, post composing with $\text{NOT}$ first and then pre composing with $f$ vs precomposing with $f$ first then poste composing with $\text{NOT}$ are the same thing and in a sense orthogonal and independent, as in they do not affect the outcome. So is there a general view in which associativity (or via natural transformation commutativity) is a measure of independence? 
	
	Can we connect this with probability/physics in an information theoretic sense using the motivation/intuition that the kl divergence (or other notion of info loss) is a functor? i.e. $XY = YX$ or $x \circ (y \circ a) = (x \circ y) \circ a$ iff $\text{info\_loss}[\text{joint}(X,Y), \otimes(X,Y)] = 0$ or some generalization? We would need a notion of joint for $X$ and $Y$ and a (not product because category of prob dists doesnt have products) tensor product, so maybe we need to consider monoidal cats) 
	
	what $X,Y$ would correspond to classical/quantum probability? In the classical/quantum case, $X,Y$ are marginal systems and $\text{joint}(X,Y)$ is the given bipartite system from which we isolate the marginals. In the classical case, $\text{info\_loss}[\text{joint}(X,Y), \otimes(X,Y)] = 0$ iff $\text{joint}(X,Y) = \otimes(X,Y)]$, that is, there is the two marginal states of the bipartite system contain as much information as the bipartite system itself, i.e. there is no interaction. Im not sure what the associated commuting/associative operations would be, but maybe we can get a clue from the above example or by looking further into similar examples, maybe toposes or other tools cover this? 
	
	If it were possible to find commutative/associative operations that capture two subsystems being independent and not having an interaction in the classical/quantum probabilistic sense, then this would seem to suggest that we would be able to recast interaction between subsystems in terms of some associative/commutative operations. How would this compare/contrast with the characterization of interaction via homological algebra using exactness? 
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	





	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Category of Functors}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0001} \tbf{Vertical Composition:} \\
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories, $F, G, H:\MC \rightarrow \MD$ functors and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, $\be : G \Rightarrow H$ natural transformations. We define the \textbf{vertical composition of $\be$ with $\al$}, denoted $\be \circ \al: F \Rightarrow H$, by 
		$$(\be \circ \al)_{A} = \be_A \circ \al_A$$ 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0002}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories, $F, G, H:\MC \rightarrow \MD$ functors and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, $\be : G \Rightarrow H$ natural transformations. Then $ \be \circ \al: F \Rightarrow H$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Since $\al_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$ and $\be_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(G(A), H(A))$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				(\be \circ \al)_A 
				& = \be_A \circ \al_A \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), H(A))
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Since $\al:F \Rightarrow G$ and $\be: G \Rightarrow H$, $G(f) \circ \al_A = \al_B \circ F(f)$ and $H(f) \circ \be_A = \be_B \circ G(f)$. Therefore 
			\begin{align*}
				H(f) \circ (\be \circ \al)_A
				& = H(f) \circ (\be_A \circ \al_A) \\
				& = (H(f) \circ \be_A) \circ \al_A \\
				& = (\be_B \circ G(f)) \circ \al_A \\
				& = \be_B \circ (G(f)\circ \al_A) \\
				& = \be_B \circ (\al_B \circ F(f)) \\
				& = (\be_B \circ \al_B) \circ F(f) \\
				& = (\be \circ \al)_B \circ F(f)
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		So $\be \circ \al: F \Rightarrow H$ is a natural transformation. 
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0003}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories, $F, G, H, K:\MC \rightarrow \MD$ functors and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, $\be : G \Rightarrow H$ and $\gam: H \Rightarrow K$ natural transformations. Then $$(\gam \circ \be) \circ \al = \gam \circ (\be \circ \al)$$
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. By definition,  
		\begin{align*}
			[(\gam \circ \be) \circ \al]_{A} 
			& = (\gam \circ \be)_A \circ \al_{A} \\
			& = (\gam_A \circ \be_A) \circ \al_A \\
			& = \gam_A \circ (\be_A \circ \al_A) \\
			& = \gam_A \circ (\be \circ \al)_A \\
			& = [\gam \circ (\be \circ \al)]_A \\
		\end{align*}
		Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, 
		$$(\gam \circ \be) \circ \al = \gam \circ (\be \circ \al)$$
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0004}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories and $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. We define the \textbf{identity natural transformation from $F$ to $F$}, denoted $\id_F: F \Rightarrow F$, by 
		$$(\id_F)_A = \id_{F(A)}^{\MD}$$
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0005}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories and $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. Then $\id_F: F \Rightarrow F$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				(\id_F)_A 
				& = \id_{F(A)}^{\MD} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), F(A))
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				F(f) \circ_{\MD} (\id_F)_A
				& = F(f) \circ_{\MD} \id_{F(A)}^{\MD} \\
				& = F(f) \\
				& = \id_{F(B)}^{\MD} \circ_{\MD} F(f) \\
				& = (\id_F)_{B} \circ_{\MD} F(f),
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(A)  \arrow[r, "(\id_F)_A"]  \arrow[d, "F(f)"']  & F(A)   \arrow[d, "F(f)"]\\
				F(B) \arrow[r, "(\id_F)_B"] &  F(B). \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0006}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories, $F,G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $\al : F \Rightarrow G$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\id_{G} \circ \al = \al$
			\item $\al \circ \id_F = \al$
		\end{enumerate} 
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				(\id_{G} \circ \al)_{A}
				& = (\id_G)_A \circ \al_A \\
				& = \id_{G(A)} \circ \al_A \\
				& = \al_A 
			\end{align*}
			Since $A \in \Obj(C)$ is arbitrary, $\id_{G} \circ \al = \al$
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				(\al \circ \id_F)_{A}
				& = \al_A \circ (\id_F)_A \\
				& = \al_A \circ \id_{F(A)} \\
				& = \al_A 
			\end{align*}
			Since $A \in \Obj(C)$ is arbitrary, $\al \circ \id_F = \al$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0007}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories, $F,G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$. If $\MC$ is small, then $\al$ is a set.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Then $\Obj(\MC)$ is a set. Since $\al: \Obj(\MC) \rightarrow \Hom_{\MD}$, \rax{11001.1} implies that $\al(\Obj(\MC))$ is a set. Then $ \Obj(\MC) \times \al(\Obj(\MC))$ is a set. Therefore $\MP(\Obj(\MC) \times \al(\Obj(\MC)))$ is a set. Since $\al \subset \Obj(\MC) \times \al(\Obj(\MC))$, we have that $\al \in \MP(\Obj(\MC) \times \al(\Obj(\MC)))$ which implies that $\al$ is a set. 
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0008}
			Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories and $F,G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. If $\MC$ is small, then there exists a class $A$ such that for each class $\al$, $\al \in A$ iff $\al: F \Rightarrow G$. 
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Define $\phi$ by 
		$$\phi(\al): \al: F \Rightarrow G$$
		\rax{11002} implies that there exists a class $A$ such that for each set $\al$, $\al \in A$ iff $\phi(\al)$. 
		Let $\al$ be a class. Suppose that $\al \in A$. By \rd{11001}, $\al$ is a set. Since $\al$ is a set and $\al \in A$, we have that $\phi(\al)$. Hence $\al:F \Rightarrow G$. \\
		Conversely, suppose that $\al: F \Rightarrow G$.  Since $\MC$ is small, \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0007} implies that $\al$ is a set. Since $\phi(\al)$, we have that $\al \in A$. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0009}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. We define the \textbf{functor category from $\MC$ to $\MD$}, denoted $\MD^{\MC}$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\MD^{\MC}) = \{F: F: \MC \rightarrow \MD\}$
			\item For $F, G \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$, $\Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F, G) = \{\al: \al: F \Rightarrow G \}$
			\item For $F, G, H \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F, G)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(G, H)$, 
			$\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al = \be \circ \al $
		\end{itemize} 
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0010}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Then $\MD^{\MC}$ is a category.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0002} implies that composition is well-defined. \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0003} implies that composition is associative. \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0005} and \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0006} imply the existence of identities.  
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0011}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ and $\MD$ are small. Then $\MD^{\MC}$ is small.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		We have that 
		\begin{align*}
			\text{$\MC$ and $\MD$ are small}
			& \iff \Obj(\MC), \Obj(\MD), \Hom_{\MC}, \Hom_{\MD} \in \Obj(\bSet) \\
			& \iff \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)}, \Hom_{\MD}^{\Hom_{\MC}} \in \Obj(\bSet) \\
			& \iff \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)} \times \Hom_{\MD}^{\Hom_{\MC}} \in \Obj(\bSet).
		\end{align*}
		Since $\MD^{\MC} \subset \Obj(\MD)^{\Obj(\MC)} \times \Hom_{\MD}^{\Hom_{\MC}}$ and $\MC$, $\MD$ are small, we have that $\MD^{\MC} \in \Obj(\bSet)$. Thus $\MD^{\MC}$ is small.
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Diagonal Functor}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0001}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories, $X, Y \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, Y)$. We define the \textbf{constant natural transformation on $\MC$ at $f$}, denoted $\del^{\MC}_f: \Del^{\MC}_X \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_Y$, by
		$$(\del^{\MC}_f)_A = f$$
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0002}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories, $X, Y \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, Y)$. Then $\del^{\MC}_f: \Del^{\MC}_X \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_Y $ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof} \
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item By definition, for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ $(\del^{\MC}_f)_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(\Del^{\MC}_X(A), \Del^{\MC}_Y(A))$.
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\Del^{\MC}_Y(g) \circ (\del^{\MC}_f)_A 
				& = \id_Y \circ f \\
				& = f \\
				& = f \circ \id_X \\
				& = (\del^{\MC}_f)_B \circ \Del^{\MC}_X(g)  
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				\Del^{\MC}_X(A)  \arrow[r, "(\del^{\MC}_f)_A"]  \arrow[d, "\Del^{\MC}_X(g)"']  & \Del^{\MC}_Y(A)   \arrow[d, "\Del^{\MC}_Y(g)"]\\
				\Del^{\MC}_X(B) \arrow[r, "(\del^{\MC}_f)_B"] &  \Del^{\MC}_Y(B) \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			=
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				X  \arrow[r, "f"]  \arrow[d, "\id_X"']  & Y   \arrow[d, "\id_Y"]\\
				X \arrow[r, "f"] &  Y \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
		\end{enumerate}
		So $\del^{\MC}_f: \Del^{\MC}_X \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_Y$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{proof}
	 
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0003}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be categories, $X, Y, Z \in \Obj(\MD)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X,Y)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MD}(Y,Z)$. Then $\del^{\MC}_{g \circ f} = \del^{\MC}_g \circ \del^{\MC}_f$.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{align*}
			(\del^{\MC}_{g \circ f})_A
			& = g \circ f \\
			& = (\del^{\MC}_g)_A \circ (\del^{\MC}_f)_A \\
			& = (\del^{\MC}_g \circ \del^{\MC}_f)_A
		\end{align*}
		Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, $\del^{\MC}_{g \circ f} = \del^{\MC}_g \circ \del^{\MC}_f$.
	\end{proof}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0004}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be categories and $X \in \Obj(\MD)$. Then $\del^{\MC}_{\id_X} = \id_{\Del^{\MC}_X}$.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}
		Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{align*}
			(\del^{\MC}_{\id_X})_A
			& = \id_X \\
			& = \id_{\Del^{\MC}_X(A)} \\
			& = (\id_{\Del^{\MC}_X})_A 
		\end{align*}
		Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, $\del^{\MC}_{\id_X} = \id_{\Del^{\MC}_X}$
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0005}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. We define the \textbf{$\MC$-ary diagonal functor} on $\MD$, denoted by $\Del^{\MC}: \MD \rightarrow \MD^{\MC}$, by
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Del^{\MC}(X) = \Del^{\MC}_X$
			\item $\Del^{\MC}(f) = \del^{\MC}_f$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0006}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Then $\Del^{\MC}: \MD \rightarrow \MD^{\MC}$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}

	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0002} implies that for each $X, Y \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, Y)$, $\Del^{\MC}(f) \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}} (\Del^{\MC}(X), \Del^{\MC}(Y))$
			\item \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0003} implies that for each $X, Y, Z \in \Obj(\MD)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, Y)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MD}(Y, Z)$, $\Del^{\MC}(g \circ f) = \Del^{\MC}(g) \circ \Del^{\MC}(f)$
			\item \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:diag_funct:0004} implies that for each $X \in \Obj(\MD)$, $\Del^{\MC}(\id_X) = \id_{\Del^{\MC}(X)}$
		\end{enumerate}
		 So $\Del^{\MC} : \MD \rightarrow \MD^{\MC}$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Isomorphisms}
	
	\subsection{Introduction}
	
	\begin{defn} 
		Let $\MC$ be a category.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, A)$. Then $f$ is said to be an \textbf{endomorphism},
				\item We define $\End_{\MC}(A) \defeq \Hom_{\MC}(A, A)$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item We define $\End_{\MC} \defeq \bigcup\limits_{A \in \Obj(\MC)} \End_{\MC}(A)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$.
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then $f$ is said to be an \textbf{isomorphism} if there exists $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$ such that $g \circ f = \id_A$ and $f \circ g = \id_B$.
				\item We define $\Iso_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B): \text{$f$ is an isomorphism}\}$
			\end{itemize}
			\item We define $\Iso_{\MC} \defeq \bigcup\limits_{(A,B) \in \Obj(\MC)^2} \Iso_{\MC}(A,B)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, A)$. Then $f$ is said to be an \textbf{automorphism},
				\item We define $\Aut_{\MC}(A) \defeq \Iso_{\MC}(A, A)$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item We define $\Aut_{\MC} \defeq \bigcup\limits_{A \in \Obj(\MC)} \Aut_{\MC}(A)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15003} \textbf{Uniqueness of Inverses:} \\
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$. Then there exists a unique $g \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, A)$ such that $g \circ f = \id_A$ and $f \circ g = \id_B$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{Existence:} \\
			By definition, since $f$ is an isomorphism, there exists $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$ such that $g \circ f = \id_{A}$ and $f \circ g = \id_B$. By definition, $g \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, A)$.
			\item \tbf{Uniqueness: } \\
			Let $g' \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, A)$. Suppose that $g' \circ f = \id_A$, $f \circ g' = \id_B$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				g'
				& = g' \circ \id_{B} \\
				& = g' \circ (f \circ g) \\
				& = (g' \circ f) \circ  g \\
				& = \id_A \circ g \\
				& = g
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15003.1}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$. Suppose that $f$ is an isomorphism. We define the \textbf{inverse of $f$}, denoted $f^{-1} \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, A)$, to be the unique $g \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, A)$ such that $g \circ f = \id_A$ and $f \circ g = \id_B$.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15004}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then $\id_A \in \Aut_{\MC}(A)$ and $(\id_A)^{-1} = \id_A$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Since $\id_A \circ \id_A = \id_A$, we have that $\id_A \in \Aut_{\MC}(A)$ and $(\id_A)^{-1} = \id_A$. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15005}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then for each $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$, $(f^{-1})^{-1} = f$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$. By definition, $f \circ f^{-1} = \id_{B}$ and $f^{-1} \circ f = \id_A$. Hence $(f^{-1})^{-1} = f$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15006}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A,B,C \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then for each $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, C)$, $g \circ f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, C)$ and $(g \circ f)^{-1} = f^{-1} \circ g^{-1}$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, C)$. Then 
		\begin{align*}
			(f^{-1} \circ g^{-1}) \circ (g \circ f) 
			& = ((f^{-1} \circ g^{-1}) \circ g) \circ f \\
			& = (f^{-1} \circ (g^{-1} \circ g)) \circ f \\
			& = (f^{-1} \circ \id_B) \circ f \\
			& = f^{-1} \circ f \\
			& = \id_{A}
		\end{align*}
		and 
		\begin{align*}
			(g \circ f) \circ (f^{-1} \circ g^{-1}) 
			& = ((g \circ f) \circ f^{-1}) \circ g^{-1} \\
			& = (g \circ (f \circ f^{-1})) \circ g^{-1} \\
			& = (g \circ \id_{B}) \circ g^{-1} \\
			& = g \circ  g^{-1} \\
			& = \id_{C}.
		\end{align*}
		Hence $g \circ f \in  \Iso_{\MC}(A, C)$ and $(g \circ f)^{-1} = f^{-1} \circ g^{-1}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15007}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then $A$ is said to be \textbf{isomorphic} to $B$ if $\Iso_{\MC}(A, B) \neq \varnothing$.
			\item We define the \tbf{isomorphism class relation on $\Obj(\MC)$}, denoted ${\cong_{\MC}} \in \MR(A, B)$, by $A \cong_{\MC} B$ iff $A$ is isomorphic to $B$. 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we may write $\cong$ in place of $\cong_{\MC}$.
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15008}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then ${\cong} \in \Equi(\Obj(C))$ \tcr{does $\MC$ neet to be small or just locally small?}.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof} \
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \textbf{reflexivity: } \\
			Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. \rex{15004} implies that $\id_A \in \Aut(A)$. Thus $A \cong A$. Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $A \cong A$ and thus $\cong$ is reflexive. 
			\item \textbf{symmetry: } \\
			Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$. Suppose that $A \cong B$. Then there exists $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A,B)$. \rex{15005} implies that $f^{-1} \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, A)$. Hence $B \cong A$.  Since $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ with $A \cong B$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $A \cong B$ implies that $B \cong A$ and thus $\cong$ is reflexive. 
			\item \textbf{transitivity: }
			Let $A, B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$. Suppose that $A \cong B$ and $B \cong C$. Then there exist $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Iso_{\MC}(B, C)$. \rex{15006} implies that $g \circ f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, C)$. Thus $A \cong C$. Since $A, B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$ with $A \cong B$ and $B \cong C$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A, B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $A \cong B$ and $B \cong C$ implies that $A \cong C$ and thus $\cong$ is transitive. 
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus ${\cong} \in \Equi(\Obj(C))$.
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Isomorphisms between Categories}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \MD)$. Write $F = (F_0, F_1)$. Then $F \in \Iso_{\Cat}$ iff $F_0, F_1 \in \Iso_{\bSet}$
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $(\implies)$: \\
			Suppose that $F \in \Iso_{\Cat}$. Then there exists $G \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MD, \MC)$ such that $G \circ_{\Cat} F = \id_{\MC}$ and $F \circ_{\Cat} G = \id_{\MD}$. Write $G = (G_0, G_1)$. By \rd{def:basics:functors:small_cat:0001}, we have that $G_0 \circ_{\bSet} F_0 = \id_{\Obj(\MC)}^{\bSet}$, $F_0 \circ_{\bSet} G_0 = \id_{\Obj(\MD)}^{\bSet}$, $G_1 \circ_{\bSet} F_1 = \id_{\Hom_{\MC}}^{\bSet}$ and $F_1 \circ_{\bSet} G_1 = \id_{\Hom_{\MD}}^{\bSet}$. Hence $F_0, G_0 \in \Iso_{\bSet}$.  
			\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
			Suppose that $F_0, F_1 \in \Iso_{\bSet}$. Define $G_0 \defeq F_0^{-1}$ and  $G_1 \defeq F_1^{-1}$.
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item Let $A', B' \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MD}(A', B')$. Define $f \in \Hom_{\MC}$ and $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ by $f \defeq G_1(f')$, $A \defeq \dom(f)$ and $B \defeq \cod(f)$. Since $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \MD)$, we have that 
				\begin{align*}
					f'
					& = F_1(f) \\
					& \in \Hom_{\MD}(F_0(A), F_0(B)).
				\end{align*}   
				Since $f' \in \Hom_{\MD}(A', B')$, we have that 
				\begin{align*}
					A'
					& = \dom(f') \\
					& = F_0(A).
				\end{align*}
				Similarly, $B' = F_0(B)$. Hence $G_0(A') = A$, $G_0(B') = B$ and 
				\begin{align*}
					G_1(f')
					& = G_1(F_1(f)) \\
					& = f \\
					& \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B) \\
					& =  \Hom_{\MC}(A, B) \\
					& = \Hom_{\MC}(G_0(A'), G_0(B')).
				\end{align*}
				\item Let $A',B', C' \in \Obj(\MD)$, $f' \in \Hom_{\MD}(A', B')$ and $g' \in \Hom_{\MD}(B', C')$. Define $f,g \in \Hom_{\MC}$ by $f \defeq G_1(f')$ and $g \defeq G_1(g')$. Then $F_1(f) = f'$ and $F_1(g) = g'$. Since $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \MD)$, we have that
				\begin{align*}
					G_1(g' \circ_{\MD} f')
					& = G_1(F_1(g) \circ_{\MD} F_1(f)) \\
					& = G_1(F_1( g \circ_{\MC} f)) \\
					& = g \circ_{\MC} f \\
					& = G_1(g') \circ_{\MC} G_1(f').
				\end{align*}
				\item Let $A' \in \Obj(\MD)$. Define $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ by $A \defeq G_0(A')$. Then $F_0(A) = A'$ and since $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \MD)$, we have that
				\begin{align*}
					G_1(\id_{A'}^{\MD})
					& = G_1(\id_{F_0(A)}^{\MD}) \\
					& = G_1(F_1(\id_A^{\MC})) \\
					& = \id_A^{\MC} \\
					& = \id_{G_0(A')}^{\MC}. 
				\end{align*}
			\end{enumerate}
			Hence $G \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MD, \MC)$. By construction, $G \circ_{\Cat} F = \id_{\MC}$ and $F \circ_{\Cat} G = \id_{\MD}$. Thus $F \in \Iso_{\Cat}$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Natural Isomorphisms}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15011.1}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories, $F,G : \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$. Then $\al$ is said to be a \textbf{natural isomorphism} if for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\al_A \in \Iso_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$. 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15011.2}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories, $F,G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $\al : F \Rightarrow G$. Suppose that $\al$ is a natural isomorphism. We define $\al^{-1}: G \Rightarrow F$ by $(\al^{-1})_A = \al_A^{-1}$. 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15011.3}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories, $F,G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $\al : F \Rightarrow G$. Suppose that $\al$ is a natural isomorphism. Then $\al^{-1}: G \Rightarrow F$ is a natural transformation
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Since $\al_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				(\al^{-1})_A
				& = \al_A^{-1} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(G(A), F(A))
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Since $G(f) \circ \al_A = \al_B \circ F(f)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(A)  \arrow[r, "\al_A"]  \arrow[d, "F(f)"']  & G(A)   \arrow[d, "G(f)"]\\
				F(B) \arrow[r, "\al_B"] &  G(B) \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				F(f) \circ (\al^{-1})_A 
				& = F(f) \circ \al_A^{-1} \\
				& = \id_{F(B)} \circ (F(f) \circ \al_A^{-1}) \\
				& = (\al_B^{-1} \circ \al_B) \circ (F(f) \circ \al_A^{-1}) \\
				& = \al_B^{-1} \circ (\al_B \circ (F(f) \circ \al_A^{-1})) \\
				& = \al_B^{-1} \circ ((\al_B \circ F(f)) \circ \al_A^{-1}) \\
				& = \al_B^{-1} \circ ((G(f) \circ \al_A) \circ \al_A^{-1}) \\
				& = \al_B^{-1} \circ (G(f) \circ (\al_A \circ \al_A^{-1})) \\
				& = \al_B^{-1} \circ (G(f) \circ \id_{G(A)}) \\
				& = \al_B^{-1} \circ G(f) \\
				& = (\al^{-1})_B \circ G(f) 
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				G(A)  \arrow[r, "(\al^{-1})_A"]  \arrow[d, "G(f)"']  & F(A)   \arrow[d, "F(f)"]\\
				G(B) \arrow[r, "(\al^{-1})_B"] &  F(B) \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			So $\al^{-1}: G \Rightarrow F$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15011.4}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories, $F,G: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $\al : F \Rightarrow G$. Suppose that $\al$ is a natural isomorphism. Then $\al^{-1} \circ \al = \id_F$ and $\al \circ \al^{-1} = \id_G$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{align*}
			(\al^{-1} \circ \al )_A 
			& = (\al^{-1})_A \circ \al_A \\
			& = \al_A^{-1} \circ \al_A \\
			& = \id_{F(A)} \\
			& = (\id_F)_A
		\end{align*}
		and 
		\begin{align*}
			(\al \circ \al^{-1} )_A 
			& = \al_A \circ (\al^{-1})_A\\
			& = \al_A \circ \al_A^{-1}\\
			& = \id_{G(A)} \\
			& = (\id_G)_A
		\end{align*}
		Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, $\al^{-1} \circ \al = \id_F$ and $\al \circ \al^{-1} = \id_G$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15011.5}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Let $F,G \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F, G)$. Then $\al$ is a natural isomorphism iff $\al \in \Iso_{\MD^{\MC}}(F, G)$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $(\implies)$: \\
