			Suppose that $\al$ is a natural isomorphism. \rex{15011.4} implies that $\al \in \Iso_{\MD^{\MC}}(F, G)$. 
			\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
			Suppose that $\al \in \Iso_{\MD^{\MC}}(F, G)$. Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\al_A \circ (\al^{-1})_A
				& = (\al \circ \al^{-1})_A \\
				& = (\id_{G})_A \\
				& = \id_{G(A)} \\
			\end{align*}
			and similarly, $\al_A^{-1} \circ \al_A = \id_{F(A)}$. Thus $\al_A \in \Iso_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$. Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\al_A \in \Iso_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$. By definition, $\al$ is a natural isomorphism.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\chapter{Fundamental Structures}
	
	
	\section{Initial and Terminal Objects}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15012}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $0 \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $1 \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $0$ is said to be \textbf{$\MC$-initial} if for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(0, A)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(0, A) = \{f\}$. 
			\item $1$ is said to be \textbf{$\MC$-terminal} if for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, 1)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(A, 1) = \{f\}$. \tcr{redo, use duality}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we say ``initial" and ``terminal" in place of ``$\MC$-initial" and ``$\MC$-terminal". 
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15012.1}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $0 \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $1 \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $0$ is $\MC$-initial iff $0$ is $\op{\MC}$-terminal
			\item $1$ is $\MC$-terminal iff $1$ is $\op{\MC}$-initial
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(\implies)$: \\
				Suppose that $0$ is $\MC$-initial. Let $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$. Since $\Obj(\op{\MC}) = \Obj(\MC)$, we have that $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Since $0$ is $\MC$-initial, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(0,A)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(0,A) = \{f\}$. Then 
				\begin{align*}
					\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, 0) 
					& = \Hom_{\MC}(0, A) \\
					& = \{f\}.
				\end{align*}
				Since $A$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, 0)$ such that $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, 0) = \{f\}$. Thus $0$ is $\op{\MC}$-terminal.
				\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
				Suppose that $0$ is $\op{\MC}$-terminal. Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Since $\Obj(\MC) = \Obj(\op{\MC})$, we have that $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$. Since $0$ is $\op{\MC}$-terminal, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,0)$ such that $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(0,A) = \{f\}$. Then 
				\begin{align*}
					\Hom_{\MC}(0, A) 
					& = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, 0) 
					& = \{f\}.
				\end{align*}
				Since $A$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(0, A) $ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(0, A)  = \{f\}$. Thus $0$ is $\MC$-initial.
			\end{itemize}
			\item Set $\MD \defeq \op{\MC}$. \rex{12005.1} implies that $\op{\MD} = \MC$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				\text{$1$ is $\MC$-terminal}
				& \iff \text{$1$ is $\MC$-terminal} \\
				& \iff \text{$1$ is $\op{\MD}$-terminal} \\
				& \iff \text{$1$ is $\MD$-initial}, \quad \text{(by \tcr{(reference) prev part})} \\
				& \iff \text{$1$ is $\op{\MC}$-initial}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15013}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $0 \in \Obj(\MC)$. 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item If $0$ is initial, then $\Hom_{\MC}(0, 0) = \{\id_0\}$.
			\item If $1$ is terminal, then $\Hom_{\MC}(1, 1) = \{\id_1\}$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Suppose that $0$ is initial. Then there exists a $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(0,0)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(0, 0) = \{f\}$. Since $\id_1 \in \Hom_{\MC}(0,0)$, $f = \id_1$ and therefore $\Hom_{\MC}(0, 0) = \{\id_1\}$.
			\item \tcr{use duality}. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15014}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $0, 0', 1, 1' \in \Obj(\MC)$. 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item If $0$ and $0'$ are initial, then 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $0 \cong_{\MC} 0'$,
				\item $\Hom_{\MC}(0, 0') = \Iso_{\MC}(0,0')$.
			\end{enumerate}
			\item If $1$ and $1'$ are terminal, then 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $1 \cong_{\MC} 1'$,
				\item $\Hom_{\MC}(1, 1') = \Iso_{\MC}(1,1')$.
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Suppose that $0$ and $0'$ are initial. 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item By definition, there exist $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(0, 0')$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MC}(0', 0)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(0, 0') = \{f\}$ and $\Hom_{\MC}(0', 0) = \{f'\}$, i.e. we have the following commutative diagram:
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					\arrow[loop left, "f' \circ f"] 0 \arrow[r, bend right= 60, "f", swap] & 0' \arrow[l, bend left=-60, "f'", swap] \arrow[loop right, "f \circ f'"] \\
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				\rex{15013} implies that $f' \circ f = \id_{0}$ and $f \circ f' = \id_{0'}$. Hence $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(0,0')$. Since $\Iso_{\MC}(0,0') \neq \varnothing$, we have that $0 \cong_{\MC} 0'$.
				\item Since
				\begin{align*}
					\Iso_{\MC}(0,0')
					& \subset \Hom_{\MC}(0, 0') \\
					& = \{f\} \\
					& \subset \Iso_{\MC}(0,0'),
				\end{align*}
				we have that $\Hom_{\MC}(0, 0') = \Iso_{\MC}(0,0')$.
			\end{enumerate}
			\item \tcr{use duality}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15015}
		Let $X, Y \in \Obj(\bSet)$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $X$ is initial iff $X = \varnothing$.
			\item $Y$ is terminal iff $Y \cong_{\bSet} \{\varnothing\}$. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(\implies)$: \\
				Suppose that $X$ is initial. Since $\Hom_{\bSet}(X, \{0,1\}) \cong_{\bSet} \MP(X)$, we have that  
				\begin{align*}
					\# \Hom_{\bSet}(X, \{0,1\}) = 1
					& \iff \# \MP(X) = 1 \\
					& \iff \MP(X) = \{\varnothing\} \\
					& \iff X = \varnothing.
				\end{align*}
				Since $X$ is initial, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(X, \{0,1\})$ such that $\Hom_{\bSet}(X, \{0,1\}) = \{f\}$. Thus $X = \varnothing$. 
				\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
				Suppose that $X = \varnothing$. Let $A \in \Obj(\bSet)$. 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item We note that for each $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}$,
					\begin{align*}
						f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(X, A) 
						& \iff f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\varnothing, A) \\
						& \implies f \subset \varnothing \times A \\
						& = \iff f \subset \varnothing \\
						& \iff f = \varnothing.
					\end{align*}
					Thus for each $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(X, A)$, $f \in \{\varnothing\}$. Hence $\Hom_{\bSet}(X, A) \subset \{\varnothing\}$. 
					\item Since  
					\begin{align*}
						\varnothing 
						& \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\varnothing, A) \\
						& = \Hom_{\bSet}(X, A),
					\end{align*}
					we have that $\{\varnothing\} \subset \Hom_{\bSet}(X, A)$.
				\end{itemize} 
				Thus $\Hom_{\bSet}(X, A) = \{\varnothing\}$. Therefore $X$ is initial.
			\end{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(\implies)$: \\
				Suppose that $Y$ is terminal. Since $\# \Hom_{\bSet}(\{\varnothing\}, Y) = \# Y$, we have that 
				\begin{align*}
					\# \Hom_{\bSet}(\{\varnothing\}, Y) = 1
					& \iff \# Y = 1 \\
					& \iff Y \cong_{\bSet} \{\varnothing\}.
				\end{align*}
				Since $Y$ is terminal, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\{\varnothing\}, Y)$ such that $\Hom_{\bSet}(\{\varnothing\}, Y) = \{f\}$. Thus $Y \cong_{\bSet} \{\varnothing\}$.
				\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
				Suppose that $Y \cong_{\bSet} \{\varnothing\}$. Then there exists $y \in Y$ such that $Y = \{y\}$. Let $A \in \Obj(\bSet)$. Define $f_0 \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y)$ by $f_0(a) \defeq y$. Let $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y)$. Let $a \in A$. Since 
				\begin{align*}
					f(a) 
					& \in Y \\
					& = \{y\}, 
				\end{align*}
				we have that $f(a) = y$. Since $a \in A$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $a \in A$, 
				\begin{align*}
					f(a) 
					& = y \\
					& = f_0(a). 
				\end{align*}
				Thus $f = f_0$. Since $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y)$, $f = f_0$. Hence $\Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y) = \{f_0\}$. Since $A \in \Obj(\bSet)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\bSet)$, there exists $f_0 \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y)$ such that $\Hom_{\bSet}(A, Y) = \{f_0\}$. Thus $Y$ is terminal. 
			\end{itemize}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15015.1}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Suppose that $\MC$ is locally small. Let $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $X$ is $\MC$-initial iff for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$ is $\bSet$-terminal.
			\item $X$ is $\MC$-terminal iff for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(A, X)$ is $\bSet$-terminal.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item We have that
			\begin{align*}
				\text{$X$ is $\MC$-initial}
				& \iff \text{for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\# \Hom_{\MC}(X, A) = 1$} \\
				& \iff \text{for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\# \Hom_{\MC}(X, A) \cong_{\bSet} \{\varnothing\}$} \\
				& \iff \text{for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\# \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$ is $\bSet$-terminal}, \quad \text{(by \rex{15015})}.
			\end{align*}
			\item We have that
			\begin{align*}
				\text{$X$ is $\MC$-terminal}
				& \iff \text{$X$ is $\op{\MC}$-initial}, \quad \text{(by \rex{15012.1})} \\
				& \iff \text{for each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, A)$ is $\bSet$-terminal}, \quad \text{(by \tcr{ref prev part})} \\
				& \iff  \text{for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(A, X)$ is $\bSet$-terminal}
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15016}
		We have that 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\0$ is $\Cat$-initial.
			\item $\1$ is $\Cat$-terminal. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $\MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. It is clear that $\Hom_{\Cat}(\0, \MC) = \{E_\MC\}$. Hence $\0$ is $\Cat$-initial. \tcr{Fill out like below ex}
			\item Let $\MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Let $F:\MC \rightarrow \1$. Since $\Obj(\1) = \{*\}$ and $\Hom_{\1}(*, *) = \{\id_*^{\1}\}$, we have for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$, $F(A) = *$ and $F(f) = \id_*^{\1}$. Thus $F = \Del^{\MC}_*$. Since $F:\MC \rightarrow \1$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $F:\MC \rightarrow \1$, $F = \Del^{\MC}_*$. Thus $\Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \1) = \{ \Del^{\MC}_* \}$. Since $\MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $\Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \1) = \{ \Del^{\MC}_* \}$. Hence $\1$ is $\Cat$-terminal.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15017}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories and $0,1 \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. Suppose that $0$ is $\MD$-initial and $1$ is $\MD$-terminal. Then for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, there exists $f_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(0, F(A))$ and $g_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), 1)$ such that $\Hom_{\MD}(0, F(A)) = \{f_A\}$ and $\Hom_{\MD}(F(A), 1) = \{g_A\}$. We define the 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \textbf{initial natural transformation induced by $0$ from $\Del^{\MC}_0$ to $F$}, denoted $\eta^{(0,F)}: \Del^{\MC}_0 \Rightarrow F$, by 
			$\eta^{(0,F)}_A \defeq f_A$.
			\item \textbf{terminal natural transformation induced by $1$ from $F$ to $\Del^{\MC}_1$}, denoted $\phi^{(F,1)}: F \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_1$, by 
			$\phi^{(F,1)}_A \defeq g_A$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15018}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories and $0 \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$. Suppose that $0$ is $\MD$-initial and $1$ is $\MD$-terminal. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\eta^{(0,F)}: \Del^{\MC}_0 \Rightarrow F$ is a natural transformation.
			\item $\phi^{(F,1)}: F \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_1$ is a natural transformation.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof} \
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item By definition, for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\eta^{(0,F)}_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(\Del^{\MC}_0(A), F(A))$
				\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$. Since 
				\begin{align*}
					F(f) \circ \eta^{(0,F)}_A 
					& \in \Hom_{\MD}(0, F(B)) \\
					& = \{\eta^{(0,F)}_B\}
				\end{align*}
				we have that 
				\begin{align*}
					F(f) \circ \eta^{(0,F)}_A 
					& = \eta^{(0,F)}_B \\
					& = \eta^{(0,F)}_B \circ \id_0^{\MC} 
				\end{align*}
				i.e. the following diagram commutes:
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					\Del^{\MC}_0(A)  \arrow[r, "\eta^{(0,F)}_A"]  \arrow[d, "\Del^{\MC}_0(f)"']  & F(A)   \arrow[d, "F(f)"]\\
					\Del^{\MC}_0(B) \arrow[r, "\eta^{(0,F)}_B"'] &  F(B) \\
				\end{tikzcd}
				=
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					0  \arrow[r, "\eta^{(0,F)}_A"]  \arrow[d, "\id_0^{\MC}"']  & F(A)   \arrow[d, "F(f)"]\\
					0 \arrow[r, "\eta^{(0,F)}_B"'] &  F(B) 
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
			\end{enumerate}
			So $\eta^{(0,F)}: \Del^{\MC}_0 \Rightarrow F$ is a natural transformation.
			\item \tcr{FINISH!!!}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15020}
		Let $\MC$, $\MD$ be categories and $0,1 \in \Obj(\MD)$. Suppose that $\MC$ is small.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item If $0$ is $\MD$-initial, then $\Del^{\MC}_0$ is $\MD^{\MC}$-initial. 
			\item If $1$ is $\MD$-terminal, then $\Del^{\MC}_1$ is $\MD^{\MC}$-terminal. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Suppose that $0$ is $\MD$-initial. Let $F \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(\Del^{\MC}_0, F)$ and $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				\al_A 
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(\Del^{\MC}_0(A), F(A)) \\
				& =  \Hom_{\MD}(0, F(A)) \\
				& = \{\eta^{(0,F)}_A\}
			\end{align*}
			Hence $\al_A = \eta^{(0,F)}_A$. Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\al_A = \eta^{(0,F)}_A$. Thus $\al = \eta^{(0,F)}$. Since $\al \in  \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(\Del^{\MC}_0, F)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(\Del^{\MC}_0, F)$, $\al = \eta^{(0,F)}$. This $\Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(\Del^{\MC}_0, F) = \{\eta^{(0,F)}\}$. Therefore $\Del^{\MC}_0$ is $\MD^{\MC}$-initial.
			\item \tcr{use duality}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Products and Coproducts}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)}, $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$ and $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $(\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X, X_{\al})$. Then $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC$-product of $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}$} if for each $Y \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(p_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(Y, X_{\al})$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(Y, X)$ such that for each $\al \in A$, from $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi = p_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					Y   \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p_{\al}"]    &  \\
					X \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
					& X_{\al}   
				\end{tikzcd}
				\] 
				\item We define 
				$$\Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \defeq \bigg \{(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X, X_{\al}): \text{$(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ is a $\MC$-product of $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}$} \bigg \}.$$
			\end{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $(\iota_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, X)$. Then $(X, (\iota_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC$-coproduct of $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}$} if for each $Y \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(i_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A}\Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y)$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$ such that for each $\al \in A$, from $\phi \circ_{\MC} \iota_{\al} = i_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					& X_{\al} \arrow[dl, "\iota_{\al}"'] \arrow[ddl, "i_{\al}"] & \\
					X \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed] & \\
					Y 
				\end{tikzcd}
				\] 
				\item We define 
				$$\Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \defeq \bigg \{(X, (\iota_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, X): \text{$(X, (\iota_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ is a $\MC$-coproduct of $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}$} \bigg \}.$$
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)} and $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) = \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$.
			\item $\Coprod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) = \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. We note that $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, X)$. Let $Y \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(i_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y)$. 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item \tbf{Existence:} \\
					Then $Y \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $(i_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(Y, X_{\al})$. Since $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(Y,X)$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\op{\MC}} \phi = i_{\al}$. Then $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$ and for each $\al \in A$, $\phi \circ_{\MC} \pi_{\al} = i_{\al}$. 
					\item \tbf{Uniqueness:} \\
					Let $\phi' \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$. Suppose that for each $\al \in A$,  $\phi' \circ_{\MC} \pi_{\al} = i_{\al}$. Then $\phi' \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(Y, X)$ and for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\op{\MC}} \phi' = i_{\al}$. Uniqueness of $\phi$ implies that $\phi' = \phi$.
				\end{itemize}
				Since $Y \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(i_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $Y \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(i_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y)$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y)$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\phi \circ_{\MC} \pi_{\al} = i_{\al}$. Thus $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. Since $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. Hence $\Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \subset \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$.
				\item \tcr{Similar, fill out!!!}
			\end{itemize}
			Since $\Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \subset \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ and $\Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \subset \Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, we have that $\Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) = \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. 
			\item \tcr{The prev part (ref)} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\Coprod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})
				& = \Prod_{\op{(\op{\MC})}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \\
				& = \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A}).
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)} and $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $(X, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, $X \cong_{\MC} Y$. 
			\item for each $(X, (\iota^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\iota^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, $X \cong_{\MC} Y$. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $(X, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item By definition, there exists a unique $\phi_{Y,X} \in \Hom_{\MC}(Y,X)$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{Y,X} = \pi^Y_{\al}$. Similarly, there exists a unique $\phi_{X,Y} \in \Hom_{\MC}(X,Y)$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{X,Y} = \pi^X_{\al}$. 
					\begin{align*}
						\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{C} (\phi_{X, Y} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{Y,X})
						& = (\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{X, Y}) \circ_{\MC} \phi_{Y,X} \\
						& = \pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{Y,X} \\
						& = \pi^Y_{\al}.
					\end{align*}
					\item By definition, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(Y,Y)$ such that $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ \phi = \pi^Y_{\al}$.
					\item We note that $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ \id_Y^{\MC} = \pi^Y_{\al}$.
				\end{itemize}
				Thus the following diagrams commutes:				
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					Y   \arrow[d, "\phi_{X, Y} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{Y,X}"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "\pi_{\al}"]    &  \\
					Y \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
					& X_{\al}   
				\end{tikzcd}
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					Y   \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "\pi_{\al}"]    &  \\
					Y \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
					& X_{\al}   
				\end{tikzcd}
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					Y   \arrow[d, "\id_Y^{\MC}"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "\pi_{\al}"]    &  \\
					Y \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
					& X_{\al}   
				\end{tikzcd}
				\] 
				Uniqueness of $\phi$ then implies that
				\begin{align*}
					\phi_{X,Y} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{Y,X}
					& = \phi \\
					& = \id_Y^{\MC},
				\end{align*} 
				\item Similarly, $\phi_{Y,X} \circ_{\MC} \phi_{X,Y} = \id_X^{\MC}$. 
			\end{itemize}
			Hence $\phi_{Y,X} \in \Iso_{\MC}(Y,X)$ and $X \cong_{\MC} Y$. Since $(X, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $(X, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, $X \cong_{\MC} Y$.
			\item Let $(X, (\iota^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\iota^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. \tcr{The prev ex (ref)} implies that $(X, (\iota^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}), (Y, (\iota^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\op{\MC}}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. \tcr{The prev part (ref)} then implies that $X \cong_{\op{\MC}} Y$. \tcr{An exercise in isomorphism section (ref)} implies that $X \cong_{\MC} Y$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{note}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item If $(X, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, we may write $\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}$ in place of $X$.
				\item If $(X, (\iota_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, we may write $\coprod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}$ in place of $X$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item If $A = \{1,2\}$, we may write 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Prod_{\MC}(X_1, X_2)$ and $\Coprod_{\MC}(X_1, X_2)$ in place of $\Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ and $\Coprod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ respectively. 
				\item $X_1 \times X_2$ in place of $\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}$ and $X_1 \coprod X_2$ in place of $\coprod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}$
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)}, $X \in \Obj(\MC)$, $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al})$. If for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} f = \pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g$, then $f = g$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Suppose that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} f = \pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g$. Since $(\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g)_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X, X_{\al})$ and $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al})$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi = \pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
		\[
		\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
			X   \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g"]    &  \\
			\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
			& X_{\al}   
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
		Since for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} f = \pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g$ and $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g = \pi_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g$, uniqueness of $\phi$ implies that 
		\begin{align*}
			f
			& = \phi \\
			& = g.
		\end{align*}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)}, $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}, (Y_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $(f_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y_{\al})$, $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ and $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al}, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((Y_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. We define the \tbf{$\MC$-product of $(f_{\al})_{\al \in A}$}, denoted $\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al} \in \Hom_{\MC}(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al})$, to be the unique $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al})$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} f = f_{\al} \circ \pi^X_{\al}$, i.e the following diagram commutes:
		\[
		\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
			\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}   \arrow[d, "f"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \pi^X_{\al}"]    &  \\
			\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi^Y_{\al}"']                        & \\
			& Y_{\al}   
		\end{tikzcd}
		\] 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)}, $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}, (Y_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $(f_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y_{\al})$, $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ and $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al}, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((Y_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. Then $(\pi^X_{\al}, \pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}, f_{\al})$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		By construction, for each $\al \in A$, 
		\begin{align*}
			f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \pi^X_{\al}
			& = \pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al},
		\end{align*}
		i.e. the following diagram commutes:
		\[ 
		\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
			\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}  \arrow[r, "\pi^X_{\al}"]  \arrow[d, "\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}"']  & X_{\al}   \arrow[d, "f_{\al}"]\\
			\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al} \arrow[r, "\pi^Y_{\al}"'] &  Y_{\al}
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
		Thus $(\pi^X_{\al}, \pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}, f_{\al})$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\tcr{Next exercise shows that the product of morphisms is in fact a product object in the arrow category}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)}, $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A}, (Y_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $(f_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\MC}(X_{\al}, Y_{\al})$, $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}, (\pi^X_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((X_{\al})_{\al \in A})$ and $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al}, (\pi^Y_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\MC}((Y_{\al})_{\al \in A})$. Define $(\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in  \prod\limits_{\al \in A}\Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}, f_{\al})$ by $\pi_{\al} \defeq (\pi^X_{\al}, \pi^Y_{\al})$. Then  $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}, \pi_{\al}) \in \Prod_{\Arr(\MC)}((f_{\al})_{\al \in A})$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $g \in \Obj(\Arr(\MC))$ and $(p_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, f_{\al})$. Define $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ by $A \defeq \dom_{\MC}(g)$ and $B \defeq \cod_{\MC}(g)$. Write $p_{\al} = (p^A_{\al}, p^A_{\al})$. We note that 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item By definition, for each $\al \in A$, $f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} p^A_{\al} = p^B_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				A  \arrow[r, "p^A_{\al}"]  \arrow[d, "g"']  & X_{\al}   \arrow[d, "f_{\al}"]\\
				B \arrow[r, "p^B_{\al}"'] &  Y_{\al}
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item By construction, for each $\al \in A$, $f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \pi^X_{\al} = \pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}  \arrow[r, "\pi^X_{\al}"]  \arrow[d, "\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}"']  & X_{\al}   \arrow[d, "f_{\al}"]\\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al} \arrow[r, "\pi^Y_{\al}"'] &  Y_{\al}
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
		\end{itemize}
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{Existence:} \\
			By definition, there exists a unique $\phi_X \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al})$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_X = p^A_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				A   \arrow[d, "\phi_X"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p^A_{\al} "]    &  \\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi^X_{\al}"']                        & \\
				& X_{\al}   
			\end{tikzcd}
			Similiarly, there exists a unique $\phi_Y \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al})$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_Y = p^B_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				B   \arrow[d, "\phi_Y"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p^B_{\al} "]    &  \\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi^Y_{\al}"']                        & \\
				& Y_{\al}   
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Then for each $\al \in A$,
			\begin{align*}
				\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} (\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_X)
				& = (\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}) \circ_{\MC} \phi_X \\
				& = (f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \pi^X_{\al}) \circ_{\MC} \phi_X \\
				& = f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} (\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_X) \\
				& = f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} p^A_{\al} \\
				& = p^B_{\al} \circ_{\MC} g \\
				& = (\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_Y) \circ_{\MC} g \\
				& = \pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} (\phi_Y \circ_{\MC} g).
			\end{align*}
			\tcr{the prev ex (ref)} then implies that $\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_X = \phi_Y \circ_{\MC} g$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				A  \arrow[r, "\phi_X"]  \arrow[d, "g"']  & \prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al}   \arrow[d, "\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}"]\\
				B \arrow[r, "\phi_Y"'] &  \prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al}
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Thus $(\phi_X, \phi_Y) \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$. Define $\phi \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$ by $\phi \defeq (\phi_X, \phi_Y)$. Let $\al \in A$. Since 
			$\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_X = p^A_{\al}$ and $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_Y = p^B_{\al}$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				\pi_{\al} \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} \phi
				& = (\pi^X_{\al}, \pi^Y_{\al}) \circ_{\Arr(\MC)}  (\phi_X, \phi_Y) \\
				& = (\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_X, \pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi_Y) \\
				& = (p^A_{\al}, p^B_{\al}) \\
				& = p_{\al}.
			\end{align*}
			Since $\al \in A$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} \phi = p_{\al}$,
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				g   \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p_{\al} "]    &  \\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
				& f_{\al}
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item \tbf{Uniqueness:} \\
			Let $\phi' \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$. Write $\phi' = (\phi'_X, \phi'_Y)$. Suppose that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} \phi' = p_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				g   \arrow[d, "\phi'"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p_{\al} "]    &  \\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
				& f_{\al}
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Let $\al \in A$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				(\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi'_X,  \pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi'_Y) 
				& = (\pi^X_{\al}, \pi^Y_{\al}) \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} (\phi'_X, \phi'_Y) \\
				& = \pi_{\al} \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} \phi' \\
				& = p_{\al} \\
				& = (p^A_{\al}, p^B_{\al}). 
			\end{align*}
			Therefore $\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi'_X = p^A_{\al}$ and $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi'_Y = p^B_{\al}$. Since $\al \in A$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi^X_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi'_X = p^A_{\al}$ and $\pi^Y_{\al} \circ_{\MC} \phi'_Y = p^B_{\al}$, i.e. the following diagrams commute:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				A   \arrow[d, "\phi'_X"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p^A_{\al} "]    &  \\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} X_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi^X_{\al}"']                        & \\
				& X_{\al}   
			\end{tikzcd}
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				B   \arrow[d, "\phi'_Y"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p^B_{\al} "]    &  \\
				\prod\limits_{\al \in A} Y_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi^Y_{\al}"']                        & \\
				& Y_{\al}   
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Uniqueness of $\phi_X$ and $\phi_Y$ imply that $\phi'_X = \phi_X$ and $\phi'_Y = \phi_Y$. Thus 
			\begin{align*}
				\phi'
				& = (\phi'_X, \phi'_Y) \\
				& = (\phi_X, \phi_Y) \\
				& = \phi.
			\end{align*}
			Since $\phi' \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\phi' \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$, $\phi' = \phi$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Thus there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} \phi = p_{\al}$. Since $g \in \Obj(\Arr(\MC))$ and $(p_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, f_{\al})$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $g \in \Obj(\Arr(\MC))$ and $(p_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \prod\limits_{\al \in A} \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, f_{\al})$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\Arr(\MC)}(g, \prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al})$ such that for each $\al \in A$, $\pi_{\al} \circ_{\Arr(\MC)} \phi = p_{\al}$,
		i.e. the following diagram commutes:
		\[
		\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
			g   \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed]  \arrow[ddr, "p_{\al} "]    &  \\
			\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al} \arrow[dr, "\pi_{\al}"']                        & \\
			& f_{\al}
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
		Hence $(\prod\limits_{\al \in A} f_{\al}, (\pi_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \in \Prod_{\Arr(\MC)}((f_{\al})_{\al \in A})$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\MC$ is said to have all
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{products} if for each $A \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $\Prod_{\MC}((A_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \neq \varnothing$,
			\item \tbf{coproducts} if for each $A \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$, $\Prod_{\MC}((A_{\al})_{\al \in A}) \neq \varnothing$,
			\item \tbf{finite products} if for each $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Prod_{\MC}(A,B) \neq \varnothing$,
			\item \tbf{finite coproducts} if for each $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Coprod_{\MC}(A,B) \neq \varnothing$,
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Equalizers and Coequalizers}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$.
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, A)$. Then $(C, f)$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC$-equalizer of $g$ and $h$} if 
				\begin{enumerate}
					\item $g \circ_{\MC} f = h \circ_{\MC} f$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
					\[ 
					\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
						&                                   & B \\
						C \arrow[r, "f"]  & A \arrow[ur, "g"] \arrow[dr, "h"'] &   \\
						&                                   & B \\
					\end{tikzcd}
					\]
					\item for each $C' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MC}(C', A)$, if $g \circ_{\MC} f' = h \circ_{\MC} f'$, then there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(C', C)$ such that $f \circ_{\MC} \phi = f'$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
					\[ 
					\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
						C' \arrow[dr, "f'"] \arrow[dd, "\phi"', dashed]&     & B \\
						& A \arrow[ur, "g"] \arrow[dr, "h"'] &   \\
						C \arrow[ur, "f"'] &                                  & B \\
					\end{tikzcd}
					\]
				\end{enumerate} 
				\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$. Then $(C, f)$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC$-coequalizer} of $g$ and $h$ if 
				\begin{enumerate}
					\item $f \circ_{\MC} g = f \circ_{\MC} h$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
					\[ 
					\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
						A \arrow[dr, "g"]  &                   &  \\
						& B \arrow[r, "f"]  & C  \\
						A \arrow[ur, "h"']  &                   & \\
					\end{tikzcd}
					\]
					\item for each $C' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C')$, if $ f' \circ_{\MC} g = f' \circ_{\MC} h$, then there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, C')$ such that $\phi \circ_{\MC} f = f'$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
					\[ 
					\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
						A \arrow[dr, "g"]  &                   & C \arrow[dd, "\phi", dashed]\\
						& B \arrow[ur, "f"]  \arrow[dr, "f'"'] &   \\
						A \arrow[ur, "h"']  &                  & C' \\
					\end{tikzcd}
					\]
				\end{enumerate} 
			\end{itemize}
			\item We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Eqzr_{\MC}(g,h) \defeq \{(C, f) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$\cod_{\MC}(f) = A$ and $f$ is a $\MC$-equalizer of $g$ and $h$}\}$
				\item $\Coeqzr_{\MC}(g,h) \defeq \{(C, f) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$\dom_{\MC}(f) = B$ and $f$ is a $\MC$-coequalizer of $g$ and $h$}\}$
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}$. Then $(C, f)$ is said to be a
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\MC$-equalizer if there exist $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ such that $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, A)$ and $f$ is a $\MC$-equalizer of $g$ and $h$. 
				\item $\MC$-coequalizer if there exist $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ such that $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$ and $f$ is a $\MC$-coequalizer of $g$ and $h$. 
			\end{enumerate}
			\item We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Eqzr_{\MC} \defeq \{(C,f) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$(C,f)$ is a $\MC$-equalizer}\}$
				\item $\Coeqzr_{\MC} \defeq \{(C,f) \in \Obj(\MC) \times \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$(C,f)$ is a $\MC$-coequalizer}\}$
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$, 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(g, h) = \Coeqzr_{\MC}(g,h)$
				\item $\Coeqzr_{\op{\MC}}(g,h) = \Eqzr_{\MC}(g,h)$
			\end{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\Eqzr_{\op{\MC}} = \Coeqzr_{\MC}$
				\item $\Coeqzr_{\op{\MC}} = \Eqzr_{\MC}$
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item Let $(C,f) \in \Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g)$. By definition \tcr{(ref def)}, $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C, A)$ and
					\begin{itemize}
						\item $g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f = h \circ_{\op{\MC}} f$,
						\item for each $C' \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C', A)$, if $g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f' = h \circ_{\op{\MC}} f'$, then there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C', C)$ such that $f \circ_{\op{\MC}} \phi = f'$. 
					\end{itemize}
					We note that $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$.  
					\begin{enumerate}
						\item Thus
						\begin{align*}
							f \circ_{\MC} g 
							& = g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f \\
							& = h \circ_{\op{\MC}} f \\
							& = f \circ_{\MC} h.
						\end{align*}
						\item Let $C' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C')$. Suppose that $f' \circ_{\MC} g = f' \circ_{\MC} h$. Then $f' \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C', B)$ and  
						\begin{align*}
							g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f' 
							& = f' \circ_{\MC} g \\
							& = f' \circ_{\MC} h \\
							& = h \circ_{\op{\MC}} f'.
						\end{align*}
						Thus there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C', C)$ such that $f \circ_{\op{\MC}} \phi = f'$. Therefore there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, C')$ such that 
						\begin{align*}
							\phi \circ_{\MC} f 
							& = f \circ_{\op{\MC}} \phi \\
							& = f'.
						\end{align*}
						Since $C' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C')$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C')$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, C')$ such that $\phi \circ_{\MC} f = f'$.
					\end{enumerate}
					Thus $(C,f) \in \Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g)$. Since $(C,f) \in \Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $(C,f) \in \Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g)$, $(C,f) \in \Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g)$. Thus $\Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g) \subset \Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g)$.
					\item Similarly, $\Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g) \subset \Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g)$. \tcr{show details}
				\end{itemize}
				Since $\Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g) \subset \Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g)$ and $\Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g) \subset \Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g)$, we have that $\Eqzr_{\op{\MC}}(f,g) = \Coeqzr_{\MC}(f,g)$
				\item \tcr{Similar}
			\end{enumerate}
			\item \tcr{FINISH!!!}
		\end{enumerate}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}

	\newpage
	\section{Exponentials}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Suppose that $\MC$ has finite products. Let $B,C \in \Obj(\MC)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $D \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\eval: D \times B \rightarrow C$. Then $(D, \eval)$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC$-exponential object of $B$ and $C$} if for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A \times B, C)$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, D)$ such that $\eval \circ_{\MC} (\phi \times \id_B^{\MC}) = f$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					A \arrow[d, "\phi"', dashed] & A \times B  \arrow[d, "\phi \times \id_B^{\MC}"', dashed]  \arrow[dr, "f", dashed] &  \\
					D                           & D \times B  \arrow[r, "\eval"'] & C 
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				\item We define 
				$$\Exp_{\MC}(B, C) \defeq \bigg \{(D, \eval) \in \coprod\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC)}\Hom_{\MC}(D \times B, C): \text{$(D, \eval)$ is a $\MC$-exponential of $B$ and $C$} \bigg \}.$$
			\end{itemize}
			\item We define \tcr{define coexponential objects} \tbf{}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A$ a set \tcr{(class?)} and $(X_{\al})_{\al \in A} \in \Obj(\MC)^A$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\Exp_{\op{\MC}}(B, C) = \Coexp_{\MC}(B, C)$.
			\item $\Coexp_{\op{\MC}}(B, C) = \Exp_{\MC}(B, C)$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		
	\end{ex}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Monomorphisms and Epimorphisms}
	
	\subsection{Introduction}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{15009}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then $f$ is said to be 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item 
			a \textbf{monomorphism} if for each $C \in \Obj(C)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, A)$, $f \circ g = f \circ h$ implies that $g = h$, i.e. we have the following implication of commutative diagrams: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				C \arrow[dr, "g"]&                                   & \\
				& A \arrow[r, "f"] & B  \\
				C \arrow[ur, "h"']&                                   & \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\implies
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				C \arrow[bend right=60, swap]{r}{h} \arrow[bend right=-60]{r}{g} & A  \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item 
			an \textbf{epimorphism} if for each $C \in \Obj(C)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$, $g \circ f = h \circ f$ implies that $g = h$, i.e. we have the following implication of commutative diagrams: \\
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				&                                   & C \\
				A \arrow[r, "f"]  & B \arrow[ur, "g"] \arrow[dr, "h"'] &   \\
				&                                   & C \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\implies
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				B \arrow[bend right=60, swap]{r}{h} \arrow[bend right=-60]{r}{g} & C  \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
		\end{itemize}
		\tcr{make note about common short-hand using parallel arrows}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Mono_{\MC} \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}:\text{$f$ is a monomorphism}\}$
				\item $\Epi_{\MC} \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}:\text{$f$ is a epimorphism}\}$
			\end{itemize}
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Mono_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \Mono_{\MC} \cap \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$.
				\item $\Epi_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \Epi_{\MC} \cap \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$.
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$,
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$
				\item $\Epi_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \Mono_{\MC}(B,A)$
			\end{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\Mono_{\op{\MC}} = \Epi_{\MC}$
				\item $\Epi_{\op{\MC}} = \Mono_{\MC}$
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\tcr{FIX!!!}
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$.
				\begin{itemize}
					\item Let $m \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$. Then $m \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,A)$. Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, C)$. Suppose that $f \circ_{\MC} m = g \circ_{\MC} m$. Then $m \circ_{\op{\MC}} f = m \circ_{\op{\MC}} g$. Since $m \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}$, we have that $f = g$. Since $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, C)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, C)$, $f \circ_{\MC} m = g \circ_{\MC} m$ implies that $f = g$. Thus $m \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$. Since $m \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $m \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$, $m \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$. Hence $\Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \subset \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$. 
					\item Let $e \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$. Then $e \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$. Let $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C, A)$. Suppose that $e \circ_{\op{\MC}} f = e \circ_{\op{\MC}} g$. Then $f \circ_{\MC} e = g \circ_{\MC} e$. Since $e \in \Epi_{\MC}$, we have that $f = g$. Since $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C, A)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C, A)$, $e \circ_{\op{\MC}} f = e \circ_{\op{\MC}} g$ implies that $f = g$. Thus $e \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$. Since $e \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $e \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$, $e \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$. Hence $\Epi_{\MC}(B,A) \subset \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$. 
				\end{itemize}
				Since $\Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \subset \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$ and $\Epi_{\MC}(B,A) \subset \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$, we have that $\Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$. 
				\item 
			\end{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item 
				Since $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \Epi_{\MC}(B,A)$. Hence 
				\begin{align*}
					\Mono_{\op{\MC}}
					& = \bigcup\limits_{(A,B) \in \Obj(\op{\MC})^2} \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \\
					& = \bigcup\limits_{(A,B) \in \Obj(\MC)^2} \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \\
					& = \bigcup\limits_{(B,A) \in \Obj(\MC)^2} \Epi_{\MC}(B,A) \\
					& = \Epi_{\MC}.
				\end{align*}
				\item \tcr{The previous part (ref needed)} implies that 
				\begin{align*}
					\Mono_{\MC}
					& = \Mono_{\op{(\op{\MC})}} \\
					& = \Epi_{\op{\MC}}.
				\end{align*}
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A,B,C \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Mono_{\MC}(B,C)$, $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,C)$,
			\item for each $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,C)$, $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A,C)$. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,B)$, $g \in \Mono_{\MC}(B,C)$, $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$. We note that since 
			\begin{align*}
				(g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \al = (g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \be
				& \iff g \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} \al) = g \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} \be) \\
				& \implies f \circ_{\MC} \al = f \circ_{\MC} \be \quad \text{($g \in \Mono_{\MC}$)} \\
				& \implies \al = \be \quad \text{($f \in \Mono_{\MC}$)}.
			\end{align*} 
			Since $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$ with $(g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \al = (g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \be$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$, $(g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \al = (g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \be$ implies that $\al = \be$. Hence $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A, C)$. Since $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Mono_{\MC}(B,C)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,B)$, $g \in \Mono_{\MC}(B,C)$, $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,C)$.
			\item Let $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,C)$. \rex{} \tcr{(ref prev ex)} implies that $f \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(B,A)$ and $g \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(C,B)$, \tcr{(ref prev part)} then implies that
			\begin{align*}
				g \circ_{\MC} f 
				& = f \circ_{\op{\MC}} g \\
				& \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}} \\
				& = \Epi_{\MC}(A,C).
			\end{align*} 
			Since $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,C)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Epi_{\MC}(B,C)$, $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A,C)$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A,B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,C)$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $g \in \Mono_{\MC}$ implies that $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}$ iff $f \in \Mono_{\MC}$.
			\item $f \in \Epi_{\MC}$ implies that $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Epi_{\MC}$ iff $g \in \Epi_{\MC}$.
		\end{enumerate} 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Suppose that $g \in \Mono_{\MC}$. 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(\implies)$: \\
				Suppose that $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}$. Let $D \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \in \Hom_{\MC}(D, A)$. Suppose that $f \circ_{\MC} \al = f \circ_{\MC} \be$. Then 
				\begin{align*}
					(g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \al \\
					& = g \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} \al) \\
					& = g \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} \be) \\
					& = (g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} \be.
				\end{align*}
				Since $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}$, $\al = \be$. Since $D \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \in \Hom_{\MC}(D, A)$ with $f \circ_{\MC} \al = f \circ_{\MC} \be$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $D \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \in \Hom_{\MC}(D, A)$, $f \circ_{\MC} \al = f \circ_{\MC} \be$ implies that $\al = \be$. Thus $f \in \Mono_{\MC}$.
				\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
				Suppose that $f \in \Mono_{\MC}$. Since $g \in \Mono_{\MC}$, \rex{} \tcr{(ref prev ex)} implies that $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\MC}$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item Suppose that $f \in \Epi_{\MC}$. \rex{} \tcr{(ref prev ex abotu duality)} implies that $f \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Epi_{\MC}
				& \iff g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}} \quad \text{(\tcr{ref prev ex about duality})} \\
				& \iff f \circ_{\op{\MC}} g \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}} \\
				& \iff g \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}} \quad \text{(\tcr{ref prev part})} \\
				& \iff g \in \Epi_{\MC} \quad \text{(\tcr{ref prev ex about duality})}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15011}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then $\Iso_{\MC}(A, B) \subset \Mono_{\MC}(A, B) \cap \Epi_{\MC}(A, B)$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item (monomorphism): \\
			Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g, h \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, A)$. Suppose that $f \circ_{\MC} g = f \circ_{\MC} h$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				g 
				& = \id_A \circ_{\MC} g \\
				& = (f^{-1} \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} g \\
				& = f^{-1} \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} g) \\
				& = f^{-1} \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} h) \\
				& = (f^{-1} \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} h \\
				& = \id_A \circ_{\MC} h \\
				& = h
			\end{align*}
			Since $g, h \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, A)$ with $f \circ_{\MC} g = f \circ_{\MC} h$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $g, h \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, A)$, $f \circ_{\MC} g = f \circ_{\MC} h$ implies that $g = h$. Therefore $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A, B)$.
			\item  (epimorphism): \\
			Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g, h \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$. Suppose that $ g \circ_{\MC} f = h \circ_{\MC} f$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				g 
				& = g \circ_{\MC} \id_B \\
				& = g \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} f^{-1}) \\
				& = (g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} f^{-1} \\
				& = (h \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MC} f^{-1} \\
				& = h \circ_{\MC} (f \circ_{\MC} f^{-1}) \\
				& = h \circ_{\MC} \id_B \\
				& = h
			\end{align*}
			Since $g, h \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$ with $g \circ_{\MC} f = h \circ_{\MC} f$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $g, h \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$, $g \circ_{\MC} f = h \circ_{\MC} f$ implies that $g = h$. Therefore $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(A, B)$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Thus $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A, B) \cap \Epi_{\MC}(A, B)$. Since $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $f \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, B)$, $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A, B) \cap \Epi_{\MC}(A, B)$. Hence $\Iso_{\MC}(A, B) \subset \Mono_{\MC}(A, B) \cap \Epi_{\MC}(A, B)$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then $\id_X \in \Mono_{\MC} \cap \Epi_{\MC}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\tcr{ref prev ex in isomorphism section} implies that $\id_X \in \Aut_{\MC}(X)$. \tcr{ref prev ex} implies that $\id_X \in \Mono_{\MC} \cap \Epi_{\MC}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{15010}
		\tcr{mono/epi in $\bSet$}
		Let $A, B \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A,B)$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $f$ is a monomorphism iff $f$ is injective
			\item $f$ is an epimorphism iff $f$ is surjective 
		\end{enumerate} 
		\tbf{Hint: } consider $C \defeq \{0\}$ and $C \defeq \{0,1\}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(\implies)$: \\
				Suppose that $f$ is injective. Let $C \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\bSet}(C, A)$. Suppose that $f \circ_{\bSet} g = f \circ_{\bSet} h$. Let $x \in C$. Then $f(g(x)) = f(h(x))$. Injectivity of $f$ implies that $g(x) = h(x)$. Since $x \in C$ is arbitrary, $g = h$. Hence $f \in \Mono_{\bSet}$. \\
				\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
				Conversely, suppose that $f \in \Mono_{\bSet}$. Let $a, b \in A$. Suppose that $f(a) = f(b)$. Set $C = \{0\}$ and define $g,h: C \rightarrow A$ by $g(0) = a$ and $h(0) = b$. Then  
				\begin{align*}
					f \circ_{\bSet} g(0) 
					& = f(g(0)) \\
					& = f(a) \\
					& = f(b) \\
					& = f(h(0)) \\
					& = f \circ_{\bSet} h(0) 
				\end{align*}
				Therefore $f \circ_{\bSet} g = f \circ_{\bSet} h$. Since $f \in \Mono_{\bSet}$, we have that $g = h$. Hence 
				\begin{align*}
					a 
					& = g(0) \\
					& = h(0) \\
					& = b
				\end{align*}
				Since $a, b \in A$ with $f(a) = f(b)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $a, b \in A$, $f(a) = f(b)$ implies that $a = b$. Thus $f$ is injective.
			\end{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $(\implies)$: \\
				Suppose that $f$ is surjective. Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\bSet}(B, C)$. Suppose that $g \circ_{\bSet} f = h \circ_{\bSet} f$. Let $y \in B$. Surjective of $f$ implies that there exists $x \in A$ such that $y = f(x)$. 
				Then 
				\begin{align*}
					g(y)
					& = g(f(x)) \\
					& = g \circ_{\bSet} f (x) \\
					& = h \circ_{\bSet} f (x) \\
					& = h(f(x)) \\
					& = h(y) 
				\end{align*}
				Since $y \in B$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $y \in B$, $g(y) = h(y)$. Hence $g = h$. Since $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\bSet}(B, C)$ with $g \circ_{\bSet} f = h \circ_{\bSet} f$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\bSet}(B, C)$, $g \circ_{\bSet} f = h \circ_{\bSet} f$ implies that $g = h$. Hence $f$ is an epimorphism. \\
				\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
				Conversely, suppose that $f$ is an epimorphism. Define $C \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $g, h: B \rightarrow C$ by $C \defeq \{0,1\}$, $g \defeq \chi_{f(A)}$ and $h \defeq \chi_{B}$. Then $g \circ_{\bSet} f = h \circ_{\bSet} f$. Since $f \in \Epi_{\MC}$, $g = h$ and $f(A) = B$. Hence $f$ is surjective. 
			\end{itemize} 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Extremal Monomorphisms and Epimorphisms}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then $f$ is said to be an
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{extremal monomorphism} if 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $f \in \Mono_{\MC}$ 
				\item for each $C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $e \in \Epi_{\MC}(A, C)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, B)$, $f = g \circ_{\MC} e$ implies that $e \in \Iso_{\MC}(A, C)$. 
			\end{itemize}
			\item \tbf{extremal epimorphism} if 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $f \in \Epi_{\MC}$ 
				\item for each $C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, C)$ and $m \in \Mono_{\MC}(C, B)$, $f = m \circ_{\MC} g$ implies that $m \in \Iso_{\MC}(C, B)$. 
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\ExtMono_{\MC} \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$f$ is an extremal monomorphism}\}$,
				\item $\ExtEpi_{\MC} \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$f$ is an extremal epiorphism}\}$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\ExtMono_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \ExtMono_{\MC} \cap \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$,
				\item $\ExtEpi_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \ExtEpi_{\MC} \cap \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$.
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$,
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B,A)$
				\item $\ExtEpi_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \ExtMono_{\MC}(B,A)$
			\end{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}} = \ExtEpi_{\MC}$
				\item $\ExtEpi_{\op{\MC}} = \ExtMono_{\MC}$
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\tcr{FIX!!!}
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$. 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $f \in \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$. 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item Then $f \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$. \tcr{ref prev ex in section on monomorphisms} implies that $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(B, A)$. 
					\item Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,C)$ and $m \in \Mono_{\MC}(C,A)$. Suppose that $f = m \circ_{\MC} g$. Then $g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C,B)$, \tcr{a prev ex in section on monomorphs} implies that $m \in \Epi_{\op{\MC}}(A,C)$ and $f = g \circ_{\op{\MC}} m$. Since $f \in \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$, we have that $m \in \Iso_{\op{\MC}}(B, C)$. \rex{} \tcr{(make and ref prev ex that $\Iso_{\MC} = \Iso_{\op{\MC}}$)} implies that $m \in \Iso_{\MC}(C, B)$. Since $C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,C)$ and $m \in \Mono_{\MC}(C,A)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,C)$ and $m \in \Mono_{\MC}(C,A)$, $f = m \circ_{\MC} g$ implies that $m \in \Iso_{\MC}(C, A)$.
				\end{itemize}
				Thus $f \in \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$. Since $f \in \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $f \in \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$, $f \in \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$. Hence $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B) \subset \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$.
				\item Let $f \in \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$. 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item Then $f \in \Epi_{\MC}(B, A)$. \tcr{ref prev ex in section on monomorphisms} implies that $f \in \Mono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$.
					\item  Let $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $e \in \Epi_{\op{\MC}}(A,C)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C,B)$. Suppose that $f = g \circ_{\op{\MC}} e$. Then $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,C)$, \tcr{a prev ex in section on monomorphs} implies that $e \in \Mono_{\MC}(C, A)$ and $f = e \circ_{\MC} g$. Since $f \in \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$, we have that $e \in \Iso_{\MC}(C, A)$. \rex{} \tcr{(make and ref prev ex that $\Iso_{\MC} = \Iso_{\op{\MC}}$)} implies that $e \in \Iso_{\op{\MC}}(A, C)$. Since $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $e \in \Epi_{\op{\MC}}(A,C)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C,B)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $e \in \Epi_{\op{\MC}}(A,C)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(C,B)$, $f = g \circ_{\op{\MC}} e$ implies that $e \in \Iso_{\op{\MC}}(A, C)$.
				\end{itemize}
				Thus $f \in \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$. Since $f \in \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $f \in \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$, $f \in \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$. Hence $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B) \subset \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$.
			\end{itemize}
			Since $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B) \subset \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$ and $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B) \subset \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$, we have that $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B) = \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$. Since $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A, B) = \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B, A)$. Therefore 
			\begin{align*}
				\ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}
				& = \bigcup\limits_{(A,B) \in \Obj(\op{\MC})^2} \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \\
				& = \bigcup\limits_{(A,B) \in \Obj(\MC)^2} \ExtMono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \\
				& = \bigcup\limits_{(B,A) \in \Obj(\MC)^2} \ExtEpi_{\MC}(B,A) \\
				& = \ExtEpi_{\MC}.
			\end{align*}
			\item \tcr{The previous part (ref needed)} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\ExtMono_{\MC}
				& = \ExtMono_{\op{(\op{\MC})}} \\
				& = \ExtEpi_{\op{\MC}}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Regular Monomorphisms and Epimorphisms}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$.
		\tcr{Rewrite using notation $\Eqzr_{\MC}$}
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $M \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $m \in \Hom_{\MC}(M, A)$. If $(M, m)$ is an equalizer of $f$ and $g$, then $m \in \Mono_{\MC}(M, A)$. 
			\item Let $E \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $e \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, E)$. If $(E, e)$ is a coequalizer of $f$ and $g$, then $e \in \Epi_{\MC}(B, E)$. 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Suppose that $(M, m)$ is an equalizer of $f$ and $g$. Let $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al, \be \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, M)$. Suppose that $m \circ_{\MC} \al = m \circ_{\MC} \be$. Since $(M, m)$ is an equalizer of $f$ and $g$, we have that $f \circ_{\MC} m = g \circ_{\MC} m$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				&                                   & B \\
				M \arrow[r, "m"]  & A \arrow[ur, "f"] \arrow[dr, "g"'] &   \\
				&                                   & B \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Define $M' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $m' \in \Hom_{\MC}(M', A)$ by $M' \defeq C$ and $m' \defeq m \circ_{\MC} \al$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				f \circ_{\MC} m'
				& = f \circ_{\MC} (m \circ_{\MC} \al) \\
				& = (f \circ_{\MC} m) \circ_{\MC} \al \\
				& = (g \circ_{\MC} m) \circ_{\MC} \al \\
				& = g \circ_{\MC} (m \circ_{\MC} \al) \\
				& = g \circ_{\MC} m'.
			\end{align*}
			Since $(E,m)$ is an equalizer of $f$ and $g$, there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC}(E', E)$ such that $m \circ_{\MC} \phi = m'$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				E' \arrow[dr, "m'"] \arrow[dd, "\phi"', dashed]&     & B \\
				& A \arrow[ur, "f"] \arrow[dr, "g"'] &   \\
				E \arrow[ur, "m"'] &                                  & B \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Since $m \circ_{\MC} \al = m'$, uniqueness of $\phi$ implies that $\phi = \al$. Since 
			\begin{align*}
				m \circ_{\MC} \be 
				& = m \circ_{\MC} \al \\
				& = m',
			\end{align*}
			uniqueness of $\phi$ implies that $\phi = \be$. Hence $\al = \be$. Since $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al,\be \Hom_{\MC}(C,E)$ with $m \circ_{\MC} \al = m \circ_{\MC} \be$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\al, \be \in \Hom_{\MC}(C, E)$, $m \circ_{\MC} \al = m \circ_{\MC} \be$ implies that $\al = \be$, i.e. we have the following implication of commutative diagrams: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				C \arrow[dr, "\al"]&                                   & \\
				& E \arrow[r, "m"] & A  \\
				C \arrow[ur, "\be"']&                                   & \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\implies
			\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
				C \arrow[bend right=60, swap]{r}{\be} \arrow[bend right=-60]{r}{\al} & E  \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Thus $m \in \Mono_{\MC}(E, A)$.
			\item \tcr{FINISH!!!}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then $f$ is said to be a 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{regular monomorphism} if there exists $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,C)$ such that $(A,f) \in \Eqzr_{\MC}(g,h)$.
			\item \tbf{regular epimorphism} if there exists $C \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $g,h \in \Hom_{\MC}(C,A)$ such that $(B,f) \in \Coeqzr_{\MC}(g,h)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\RegMono_{\MC} \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$f$ is a regular monomorphism}\}$,
				\item $\RegEpi_{\MC} \defeq \{f \in \Hom_{\MC}: \text{$f$ is a regular epiorphism}\}$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\RegMono_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \RegMono_{\MC} \cap \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$,
				\item $\RegEpi_{\MC}(A,B) \defeq \RegEpi_{\MC} \cap \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$.
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$,
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\RegMono_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \RegEpi_{\MC}(B,A)$
				\item $\RegEpi_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) = \RegMono_{\MC}(B,A)$
			\end{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\RegMono_{\op{\MC}} = \RegEpi_{\MC}$
				\item $\RegEpi_{\op{\MC}} = \RegMono_{\MC}$
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then for each $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$,
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $\RegMono_{\MC}(A,B) \subset \ExtMono_{\MC}(A,B)$,
			\item $\RegEpi_{\MC}(A,B) \subset \ExtEpi_{\MC}(A,B)$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$. \tcr{FINISH!!!}
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\item 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $A,B \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A,B)$. Then $(\Eqzr(f,g), \iota_{\Eqzr(f,g)}) \in \Eqzr_{\bSet}(f,g)$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		Define $E \in \Obj(\bSet)$ by $E \defeq \Eqzr(f,g)$.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item By definition, $E = \{x \in A: f(x) = g(x)\}$. Therefore for each $x \in E$,
			\begin{align*}
				f \circ_{\bSet} \iota_E(x)
				& = f(\iota_E(x)) \\
				& = f(x) \\
				& = g(x) \\
				& = g(\iota_E(x)) \\
				& = g \circ_{\bSet} \iota_E (x).
			\end{align*}
			Thus $f \circ_{\bSet} \iota_E = g \circ_{\bSet} \iota_E$. 
			\item Let $E' \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $e' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E',A)$. Suppose that $f \circ_{\bSet} e' = g \circ_{\bSet} e'$. Let $x \in E'$. Define $a \in A$ by $a \defeq e'(x)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				f(a)
				& = f(e'(x)) \\
				& = f \circ_{\bSet} e'(x) \\
				& = f \circ_{\bSet} e'(x) \\
				& = g(e'(x)) \\
				& = g(a).
			\end{align*}
			Thus $a \in \Eqzr(f,g)$. Therefore
			\begin{align*}
				e'(x)
				& = a \\
				& \in \Eqzr(f,g) \\
				& = E.
			\end{align*}
			Since $x \in E'$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $x \in E'$, $e'(x) \in E$.
			Define $\phi \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E', E)$ by $\phi(x) \defeq e'(x)$. 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item For each $x \in E'$,
				\begin{align*}
					\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi(x) \\
					& = \iota_E(\phi(x)) \\
					& = \iota_E (e'(x)) \\
					& = e'(x).
				\end{align*}
				Thus $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi = e'$.
				\item Let $\phi' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E', E)$. Suppose that $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi' = e'$. Then for each $x \in E'$,
				\begin{align*}
					\phi'(x)
					& = \iota_E (\phi'(x)) \\
					& = \iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi'(x) \\
					& = e'(x) \\
					& = \iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi(x) \\
					& = \iota_E (\phi(x)) 
					& = \phi(x).
				\end{align*}
				Hence $\phi' = \phi$. Since $\phi' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E', E)$ with $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi' = e'$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\phi' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E', E)$, $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi' = e'$ implies that $\phi' = \phi$.
			\end{itemize} 
			Thus there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E', E)$ such that $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi = e'$. Since $E' \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $e' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E',A)$ with $f \circ_{\bSet} e' = g \circ_{\bSet} e'$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $E' \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $e' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E',A)$, $f \circ_{\bSet} e' = g \circ_{\bSet} e'$ implies that there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\bSet}(E', E)$ such that $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \phi = e'$. 
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $(E, \iota_E) \in \Eqzr_{\bSet}(f,g)$. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		We have that $\RegMono_{\bSet} = \Mono_{\bSet}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tcr{a prev ex} implies that $\RegMono_{\bSet} \subset \Mono_{\bSet}$.
			\item Let $m \in \Mono_{\bSet}$. Define $M, A \in \Obj(\bSet)$ by $M \defeq \dom_{\bSet}(m)$ and $A \defeq \cod_{\bSet}(m)$. \tcr{a prev ex} implies that $m$ is injective. Define $B \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $f,g \in \Hom_{\bSet}(A,B)$ by $B \defeq m(M) \cup \{0,1\}$ and
			\[
			f(x) \defeq 
			\begin{cases}
				x, & x \in m(M) \\
				0, & x \in m(M)^c,
			\end{cases}
			g(x) \defeq 
			\begin{cases}
				x, & x \in m(M) \\
				1, & x \in m(M)^c.
			\end{cases}
			\]
			Define $E \in \Obj(\bSet)$ by $E \defeq \Eqzr(f,g)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				E
				& = \Eqzr(f,g) \\
				& = \{x \in A: f(x) = g(x)\} \\
				& = m(M).
			\end{align*}
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item By construction, for each $x \in M$, 
				\begin{align*}
					f \circ_{\bSet} m(x)
					& = f(m(x)) \\
					& = g(m(x)) \quad \text{(since $m(x) \in E$)} \\
					& = g \circ_{\bSet} m(x).
				\end{align*}
				Thus $f \circ_{\bSet} m = g \circ_{\bSet} m$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					&                                   & B \\
					M \arrow[r, "m"]  & A \arrow[ur, "f"] \arrow[dr, "g"'] &   \\
					&                                   & B \\
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				\item Let $M' \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $m' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', A)$. Suppose that $f \circ_{\bSet} m' = g \circ_{\bSet} m'$. \rex{} \tcr{ref prev ex} implies that $(E, \iota_E) \in \Eqzr_{\bSet}(f,g)$. Thus 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item there exists a unique $\al \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M, E)$ such that $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \al = m$,
					\item there exists a unique $\al' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', E)$ such that $\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \al' = m'$,
				\end{itemize}
				i.e. the following diagram commutes:
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					M' \arrow[dr, "m'"] \arrow[bend right=60, swap, dashed]{dd}{\al'}&     & B \\
					M \arrow[r, "m"] \arrow[d, "\al"', dashed] & A \arrow[ur, "f"] \arrow[dr, "g"'] &   \\
					E \arrow[ur, "\iota_E"'] &                                  & B \\
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				Since $\iota_E \circ m|^E = m$, uniqueness of $\al$ implies that $\al = m|^E$. Since $m$ is injective, $m|^E \in \Iso_{\bSet}(M, E)$. 
				\begin{itemize}
					\item Define $\phi \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$ by $\phi' \defeq \al^{-1} \circ_{\bSet} \al'$. Then 
					\begin{align*}
						m \circ_{\bSet} \phi 
						& = (\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} m|^E) \circ_{\bSet} (\al^{-1} \circ_{\bSet} \al') \\
						& = \iota_E \circ_{\bSet} (m|^E \circ_{\bSet} \al^{-1}) \circ_{\bSet} \al' \\
						& = \iota_E \circ_{\bSet} (\al \circ_{\bSet} \al^{-1}) \circ_{\bSet} \al' \\
						& = \iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \id_E \circ_{\bSet} \al' \\
						& = \iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \al' \\
						& = m'.
					\end{align*}
					\item  
					\begin{itemize}
						\item Let $\phi_0 \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$. Suppose that $m \circ \phi_0 = m'$. Then 
						\begin{align*}
							\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} (\al \circ_{\bSet} \phi_0) 
							& = (\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} \al) \circ_{\bSet} \phi_0 \\
							& = (\iota_E \circ_{\bSet} m|^E) \circ_{\bSet} \phi_0 \\
							& = m \circ_{\bSet} \phi_0 \\
							& = m'.
						\end{align*}
						Uniqueness of $\al'$ implies that $\al \circ_{\bSet} \phi_0 = \al'$. Since $\phi_0 \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$ such that $m \circ \phi_0 = m'$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\phi_0 \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$, $m \circ \phi_0 = m'$ implies that $\al \circ_{\bSet} \phi_0 = \al'$.
						\item In particular, \tcr{ref prev part (above)} implies that $\al \circ_{\bSet} \phi = \al'$.
						\item Let $\phi' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$. Suppose that $m \circ \phi' = m'$. \tcr{ref above prev parts} implies that
						\begin{align*}
							\al \circ_{\bSet} \phi' 
							& = \al' \\
							& = \al \circ_{\bSet} \phi.
						\end{align*}
						Since 
						\begin{align*}
							\al
							& = m|^E \\
							& \in \Iso_{\bSet}(M,E) \\
							& \subset \Mono_{\bSet}(M, E),
						\end{align*}
						we have that $\phi' = \phi$. Since $\phi' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$ with $m \circ \phi' = m'$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $\phi' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$, $m \circ \phi' = m'$ implies that $\phi' = \phi$.
					\end{itemize}
				\end{itemize}
				Thus there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$ such that $m \circ_{\bSet} \phi = m'$. Since $M' \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $m' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', A)$ with $f \circ_{\bSet} m' = g \circ_{\bSet} m'$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $M' \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $m' \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', A)$, $f \circ_{\bSet} m' = g \circ_{\bSet} m'$ implies that there exists a unique $\phi \in \Hom_{\bSet}(M', M)$ such that $m \circ_{\bSet} \phi = m'$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
				\[ 
				\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
					M' \arrow[dr, "m'"] \arrow[dd, "\phi"', dashed]&     & B \\
					& A \arrow[ur, "f"] \arrow[dr, "g"'] &   \\
					M \arrow[ur, "m"'] &                                  & B \\
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
			\end{enumerate}
			Therefore $(M, m) \in \Eqzr_{\bSet}(f,g)$. Hence $m \in \RegMono_{\bSet}$. Since $m \in \Mono_{\bSet}$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $m \in \Mono_{\bSet}$, $m \in \RegMono_{\bSet}$. Thus $\Mono_{\bSet} \subset \RegMono_{\bSet}$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Since $\RegMono_{\bSet} \subset \Mono_{\bSet}$ and $\Mono_{\bSet} \subset \RegMono_{\bSet}$, we have that $\RegMono_{\bSet} = \Mono_{\bSet}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Subobjects and Quotient Objects}
	
	\begin{defn}
		\tcr{maybe move this to subsection on subcategories, define wide category generated by hom closed morphisms}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $H \subset \Hom_{\MC}$. Then $H$ is said to be \tbf{hom closed} if 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\item 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		\tcr{define wide category with all morphisms mono, resp epi}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. We define 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{the restriction of $\MC$ to $\Mono_{\MC}$,} denoted $\bMono(\MC, M)$, by
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Obj(\bMono(\MC, M)) \defeq \Obj(\MC)$
				\item For $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\bMono(\MC, M)}(A,B) \defeq \Mono_{\MC}(A,B)$
				\item For $A,B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\bMono(\MC, M)}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\bMono(\MC, M)}(B, C)$, $g \circ_{\bMono(\MC, M)} f \defeq g \circ_{\MC} f$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item \tbf{the restriction of $\MC$ to $\Epi_{\MC}$,} denoted $\bEpi(\MC)$, by
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Obj(\bEpi(\MC)) \defeq \Obj(\MC)$
				\item For $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\bEpi(\MC)}(A,B) \defeq \Epi_{\MC}(A,B)$
				\item For $A,B, C \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\bEpi(\MC)}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\bEpi(\MC)}(B, C)$, $g \circ_{\bEpi(\MC)} f \defeq g \circ_{\MC} f$.
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\bMono(\MC, M)$ is a category ,
				\item $\bMono(\MC, M)$ is a wide subcategory of $\MC$,
			\end{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\bEpi(\MC)$ is a category,
				\item $\bEpi(\MC)$ is a wide subcategory of $\MC$.
			\end{enumerate}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\tcr{clear.} \tcr{fill out, ref exercies showing that composition of mono is mono, $\id_X$ is mono}
	\end{proof}

	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $M \subset \Mono_{\MC}$, $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Mono_{\MC}(A,B)$. Then $(A, f)$ is said to be an \tbf{$M$-subobject} of $B$ if $f \in M$.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $M \subset \Mono_{\MC}$ and $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. We define the \tbf{category of $M$-subobjects of $X$}, denoted $\Sub^M_{\MC}(X)$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\Sub^M_{\MC}(X)) \defeq \{(A, \al) \in \Obj(\MC/X): \text{$\al$ is an $M$-subobject of $X$}\}$
			\item for $(A,f), (B,g) \in \Obj(\Sub_{\MC}^M(X))$, $\Hom_{(\Sub_{\MC}^M(X))}((A,f), (B,g)) \defeq \Hom_{\MC/X}((A,f), (B,g))$
			\item 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
