	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:subcats:0001}
		Let $\MC$ be a category. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $\MD$ be categories. Then $\MD$ is said to be a \tbf{subcategory of $\MC$}, denoted $\MD \subset \MC$, if 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $\Obj(\MD) \subset \Obj(\MC)$
				\item for each $A, B \in \Obj(\MD)$, $\Hom_{\MD}(A,B) \subset \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$
				\item for each $A,B,C \in \Obj(\MD)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(A, B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MD}(B, C)$, $g \circ_{\MD} f = g \circ_{\MC} f$
				\item for each $A \in \Obj(\MD)$, $\id_A^{\MD} = \id_A^{\MC}$
			\end{enumerate}
			\item We define $\Subcat(\MC) \defeq \{\MD \in \Cat: \text{$\ML$ is a subcategory of $\MC$}\}$. \tcr{need to give more justification for why we restrict to $\Cat$, with universes, this should not be an issue, but need to formalize it}
			\item We define the \tbf{subcategory relation on $\Subcat(\MC)$}, denoted ${\leqcat} \subset \Subcat(\MC) \times \Subcat(\MC)$, by $\MD \leqcat \MC$ iff $\MD$ is a subcat of $\MC$.  
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MD \in \Subcat(\MC)$. We define the \tbf{inclusion functor} from $\MD$ to $\MC$, denoted $\iota_{\MD}^{\MC}:\MD \rightarrow \MC$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\iota_{\MD}^{\MC}(X) \defeq X, \quad X \in \Obj(\MD)$
			\item $\iota_{\MD}^{\MC}(f) \defeq f \in \Hom_{\MD}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we may write $\iota_{\MD}$ in place of $\iota_{\MD}^{\MC}$.
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MD \in \Subcat(\MC)$. Then $\iota_{\MD}:\MD \rightarrow \MC$ is a functor. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $X, Y \in \Obj(\MD)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X,Y)$. By \rd{def:basics:contructs:subcats:0001},
			\begin{align*}
				\iota_{\MD}(f)
				& = f \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(X,Y) \\
				& \subset \Hom_{\MC}(X,Y) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\iota_{\MD}(X), \iota_{\MD}(Y)).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $X,Y,Z \in \Obj(\MD)$, $g \in \Hom_{\MD}(X,Y)$ and $h \in \in \Hom_{\MD}(Y,Z)$. By \rd{def:basics:contructs:subcats:0001},
			\begin{align*}
				\iota_{\MD}(g \circ_{\MD} f)
				& = g \circ_{\MD} f \\
				& = g \circ_{\MC} f \\
				& = \iota_{\MD}(g) \circ_{\MC} \iota_{\MD}(f).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $X \in \Obj(\MD)$. By \rd{def:basics:contructs:subcats:0001},
			\begin{align*}
				\iota_{\MD}(\id_X^{\MD})
				& = \id_X^{\MD} \\
				& = \id_X^{\MC} \\
				& = \id_{\iota_{\MD}(X)}^{\MC}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
		Hence $\iota_{\MD}:\MD \rightarrow \MC$ is a functor. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		We define the \tbf{forgetful functor from $\Cat$ to $\bQuiv$}, denoted $\text{Forget}^{\Cat}_{\bQuiv}: \Cat \rightarrow \bQuiv$
		\tcr{finish}  
	\end{defn}

		Let $\MC$ be a category and $H \subset \Hom_{\MC}$. We define the \tbf{subcategory of $\MC$ generated by $H$}, denoted $\SubcatGen(H, \MC)$, by $\SubcatGen(H, \MC) \defeq $
	\end{defn}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Suppose that $\MD$ is a subcategory of $\MC$. Then $\MC$ is said to be 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{full} if for each $A, B \in \Obj(\MD)$, $\Hom_{\MD}(A,B) = \Hom_{\MC}(A,B)$,
			\item \tbf{wide} or \tbf{lluf} if for each $\Obj(\MD) = \Obj(\MC)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		The motivation for the adjective ``lluf" seems to be that it is just ``full" backwards.  
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex}
		content...
	\end{ex}
	
	
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{erase after making iff}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $\MD_0 \subset \Obj(\MC)$ and $\MD_1 \subset \Hom_{\MC}$. Define $\MD_1^{(2)} \subset \MD_1 \times \MD_1$ by $\MD_1^{(2)} \defeq \{(g,f) \in \MD_1 \times \MD_1: \dom_{\MC}(g) = \cod_{\MC}(f)\}$. If 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\dom_{\MC}(\MD_1), \cod_{\MC}(\MD_1) \subset \MD_0$,
			\item $\circ_{\MC}(\MD_1^{(2)}) \subset \MD_1$,
			\item for each $X \in \MD_0$, $\id_X^{\MC} \in \MD_1$,
		\end{itemize}
		then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item $(\MD_0, \MD_1, \dom_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}, \cod_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}, \circ_{\MC}|_{\MD_1^{(2)}})$ is a category,
			\item $(\MD_0, \MD_1, \dom_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}, \cod_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}, \circ_{\MC}|_{\MD_1^{(2)}})$ is a subcategory of $\MC$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Set $\dom_{\MD} \defeq \dom_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}$, $\cod_{\MD} \defeq \cod_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}$, $\circ_{\MD} \defeq \circ_{\MC}|_{\MD_1^{(2)}}$ and $\MD \defeq (\MD_0, \MD_1, \dom_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}, \cod_{\MC}|_{\MD_1}, \circ_{\MC}|_{\MD_1^{(2)}})$.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item \tbf{(Composition:)} \\
				For each $(g,f) \in \MD_1^{(2)}$, 
				\begin{align*}
					\dom_{\MD}(g \circ_{\MD} f)
					& = \dom_{\MC}(g \circ_{\MC}) \\
					& = \dom_{\MC}(f) \\
					& = \dom_{\MD}(f).
				\end{align*}
				and 
				\begin{align*}
					\cod_{\MD}(g \circ_{\MD} f)
					& = \cod_{\MC}(g \circ_{\MC}) \\
					& = \cod_{\MC}(g) \\
					& = \cod_{\MD}(g).
				\end{align*}
				\item \tbf{(Associativity:)} \\
				For each $f,g,h \in \MD_1$, if $(g,f), (h,g) \in \MD_1^{(2)}$, then 
				\begin{align*}
					(h \circ_{\MD} g) \circ_{\MD} f 
					& = (h \circ_{\MC} g) \circ_{\MC} f \\
					& = h \circ_{\MC} (g \circ_{\MC} f) \\
					& = h \circ_{\MD} (g \circ_{\MD} f).
				\end{align*}  
				\item \tbf{(Identity:)} \\
				Let $X \in \MD_0$. Since $\id_X^{\MC} \in \MD_1$,  
				\begin{align*}
					\dom_{\MD}(\id_X^{\MC}) 
					& = \dom_{\MC}(\id_X^{\MC}) \\
					& = X,
				\end{align*}
				\begin{align*}
					\cod_{\MD}(\id_X^{\MC}) 
					& = \cod_{\MC}(\id_X^{\MC}) \\ 
					& = X,
				\end{align*}
				and for each $f, g \in \MD_1$, if $\dom_{\MD}(f) = X$ and $\cod_{\MD}(g) = X$, then 
				\begin{align*}
					f \circ_{\MD} \id_X^{\MC}
					& = f \circ_{\MC} \id_X^{\MC} \\
					& = f
				\end{align*}
				and 
				\begin{align*}
					\id_X^{\MC} \circ_{\MD} g 
					& = id_X^{\MC} \circ_{\MC} g \\
					& = g.
				\end{align*} 
			\end{enumerate}
			Hence $\MD$ is a category.
			\item Clear by construction.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Product Categories}
	
	\subsection{Introduction}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:products:0001}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. We define the \textbf{product category of $\MC$ and $\MD$}, denoted $\MC \times \MD$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\Obj(\MC \times \MD) \defeq \Obj(\MC) \times \Obj(\MD)$
			\item for each $(A, A'), (B, B') \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD)$, 
			$$\Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((A, A'), (B, B')) \defeq \Hom_{\MC}(A, B) \times \Hom_{\MC}(A', B').$$
			\item for each  $(A, A'), (B, B'), (C, C') \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD)$, $(f, f') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((A, A'), (B, B'))$ and $(g, g') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((B, B'), (C, C'))$, 
			$$(g,g') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (f, f') \defeq  (g \circ_{\MC} f, g' \circ_{\MD} f')$$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0002}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Then $\MC \times \MD$ is a category. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \textbf{well-definedness of composition: } \\ 
			Let $(A, A'), (B, B'), (C, C') \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD)$, $(f, f') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((A, A'), (B, B'))$ and $(g, g') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((B, B'), (C, C'))$. Then $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, B)$, $g \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, C)$, $f'  \in \Hom_{\MD}(A', B')$, and  $g' \in \Hom_{\MD}(B', C')$. Hence $g \circ_{\MC} f \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, C)$ and $g' \circ_{\MD} f' \in \Hom_{\MD}(A', C')$. Thus 
			\begin{align*}
				(g,g') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (f, f') 
				&= (g \circ_{\MC} f, g' \circ_{\MD} f') \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((A, A'), (C, C'))
			\end{align*}
			Thus, composition is well defined. \\
			\item \textbf{associativity of composition:} \\
			Let $(A, A'), (B, B'), (C, C'), (D, D') \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD)$, $(f, f') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((A, A'), (B, B'))$, $(g, g') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((B, B'), (C, C'))$ and $(h, h') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}((C, C'), (D, D'))$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				[(h, h') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (g , g') ] \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (f, f')
				& = (h \circ_{\MC} g, h' \circ_{\MD} g') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (f, f') \\
				& = ((h \circ_{\MC} g) \circ_{\MC} f, (h' \circ_{\MD} g') \circ_{\MD} f') \\
				& = (h \circ_{\MC} ( g \circ_{\MC} f), h' \circ_{\MD} (g' \circ_{\MD} f')) \\
				& = (h, h') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (g \circ_{\MC} f, g' \circ_{\MD} f') \\
				& = (h, h') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} [(g, g') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (f, f')]
			\end{align*} 
			Thus composition is associative. \\
			\item \textbf{existence of identities: } \\
			Let $(A, B) \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD)$, $(f, f'), (g,g') \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}$. Suppose that $\dom_{\MC \times \MD}(f, f') = (A, B)$ and $\cod_{\MC \times \MD}(g, g') = (A, B)$. Then $\dom_{\MC}(f) = A$, $\dom_{\MD}(f') = B$, $\cod_{\MC}(g) = A$ and  $\cod_{\MD}(g') = B$. Hence
			\begin{align*}
				(f, f') \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (\id_A^{\MC}, \id_{B}^{\MD}) 
				& = (f \circ_{\MC} \id_A^{\MC}, f' \circ_{\MD} \id_{B}^{\MD}) \\
				& = (f, f)
			\end{align*}
			and
			\begin{align*}
				(\id_A^{\MC}, \id_{B}^{\MD})  \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (g, g')
				& = (\id_A^{\MC} \circ_{\MC} g , \id_{B}^{\MD} \circ_{\MD} g') \\
				& = (g, g')
			\end{align*}
			Therefore $\id_{(A, B)}^{\MC \times \MD} = (\id_A^{\MC}, \id_{B}^{\MD})$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0002.1}
		Let $\MC$ and $\MD$ be categories. Then $\MC$ and $\MD$ are small iff $\MC \times \MD$ is small.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		We have that 
		\begin{align*}
			\text{$\MC$ and $\MD$ are small}
			& \iff \Obj(\MC), \Hom_{\MC}, \Obj(\MD), \Hom_{\MD} \in \Obj(\bSet) \\
			& \text{$\iff \Obj(\MC) \times \Obj(\MD) \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $\Hom_{\MC} \times \Hom_{\MD} \in \Obj(\bSet)$} \\
			& \text{$\iff (\Obj(\MC \times \MD) \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $\Hom_{\MC \times \MD} \in \Obj(\bSet)$} \\
			& \text{$\iff \MC \times \MD$ is small}.
		\end{align*}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:products:0003}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC, \MD$ be categories and $F: \MA \rightarrow \MC$, $G: \MB \rightarrow \MD$. We define the \tbf{product functor of $F$ and $G$}, denoted $F \times G: \MA \times \MB \rightarrow  \MC \times \MD$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $F \times G(A, B) \defeq (F(A), G(B)), \quad (A, B) \in \Obj(\MA \times \MB)$,  
			\item $F \times G(f,g) \defeq (F(f), G(g)), \quad (f,g) \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC, \MD$ be categories and $F: \MA \rightarrow \MC$, $G: \MB \rightarrow \MD$. Then $F \times G$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $X, Y \in \Obj(\MA \times \MB)$ and $h \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}(X, Y)$. Then there exist $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$ such that $X = (A_1, B_1)$, $Y = (A_2, B_2)$ and $h = (f, g)$. Since $F(f) \in \Hom_{\MC}(F(A_1), F(A_2))$ and $G(g) \in \Hom_{\MD}(G(B_1), G(B_2))$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				F \times G(h)
				& = F \times G(f,g) \\
				& = (F(f), G(g)) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB} ((F(A_1), G(B_1)), (F(A_2), G(B_2))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MA \times \MB} (F \times G(A_1, B_1), F \times G(A_2, B_2)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MA \times \MB} (F \times G(X), F \times G(Y) ).
			\end{align*} 
			\item Let $X_1,X_2,X_3 \in \Obj(\MA \times \MB)$, $h_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}(X_1,X_2)$ and $h_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}(X_2, X_3)$. Then there exist $A_1, A_2, A_3 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $B_1, B_2, B_3 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $f_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $g_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$, $f_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_2, A_3)$ and $g_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_2, B_3)$, such that $X_1 = (A_1, B_1)$, $X_2 = (A_2, B_2)$, $X_3 = (A_3, B_3)$, $h_{1,2} = (f_{1,2}, g_{1,2})$ and $h_{2,3} = (f_{2,3}, g_{2,3})$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				F \times G(h_{2,3} \circ_{\MA \times B} h_{1,2}) 
				& = F \times G ((f_{2,3}, g_{2,3}) \circ_{\MA \times \MB}, (f_{1,2}, g_{1,2})) \\
				& = F \times G (f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}, g_{2,3} \circ_{\MB} g_{1,2}) \\
				& = (F(f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}), G(g_{2,3} \circ_{\MB} g_{1,2})) \\
				& = (F(f_{2,3}) \circ_{\MC} F(f_{1,2}), G(g_{2,3}) \circ_{\MD} G(g_{1,2})) \\
				& = (F(f_{2,3}), G(g_{2,3})) \circ_{\MC \times \MD} (F(f_{1,2}), G(g_{1,2})) \\
				& = F \times G(f_{2,3}, g_{2,3}) \circ_{\MC \times \MD} F \times G(f_{1,2}, g_{1,2}) \\
				& = F \times G(h_{2,3}) \circ_{\MC \times \MD} F \times G(h_{1,2}).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $X \in \Obj(\MA \times \MB)$. Then there exists $A \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $B \in \Obj(\MB)$ such that $X = (A, B)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				F \times G(\id_X^{\MA \times \MB})
				& = F \times G(\id_{(A,B)}^{\MA \times \MB}) \\
				& = F \times G(\id_A^{\MA}, \id_B^{\MB}) \\
				& = (F(\id_A^{\MA}), G(\id_B^{\MB})) \\
				& = (\id_{F(A)}^{\MC}, \id_{G(B)}^{\MD}) \\
				& = \id_{(F(A), G(B))}^{\MC \times \MD} \\
				& = \id_{F \times G(A,B)}^{\MC \times \MD} \\
				& = \id_{F \times G(X)}^{\MC \times \MD}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $F \times G$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004.1}
		 Let $\MC_1, \MC_2, \MC_3 \MD_1, \MD_2, \MD_3 \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $F_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC_1, \MC_2)$, $F_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC_2, \MC_3)$, $G_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MD_1, \MD_2)$ and $G_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MD_2, \MD_3)$. Then 
		 $$(F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}) \times (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}) = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat} (F_{1,2} \times G_{1,2}).$$
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $A \in \Obj(\MC_1)$ and $B \in \Obj(\MD_1)$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				[(F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}) \times (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})](A,B)
				& = (F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}(A), (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}(B)) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} (F_{1,2}(A)), G_{2,3}(G_{1,2}(B))) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3})(F_{1,2}(A), G_{1,2}(B)) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \times  G_{2,3})((F_{1,2} \times G_{1,2})(A, B)) \\
				& = [(F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat } (F_{1,2} \times G_{1,2})](A, B).
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MC_1)$, $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MD_1)$
			Then 
			\begin{align*}
				(F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}) \times (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})(f,g)
				& = (F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}(f), G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}(g)) \\
				& = (F_{2,3}(F_{1,2}(f)), G_{2,3}(G_{1,2}(g)) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3})(F_{1,2}(f), G_{1,2}(g)) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3})((F_{1,2} \times G_{1,2})(f,g)) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat}(f,g).
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
		Hence $(F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}) \times (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}) = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat} (F_{1,2} \times G_{1,2})$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004.2}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\id_{\MC}^{\Cat} \times \id_{\MD}^{\Cat} = \id_{\MC \times \MD}^{\Cat}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $(A,B) \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MC}^{\Cat} \times \id_{\MD}^{\Cat}(A,B)
				& = (\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}(A), \id_{\MD}^{\Cat}(B)) \\
				& = (A, B) \\
				& = \id_{\MC \times \MD}^{\Cat}(A,B).
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $(f,g) \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD}$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{\MC}^{\Cat} \times \id_{\MD}^{\Cat}(f,g) \\
				& = (\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}(f), \id_{\MD}^{\Cat}(g)) \\
				& = (f, g) \\
				& = \id_{\MC \times \MD}^{\Cat}(f,g).
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
		Hence $\id_{\MC}^{\Cat} \times \id_{\MD}^{\Cat} = \id_{\MC \times \MD}^{\Cat}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:products:0004.3}
		We define the \tbf{product functor on $\Cat$}, denoted $(- \times -): \Cat \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $(- \times -) (\MA, \MB) \defeq \MA \times \MB , \quad (\MA, \MB) \in \Obj(\Cat \times \Cat)$,
			\item $(- \times -) (F, G) \defeq F \times G$, $\quad$ $(\MC_1, \MD_1), (\MC_1, \MD_2) \in \Obj(\Cat \times \Cat)$ and $(F, G) \in \Hom_{\Cat \times \Cat}((\MC_1, \MD_1), (\MC_2, \MD_2))$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004.4}
		We have that $(- \times -): \Cat \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $(\MC_1, \MD_1), (\MC_2, \MD_2) \in \Obj(\Cat \times \Cat)$ and $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\Cat \times \Cat}((\MC_1, \MD_1), (\MC_2, \MD_2))$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				(- \times -)(F,G)
				& = F \times G \\
				& \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC_1 \times \MD_1, \MC_2 \times \MD_2) \\
				& = \Hom_{\Cat}((- \times -)(\MC_1, \MD_1), (- \times -)(\MC_2, \MD_2)).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $(\MC_1, \MD_1), (\MC_2, \MD_2), (\MC_3, \MD_3) \in \Obj(\Cat \times \Cat)$, $(F_{1,2},G_{1,2}) \in \Hom_{\Cat \times \Cat}((\MC_1, \MD_1), (\MC_2, \MD_2))$ and $(F_{2,3},G_{2,3}) \in \Hom_{\Cat \times \Cat}((\MC_2, \MD_2), (\MC_3, \MD_3))$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004.1} implies that
			\begin{align*}
				(- \times -)((F_{2,3},G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat \times \Cat} (F_{1,2},G_{1,2}))
				& = (- \times -)(F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}, G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}) \times (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}) \\
				& = (F_{2,3} \times G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat} (F_{1,2} \times G_{1,2}) \\
				& = (- \times -)(F_{2,3}, G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat} (- \times -)(F_{1,2}, G_{1,2}).
			\end{align*} 
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0004.2} implies that for each $(\MC, \MD) \in \Obj(\Cat \times \Cat)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				(- \times -)(\id_{(\MC, \MD)}^{\Cat \times \Cat})
				& = (- \times -)(\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}, \id_{\MD}^{\Cat}) \\
				& = \id_{\MC}^{\Cat} \times \id_{\MD}^{\Cat} \\
				& = \id_{\MC \times \MD}^{\Cat} \\
				& = \id_{(- \times -)(\MC, \MD)}^{\Cat}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $(- \times -): \Cat \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{maybe switch order of 'basic construction and operations' and 'fundamental structures' and redo the previous exercises by showing that if $\MC$ has finite products, then $\times : \MC \times \MC \mapsto \MC$ given by $\times (A,B) \defeq A \times B$ and $\times(f, g) \defeq f \times g$ is a functor and then the previous exercise would be a corollary with $\MC = \Cat$ (if we show that $(\MC \times \MD, (\pi_{\MC}, \pi_{\MD})) \in \Prod_{\Cat}(\MC, \MD)$ and $F \times G$ is the product of morphisms in $\Cat$ as defined in the section on products in the basic ).}
	\end{ex}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Slicing}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:products:0005}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MD$ be categories, $F: \MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MD$ and $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$. We define the 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{slice functor of $F$ at $B_0$}, denoted $F(\cdot, B_0): \MA \rightarrow \MD$ by 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $F(\cdot, B_0)(A) \defeq F(A, B_0), \quad A \in \Obj(\MA)$
				\item $F(\cdot, B_0)(f) \defeq F(f, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}), \quad f \in \Hom_{\MA}$
			\end{itemize} 
			\item \tbf{slice functor of $F$ at $A_0$}, denoted $F(A_0, \cdot): \MB \rightarrow \MD$ 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $F(A_0, \cdot)(B) \defeq F(A, B), \quad B \in \MB$
				\item $F(A_0, \cdot)(g) \defeq F(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g), \quad g \in \Hom_{\MB}$
			\end{itemize} 			
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0006}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MD$ be categories, $F: \MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MD$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $F(\cdot, B_0): \MA \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor,
			\item for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $F(A_0, \cdot): \MB \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$.
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item Let $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f_{12} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$. Then $(f_{12}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}((A_1, B_0), (A_2, B_0))$. Since $F:\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MD$, we have that
				\begin{align*}
					F(\cdot, B_0)(f_{12})
					& = F(f_{12}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \\
					& \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A_1, B_0), F(A_2, B_0)) \\
					& = \Hom_{\MD}(F(\cdot, B_0)(A_1), F(\cdot, B_0)(A_2)) \\
				\end{align*}
				\item Let $A_1, A_2, A_3 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $f_{12} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $f_{23} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_2, A_3)$. Since $F:\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MD$, we have that
				\begin{align*}
					F(\cdot, B_0)(f_{23} \circ_{\MA} f_{12})
					& = F(f_{23} \circ_{\MA} f_{12}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \\
					& = F(f_{23} \circ_{\MA} f_{12}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB} \circ_{\MB} \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \\
					& = F[(f_{23}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \circ_{\MA \times \MB} (f_{12}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB})] \\
					& = F(f_{23}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \circ_{\MD} F(f_{12}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \\
					& = F(\cdot, B_0)(f_{23}) \circ_{\MD} F(\cdot, B_0)(f_{12}).
				\end{align*} 
				\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MA)$. Then 
				\begin{align*}
					F(\cdot, B_0)(\id_A^{\MA}) 
					& = F(\id_A^{\MA}, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \\
					& = F(\id_{(A, B_0)}^{\MA \times \MB}) \\
					& = \id_{F(A, B_0)}^{\MD} \\
					& = \id_{F(\cdot, B_0)(A)}^{\MD}.  
				\end{align*}
			\end{enumerate}
			Thus $F(\cdot, B_0):\MA \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor.
			\item Similar to previous part \tcr{ref prev part}.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:products:0007}
		Let $\MA, \MB$ be categories, $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$. We define the
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{embedding functor of $\MA$ into $\MA \times \MB$ at $B_0$}, denoted $\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}: \MA \rightarrow \MA \times \MB$, by 
			$\iota_{\MA}^{B_0} \defeq \id_{\MA} \times \id_{\MB}(\cdot, B_0)$
			\item \tbf{embedding functor of $\MB$ into $\MA \times \MB$ at $A_0$}, denoted $\iota_{\MB}^{A_0}: \MB \rightarrow \MA \times \MB$, by $\iota_{\MB}^{A_0} \defeq \id_{\MA} \times \id_{\MB}(A_0, \cdot)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0008}
		Let $\MA, \MB$ be categories. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $B_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}:\MA \rightarrow \MA \times \MB$ is a functor and 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}(A) \defeq (A, B_0), \quad A \in \Obj(\MA)$,
				\item $\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}(f) \defeq (f, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}), \quad f \in \Hom_{\MA}$,
			\end{itemize}
			\item for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $\iota_{\MB}^{A_0}:\MB \rightarrow \MA \times \MB$ is a functor and 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\iota_{\MB}^{A_0}(B) \defeq (A_0, B), \quad B \in \Obj(\MB)$,
				\item $\iota_{\MB}^{A_0}(g) \defeq (\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g), \quad g \in \Hom_{\MB}$.
			\end{itemize}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$. \tcr{By prev exercises}, $\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}$ is a functor. By definition, we have that
			\begin{itemize}
				\item for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$, 
				\begin{align*}
					\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}(A)
					& = \id_{\MA} \times \id_{\MB}(A, B_0) \\
					& = (\id_{\MA}(A), \id_{\MB}(B_0)) \\ 
					& = (A, B_0),
				\end{align*}
				\item for each $f \in \Hom_{\MA}$, 
				\begin{align*}
					\iota_{\MA}^{B_0}(f)
					& = \id_{\MA} \times \id_{\MB}(f, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}) \\
					& = (\id_{\MA}(f), \id_{\MB}(\id_{B_0}^{\MB})) \\
					& = (f, \id_{B_0}^{\MB}).
				\end{align*}
			\end{itemize} 
			\item Similar \tcr{to prev part (ref prev part)}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:products:0009}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories, $F,G :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$, $\al: F \Rightarrow G$, $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$. We define the
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{slice transformation of $\al$ at $A_0$}, denoted $\al_{(A_0, \cdot)}: F(A_0, \cdot) \Rightarrow G(A_0, \cdot)$, by 
			$(\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_B \defeq \al_{(A_0, B)}$
			\item \tbf{slice transformation of $\al$ at $B_0$}, denoted $\al_{(\cdot, B_0)}: F(\cdot, B_0) \Rightarrow G(\cdot, B_0)$, by 
			$(\al_{(\cdot, B_0)})_A \defeq \al_{(A, B_0)}$. 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0010}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories, $F,G :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$ and $\al: F \Rightarrow G$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $\al_{(A_0, \cdot)}: F(A_0, \cdot) \Rightarrow G(A_0, \cdot)$ is a natural transformation,
			\item for each $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $\al_{(\cdot, B_0)}: F(\cdot, B_0) \Rightarrow G(\cdot, B_0)$ is a natural transformation.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$.
			\begin{itemize}
				\item By construction, for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, 
				\begin{align*}
					(\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_B
					& = \al_{(A_0, B)} \\
					& \in \Hom_{\MC}(F(A_0, B), G(A_0, B)) \\
					& = \Hom_{\MC}(F(A_0, \cdot)(B), G(A_0, \cdot)(B)).
				\end{align*}
				\item Let $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$. Since $\al:F \Rightarrow G$, we have that for each $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$, $G(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g) \circ_{\MC} \al_{(A_0, B_1)} = \al_{(A_0, B_2)} \circ_{\MC} F(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
				\[
				\begin{tikzcd}
					F(A_0, B_1)  \arrow[r, "\al_{(A_0, B_1)}"] \arrow[d, "{F(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g)}"'] & G(A_0, B_1) \arrow[d, "{G(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g)}"] \\
					F(A_0, B_2) \arrow[r, "\al_{(A_0, B_2)}"] &  G(A_0, B_2).
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				Therefore
				\begin{align*}
					G(A_0, \cdot)(g) \circ_{\MC} (\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_{B_1}
					& = G(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g) \circ_{\MC} \al_{(A_0, B_1)} \\
					& = \al_{(A_0, B_2)}  \circ_{\MC} F(\id_{A_0}^{\MA}, g) \\
					& = (\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_{B_2} \circ_{\MC} F(A_0, \cdot)(g),
				\end{align*}
				i.e. the following diagram commutes: 
				\[
				\begin{tikzcd}
					F(A_0, \cdot)(B_1)  \arrow[r, "{(\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_{B_1}}"] \arrow[d, "{F(A_0, \cdot)(g)}"'] & G(A_0, \cdot)(B_1) \arrow[d, "{G(A_0, \cdot)(g)}"] \\
					F(A_0, \cdot)(B_2) \arrow[r, "{(\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_{B_2}}"] &  G(A_0, \cdot)(B_2).
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				Since $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $G(A_0, \cdot)(g) \circ_{\MC} (\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_{B_1} = (\al_{(A_0, \cdot)})_{B_2} \circ_{\MC} F(A_0, \cdot)(g)$.  
			\end{itemize}
			Thus $\al_{(A_0, \cdot)}: F(A_0, \cdot) \Rightarrow G(A_0, \cdot)$ is a natural transformation. Since $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $\al_{(A_0, \cdot)}: F(A_0, \cdot) \Rightarrow G(A_0, \cdot)$ is a natural transformation.
			\item \tcr{Similar to previous part (ref prev part)}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0010.1}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories, $F_1,F_2, F_3 :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$, $\al_{1,2}: F_1 \Rightarrow F_2$ and $\al_{2,3}: F_2 \Rightarrow F_3$. Then 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $(\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)} = (\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, \cdot)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}$.
			\item for each $B_0 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $(\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(\cdot, B_0)} = (\al_{2,3})_{(\cdot, B_0)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(\cdot, B_0)}$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $B \in \Obj(\MB)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				[(\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B
				& = (\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(A_0, B)} \\
				& = (\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, B)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, B)} \\
				& = [(\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B \circ [(\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B \\
				& = [(\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, \cdot)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B.
			\end{align*}
			Since $B \in \Obj(\MB)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, $[(\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B = [(\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, \cdot)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B$. Thus $(\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)} = (\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, \cdot)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}$. Since $A_0 \in \Obj$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $(\al_{2,3} \circ \al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)} = (\al_{2,3})_{(A_0, \cdot)} \circ (\al_{1,2})_{(A_0, \cdot)}$.
			\item \tcr{Similar to prev part (ref prev part)}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0010.2}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories and $F \in \MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $(\id_F)_{(A_0, \cdot)} = \id_{F(A_0, \cdot)}$,
			\item for each $B_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $(\id_F)_{(\cdot, B_0)} = \id_{F(\cdot, B_0)}$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$. Then for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				[(\id_F)_{(A_0, \cdot)}]_B
				& = (\id_F)_{(A_0, B)} \\
				& = \id_{F(A_0, B)} \\
				& = \id_{F(A_0, \cdot)(B)} \\
				& = (\id_{F(A_0, \cdot)})_B.
			\end{align*}
			Hence $(\id_F)_{(A_0, \cdot)} = \id_{F(A_0, \cdot)}$. Since $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A_0 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $(\id_F)_{(A_0, \cdot)} = \id_{F(A_0, \cdot)}$.
			\item \tcr{Similart to (ref) prev part}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage

	\section{Functor Categories}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:func_cats:0001}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$. We define the \tbf{evaluation functor from $\MC \times \MD^{\MC}$ to $\MD$}, denoted $\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}:\MC \times \MD^{\MC} \rightarrow \MD$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(A, F) \defeq F(A), \quad (A,F) \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD^{\MC})$
			\item $\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(f, \al) \defeq G(f) \circ_{\MD} \al_A, \quad (f, \al) \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD^{\MC}}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0002}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}: \eval:\MC \times \MD^{\MC} \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $(A, F), (B,G) \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD^{\MC})$ and $(f, \al) \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD^{\MC}}((A, F), (B,G))$. Then $G(f) \in \Hom_{\MD}(G(A), G(B))$ and $\al_A \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), G(A))$. Hence
			\begin{align*}
				\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(f, \al)
				& = G(f) \circ_{\MD} \al_A \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), G(B)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MD}(\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(A, F), \eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(B, G)). 
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $(A, F), (B,G), (C, H) \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD^{\MC})$, $(f, \al) \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD^{\MC}}((A, F), (B,G))$ and $(g, \be) \in \Hom_{\MC \times \MD^{\MC}}((B, G), (C,H))$. 
			Since $\be \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(G,H)$, we have that $H(f) \circ_{\MD} \be_A = \be_B \circ_{\MD} G(f)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				G(A)  \arrow[r, "\be_A"] \arrow[d, "{G(f)}"'] & H(A) \arrow[d, "{H(f)}"] \\
				G(B)  \arrow[r, "\be_B"] & H(B).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\begin{align*}
				\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}((g, \be) \circ_{\MC \times \MD^{\MC}} (f, \al))
				& = \eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(g \circ_{\MC} f, \be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al) \\
				& = H(g \circ_{\MC} f) \circ_{\MD} (\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al)_A \\
				& = H(g) \circ_{\MD} (H(f) \circ_{\MD} \be_A) \circ_{\MD} \al_A \\
				& = H(g) \circ_{\MD} (\be_B \circ_{\MD} G(f)) \circ_{\MD} \al_A \\
				& = (H(g) \circ_{\MD} \be_B) \circ_{\MD} (G(f) \circ_{\MD} \al_A) \\
				& = \eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(g, \be) \circ_{D} \eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(f, \al)).
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $(A, F) \in \Obj(\MC \times \MD^{\MC})$, we have that 
			\begin{align*}
				\eval_{(\MC, \MD)} (\id_{(A,F)}^{\MC \times \MD^{\MC}}) 
				& = \eval_{(\MC, \MD)} (\id_A^{\MC}, \id_F^{\MD^{\MC}}) \\ 
				& = \eval_{(\MC, \MD)} (\id_A^{\MC}, \id_F^{\MD^{\MC}}) \\ 
				& = F(\id_A^{\MC}) \circ_{\MD} (\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}})_A \\
				& = \id_{F(A)}^{\MD} \circ_{\MD} \id_{F(A)}^{\MD} \\
				& = \id_{F(A)}^{\MD} \\
				& = \id_{\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}(A,F)}^{\MD}
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $\eval_{(\MC, \MD)}:\MC \times \MD^{\MC} \rightarrow \MD$ is a functor. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{Find two functors $F,G: \Cat \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ such that $\eval \mapsto \eval_{(\MC, \MD)}$ is a natural isomorphism $F \Rightarrow G$.}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:func_cats:0003}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$, $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$, $H,J \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $H \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$, we define the \tbf{internal Hom functor object induced by $F$ and $G$ at $H$}, denoted $G^F(H) \in \Obj(\MB_2^{\MA_2})$, by $G^F(H) \defeq G \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} F$
			\item \tbf{internal Hom functor natural transformation induced by $F$ and $G$ at $\al$}, denoted $G^F(\al): G^F(H) \Rightarrow G^F(J)$, by $G^F(\al)_A \defeq G(\al_{F(A)})$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0004}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$, $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$, $H,J \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$. Then $G^F(\al):G^F(H) \Rightarrow G^F(J)$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MA_2)$. Since $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$, we have that $\al_{F(A} \in \Hom_{\MB_1}(H(F(A)), J(F(A)))$. Then
			\begin{align*}
				G^F(\al)_A
				& = G(\al_{F(A)}) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MB_2}(G(H(F(A))), G(J(F(A)))) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MB_2}(G^F(H)(A)), G^F(J)(A)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $A \in \Obj(\MA_2)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MA_2)$, $G^F(\al)_A \in \Hom_{\MB_2}(G^F(H)(A)), G^F(J)(A))$.
			\item Let $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA_2)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA_2}(A_1, A_2)$. Define $A'_1, A'_2 \in \Obj(\MA_1)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MA_1}(A'_1, A'_2)$ by $A'_k \defeq F(A_k)$ and $f' \defeq F(f)$. Since $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$, we have that
			\begin{align*}
				J(f') \circ_{\MB_1} \al_{A'_1}
				& = \al_{A'_2} \circ_{\MB_1} H(f'),
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				H(A'_1)  \arrow[r, "\al_{A'_1}"] \arrow[d, "{H(f')}"'] & J(A'_1) \arrow[d, "{J(f')}"] \\
				H(A'_2) \arrow[r, "\al_{A'_2}"] &  J(A'_2).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Therefore,
			\begin{align*}
				G^F(J)(f) \circ_{\MB_2} G^F(\al)_{A_1}
				& = [G \circ_{\Cat} J \circ_{\Cat} F](f) \circ_{\MB_2} G(\al_{F(A_1)}) \\
				& = G(J(F(f))) \circ_{\MB_2} G(\al_{F(A_1)}) \\
				& = G(J(f')) \circ_{\MB_1} G(\al_{A'_2}) \\
				& = G(J(f') \circ_{\MB_1} \al_{A'_1}) \\
				& = G(\al_{A'_2} \circ_{\MB_1} H(f')) \\
				& = G(\al_{A'_2}) \circ_{\MB_2} G(H(f')) \\
				& = G(\al_{F(A_2)}) \circ_{\MB_2} G(H(F(f))) \\
				& = G(\al_{F(A_2)}) \circ_{\MB_2} [G \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} F](f) \\
				& = G^F(\al)_{A_2} \circ_{\MB_2} G^F(H)(f),
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				G^F(H)(A_1)  \arrow[r, "(G^F_\al)_{A_1}"] \arrow[d, "{G^F(H)(f)}"'] & G^F(J)(A_1) \arrow[d, "{G^F(J)(f)}"] \\
				G^F(H)(A_2) \arrow[r, "(G^F_\al)_{A_2}"] &  G^F(J)(A_2).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Since $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA_2)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA_2}(A_1, A_2)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA_2)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA_2}(A_1, A_2)$, $G^F(J)(f) \circ_{\MB_2} G^F(\al)_{A_1} = G^F(\al)_{A_2} \circ_{\MB_2} G^F(H)(f)$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Thus $G^F(\al):G^F(H) \Rightarrow G^F(J)$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0005}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$, $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$, $H,J, K \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(J,K)$. Then $G^F(\be \circ_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}} \al) = G^F(\be) \circ_{\MB_2^{\MA_2}} G^F(\al)$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		For each $A \in \Obj(\MA_2)$,
		\begin{align*}
			G^F(\be \circ_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}} \al)_A
			& = G([\be \circ_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}} \al]_{F(A)}) \\
			& = G(\be_{F(A)} \circ_{\MB_1} \al_{F(A)}) \\
			& = G(\be_{F(A)}) \circ_{\MB_2} G(\al_{F(A)}) \\
			& = G^F(\be)_A \circ_{\MB_2} G^F(\al)_A \\
			& = (G^F(\be) \circ_{\MB_2^{\MA_2}} G^F(\al))_A.
		\end{align*}
		Hence $G^F(\be \circ_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}} \al) = G^F(\be) \circ_{\MB_2^{\MA_2}} G^F(\al)$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0006}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$, $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$, $H \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$, Then $G^F(\id_H^{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}) = \id_{G^F(H)}^{\MB_2^{\MA_2}}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		For each $A \in \MA_2$,
		\begin{align*}
			G^F(\id_H^{\MB_1^{\MA_1}})_A
			& = G((\id_H^{\MB_1^{\MA_1}})_{F(A)}) \\
			& = G(\id_{H(F(A))}^{\MB_1}) \\
			& = \id_{G(H(F(A)))}^{\MB_1} \\
			& = \id_{G \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} F(A)}^{\MB_1} \\
			& = \id_{G^F(H)(A)}^{\MB_1} \\
			& = (\id_{G^F(H)}^{\MB_2^{\MA_2}})_A.
		\end{align*}
		Hence $G^F(\id_H^{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}) = \id_{G^F(H)}^{\MB_2^{\MA_2}}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:func_cats:0007}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$ and $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$. We define the \tbf{internal Hom functor of $\Cat$ at $(F,G)$}, denoted $[F,G]_{\Cat}:\MB_1^{\MA_1} \rightarrow \MB_2^{\MA_2}$ or $G^F:\MB_1^{\MA_1} \rightarrow \MB_2^{\MA_2}$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $[F,G]_{\Cat}(H) \defeq G^F(H), \quad H \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ 
			\item $[F,G]_{\Cat}(\al) \defeq G^F(\al), \quad \al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0008}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$ and $(F,G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$. Then $G^F:\MB_1^{\MA_1} \rightarrow \MB_2^{\MA_2}$ is a functor. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0004} implies that for each $H, J \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$, $G^F(\al) \in \Hom_{\MB_2^{\MA_2}}(G^F(H), G^F(J))$. 
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0005} implies that for each $H,J, K \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H,J)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(J,K)$, $G^F(\be \circ_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}} \al) = G^F(\be) \circ_{\MB_2^{\MA_2}} G^F(\al)$.
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0006} implies that for each $A \in \Obj(\MA_2)$, $G^F(\id_H^{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}) = \id_{G^F(H)}^{\MB_2^{\MA_2}}$.
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $G^F:\MB_1^{\MA_1} \rightarrow \MB_2^{\MA_2}$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0009}
		Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2), (\MA_3, \MB_3) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$, $(F_{1,2}, G_{1,2}) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$ and  $(F_{2,3}, G_{2,3}) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_2, \MB_2), (\MA_3, \MB_3))$. Then 
		$$(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}} = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}.$$
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $H \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$, 
			\begin{align*}
				(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}}(H)
				& = G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2} \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} (F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}) \\
				& = G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2} \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} (F_{1,2} \circ_{\Cat} F_{2,3}) \\
				& = G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} (G_{1,2} \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} F_{1,2}) \circ_{\Cat} F_{2,3} \\
				& = G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} (G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}(H)) \circ_{\Cat} F_{2,3} \\
				& = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} (G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}(H)) \\
				& = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}(H).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $H,K \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H, K)$. Then for each $A \in \Obj(\MA_3)$,
			\begin{align*}
				[(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}}(\al)]_A
				& = [(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{1,2} \circ_{\Cat} F_{2,3}}(\al)]_A \\
				& = G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}(\al_{F_{1,2} \circ_{\Cat} F_{2,3}(A)}) \\
				& = G_{2,3}(G_{1,2}(\al_{F_{1,2}(F_{2,3}(A))})) \\
				& = G_{2,3}(G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}(\al)_{F_{2,3}(A)}) \\
				& = [G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}}(G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}(\al))]_A \\
				& = [G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}} (\al)]_A
			\end{align*}
			Thus $(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}}(\al) = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}} (\al)$. Since $H,K \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H, K)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $H,K \in \Obj(\MB_1^{\MA_1})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB_1^{\MA_1}}(H, K)$, $(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}}(\al) = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}} (\al)$.
		\end{itemize}
		Therefore $(G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}} = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0010}
		Let $\MA, \MB \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then
		$$(\id_{\MB}^{\Cat})^{\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}} = \id_{\MB^{\MA}}^{\Cat}.$$
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		Let $\MA, \MB \in \Obj(\Cat)$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $H \in \Obj(\MB^{\MA})$, 
			\begin{align*}
				(\id_{\MB}^{\Cat})^{\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}}(H) 
				& = \id_{\MB}^{\Cat} \circ_{\Cat} H \circ_{\Cat} \id_{\MA}^{\Cat} \\
				& = H \\
				& = \id_{\MB^{\MA}}^{\Cat}(H).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $H,K \in \Obj(\MB^{\MA})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MB^{\MA}}(H, K)$. Then for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$,
			\begin{align*}
				[(\id_{\MB}^{\Cat})^{\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}}(\al)]_A
				& = \id_{\MB}^{\Cat}(\al_{\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}(A)}) \\
				& = \id_{\MB}^{\Cat}(\al_A) \\
				& = \al_A \\
				& = [\id_{\MB^{\MA}}^{\Cat}(\al)]_A
			\end{align*}
			Hence $(\id_{\MB}^{\Cat})^{\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}}(\al) = \id_{\MB^{\MA}}^{\Cat}(\al)$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:func_cats:0011}
		We define the \tbf{internal Hom functor of $\Cat$}, denoted $[\cdot, \cdot]_{\Cat}: \op{\Cat} \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $[\MC, \MD]_{\Cat} \defeq \MD^{\MC}, \quad (\MC, \MD) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$,
			\item $[F, G]_{\Cat} \defeq G^F, \quad (F, G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0012}
		We have that $[\cdot, \cdot]_{\Cat}: \op{\Cat} \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we may write $[\cdot, \cdot]$ in place of $[\cdot, \cdot]_{\Cat}$.
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$ $(F, G) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0008} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				[\cdot, \cdot](F,G)
				& = G^F \\
				& \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MB_1^{\MA_1}, \MB_2^{\MA_2}) \\
				& = \Hom_{\Cat}([\MA_1, \MB_1], [\MA_2, \MB_2]) \\
				& = \Hom_{\Cat}([\cdot, \cdot](\MA_1, \MB_1), [\cdot, \cdot](\MA_2, \MB_2)).
			\end{align*}
			\item $(\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2), (\MA_2, \MB_3) \in \Obj(\op{\Cat} \times \Cat)$ $(F_{1,2}, G_{1,2}) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_1, \MB_1), (\MA_2, \MB_2))$ and  $(F_{2,3}, G_{2,3}) \in \Hom_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat}((\MA_2, \MB_2), (\MA_3, \MB_3))$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0009} then implies that
			\begin{align*}
				[\cdot, \cdot]((F_{2,3}, G_{2,3}) \circ_{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat} (F_{1,2}, G_{1,2})) 
				& = [\cdot, \cdot](F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}, G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}) \\
				& = (G_{2,3} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2})^{F_{2,3} \circ_{\op{\Cat}} F_{1,2}} \\
				& = G_{2,3}^{F_{2,3}} \circ_{\Cat} G_{1,2}^{F_{1,2}} \\
				& = [\cdot, \cdot](F_{2,3}, G_{2,3}) \circ_{\Cat} [\cdot, \cdot](F_{1,2}, G_{1,2}).
			\end{align*}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:func_cats:0010} implies that for each $\MA, \MB \in \Obj(\Cat)$,
			\begin{align*}
				[\cdot, \cdot](\id_{(\MA, \MB)}^{\op{\Cat} \times \Cat})
				& = [\cdot, \cdot](\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}, \id_{\MB}^{\Cat}) \\
				& = (\id_{\MB}^{\Cat})^{\id_{\MA}^{\Cat}} \\
				& = \id_{\MB^{\MA}}^{\Cat} \\
				& = \id_{[\cdot, \cdot](\MA, \MB)}^{\Cat}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $[\cdot, \cdot]: \op{\Cat} \times \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Opposition}
	
	\tcr{relabel and organize}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:intro:0006}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be a categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$. We define the \tbf{opposite of $F$}, denoted $\op{F}: \op{\MC} \rightarrow \op{\MD}$, by
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\op{F}(A) \defeq F(A), \quad A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$
			\item $\op{F}(f) \defeq F(f), \quad f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:intro:0007}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be a categories and $F:\MC \rightarrow \MD$. Then $\op{F}: \op{\MC} \rightarrow \op{\MD}$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item For each $A,B \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\op{F}(f)
				& = f \\
				& \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,B) \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(\op{F}(A), \op{F}(B)).
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $A,B,C \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(B,C)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\op{F}(g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f) 
				& = g \circ_{\op{\MC}} f \\
				& = \op{F}(g) \circ_{\op{\MC}} \op{F}(f). 
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\op{F}(\id_A^{\op{\MC}})
				& = \id_A^{\op{\MC}} \\
				& = \id_{\op{F}(A)}^{\op{\MC}}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $\op{F}: \op{\MC} \rightarrow \op{\MD}$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0011}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MA, \MB)$ and $G \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MB, \MC)$. Then $\op{G \circ_{\Cat} F} = \op{G} \circ_{\Cat} \op{F}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $A \in \Obj(\op{A})$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\op{G \circ_{\Cat} F}(A)
				& = G \circ_{\Cat} F(A) \\
				& = G(F(A)) \\
				& = \op{G}(\op{F}(A)) \\
				& = \op{G} \circ_{\Cat} \op{F}(A).
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $A,B,C \in \Obj(\op{\MA})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MA}}(A,B)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\op{G \circ_{\Cat} F}(f) 
				& = G \circ_{\Cat} F(f) \\
				& = G(F(f)) \\
				& = \op{G}(\op{F}(f)) \\
				& = \op{G} \circ_{\Cat} \op{F}(f).
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
		Thus $\op{G \circ_{\Cat} F} = \op{G} \circ_{\Cat} \op{F}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0012}
		Let $\MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\op{\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}} = \id_{\op{\MC}}^{\Cat}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$,
			\begin{align*}
				\op{\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}}(A)
				& = \id_{\MC}^{\Cat}(A) \\
				& = A \\
				& = \id_{\op{\MC}}^{\Cat}(A).
			\end{align*}
			\item For each $A,B \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A,B)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\op{\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}}(f)
				& = \id_{\MC}^{\Cat}(f) \\
				& = f \\
				& = \id_{\op{\MC}}^{\Cat}(f).
			\end{align*}
		\end{itemize}
		Thus $\op{\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}} = \id_{\op{\MC}}^{\Cat}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:functors:small_cat:0013}
		We define the \tbf{opposite functor on $\Cat$}, denoted $\opp^{\Cat}: \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\opp^{\Cat}(\MC) \defeq \op{\MC}$
			\item $\opp^{\Cat}(F) \defeq \op{F}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		When the context is clear, we may write $\opp$ in place of $\opp^{\Cat}$.
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0014}
		We have that $\opp^{\Cat}: \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:functors:intro:0007} implies that for each $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MC, \MD)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\opp(F)
				& = \op{F} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\op{\MC}, \op{\MD}) \\
				& = \Hom_{\Cat}(\opp(\MC), \opp(\MD)).
			\end{align*}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0011} implies that for each $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $F \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MA, \MB)$ and $G \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\MB, \MC)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\opp(G \circ_{\Cat} F)
				& = \op{G \circ_{\Cat} F} \\
				& = \op{G} \circ_{\Cat} \op{F} \\
				& = \opp((G) \circ_{\Cat} \opp(F).
			\end{align*}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:functors:small_cat:0012} implies that for each $\MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\opp(\id_{\MC}^{\Cat})
				& = \op{\id_{\MC}^{\Cat}} 
				& = \id_{\op{\MC}}^{\Cat} \\
				& = \id_{\opp(\MC)}^{\Cat}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $\opp: \Cat \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0012}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be categories, $F,G:\MC \rightarrow \MD$ functors and $\al:F \Rightarrow G$ a natural transformation. We define the \tbf{opposite of $\al$}, denoted $\op{\al}: \op{G} \Rightarrow \op{F}$, by 
		$$\op{\al}_A \defeq \al_A, \quad A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$$
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0013}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be categories, $F,G:\MC \rightarrow \MD$ functors and $\al:F \Rightarrow G$ a natural transformation. Then $\op{\al}: \op{G} \Rightarrow \op{F}$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$. Then $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ and
			\begin{align*}
				\op{\al}_A
				& = \al_A \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), G(A)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MD}}(G(A), F(A)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MD}}(\op{G}(A), \op{F}(A)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $\op{\al}_A \in \Hom_{\op{\MD}}(\op{G}(A), \op{F}(A))$.
			\item Let $A, B \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$. Then $A, B \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(B, A)$. Since $\al:F \Rightarrow G$ is a natural transformation, $G(f) \circ_{\MD} \al_B = \al_A \circ_{\MD} F(f)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(B)  \arrow[r, "\al_B"]  \arrow[d, "F(f)"']  & G(B)   \arrow[d, "G(f)"]\\
				F(A) \arrow[r, "\al_A"'] &  G(A).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Therefore
			\begin{align*}
				\op{F}(f) \circ_{\op{\MD}} \op{\al}_A
				& = F(f) \circ_{\op{\MD}} \al_A \\
				& = \al_A \circ_{\MD} F(f) \\
				& = G(f) \circ_{\MD} \al_B \\
				& = \al_B \circ_{\op{\MD}} G(f) \\
				& = \op{\al}_B \circ_{\op{\MD}} \op{G}(f),
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				\op{G}(A)  \arrow[r, " \op{\al}_A "]  \arrow[d, "\op{G}(f)"']  & \op{F}(A)   \arrow[d, "\op{F}(f)"] \\
				\op{G}(B) \arrow[r, "\op{\al}_B"'] &  \op{F}(B).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Since $A, B \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A, B \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$, $\op{F}(f) \circ_{\op{\MD}} \op{\al}_A = \op{\al}_B \circ_{\op{\MD}} \op{G}(f)$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Thus $\op{\al}: \op{G} \Rightarrow \op{F}$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0014}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $F,G,H \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F,G)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(G,H)$. Then $\op{(\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al)} = \op{\al} \circ_{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}} \op{\be}$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		For each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$,
		\begin{align*}
			\op{(\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al)}_A
			& = (\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al)_A \\
			& = \be_A \circ_{\MD} \al_A \\
			& = \al_A \circ_{\op{\MD}} \be_A \\
			& = \op{\al}_A \circ_{\op{\MD}} \op{\be}_A \\
			& = (\op{\al} \circ_{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}} \op{\be})_A.
		\end{align*}
		Thus $\op{(\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al)} = \op{\al} \circ_{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}} \op{\be}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0015}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$. Then $\op{(\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}})} = \id_{\op{F}}^{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}}$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		For each $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, 
		\begin{align*}
			(\op{\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}}})_A
			& = (\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}})_A \\
			& = \id_{F(A)}^{\MD} \\
			& = \id_{F(A)}^{\op{\MD}} \\
			& = \id_{\op{F}(A)}^{\op{\MD}} \\
			& = (\id_{\op{F}}^{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}})_A.
		\end{align*}
		Thus $\op{(\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}})} = \id_{\op{F}}^{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$. We define the \tbf{opposite functor on $\MD^{\MC}$}, denoted $\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}: \MD^{\MC} \rightarrow \op{[(\op{\MD})^{{\op{\MC}}}]}$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(F) \defeq \op{F}$
			\item $\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\al) \defeq \op{\al}$
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC, \MD \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}: \MD^{\MC} \rightarrow \op{[(\op{\MD})^{{\op{\MC}}}]}$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $F,G \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F,G)$. \rex{ex:basics:functors:intro:0007} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(F), \opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(G) 
				& \in \Obj((\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}) \\
				& = \Obj(\op{[(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}]})
			\end{align*}
			and \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0013} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\al)
				& \in \Hom_{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}}(\op{G}, \op{F}) \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{[(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}]}}(\op{F}, \op{G}) \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{[(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}]}}(\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(F), \opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(G)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $F,G \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F,G)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $F,G \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F,G)$, $\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\al) \in \Hom_{\op{[(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}]}}(\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(F), \opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(G))$.
			\item Let $F,G,H \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(F,G)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MD^{\MC}}(G,H)$. \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0014} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al)
				& = \op{\be \circ_{\MD^{\MC}} \al} \\
				& = \op{\al} \circ_{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}} \op{\be} \\
				& = \op{\be} \circ_{\op{[(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}]}} \op{\al} \\
				& = \opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\be) \circ_{\op{[(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}]}} \opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\al).
			\end{align*}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0015} implies that for each $F \in \Obj(\MD^{\MC})$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}}) 
				& = \op{(\id_F^{\MD^{\MC}})} \\
				& = \id_{\op{F}}^{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}} \\
				& = \id_{\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}(F)}^{(\op{\MD})^{\op{\MC}}}. 
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $\opp_{(\MC, \MD)}: \MD^{\MC} \rightarrow \op{[(\op{\MD})^{{\op{\MC}}}]}$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		We define $\opp: [\cdot, \cdot]_{\Cat} \Rightarrow \opp^{\Cat} \circ_{\Cat} [\cdot, \cdot] \circ (\opp^{\Cat} , \opp^{\Cat})$ by 
		$\opp_{(\MC, \MD)} \defeq \opp_{(\MC, \MD)}$
		\tcr{rename stuff and reorganize the opposite stuff}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\o
	\end{ex}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\newpage
	\section{Currying}
	
	\begin{defn}  \ld{def:basics:contructs:currying:0001}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories, $F :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$, $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$. We define the 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \tbf{natural transformation from $F(A_1, \cdot)$ to $F(A_2, \cdot)$ induced by $f$}, denoted $\al(F)^f:F(A_1, \cdot) \Rightarrow F(A_2, \cdot)$, by $\al(F)^f_B \defeq F(f, \id_B^{\MB})$,
			\item \tbf{natural transformation from $F(\cdot, B_1)$ to $F(\cdot, B_2)$ induced by $g$}, denoted $\be(F)^g:F(\cdot, B_1) \Rightarrow F(\cdot, B_2)$, by $\be(F)^g_A \defeq F(\id_A^{\MA}, g)$,
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0002}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories and $F :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $\al(F)^f:F(A_1, \cdot) \Rightarrow F(A_2, \cdot)$ is a natural transformation,
			\item for each $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$ and $g_0 \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$, $\be(F)^g:F(\cdot, B_1) \Rightarrow F(\cdot, B_2)$ is a natural transformation.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$.
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $B \in \Obj(\MB)$. Then $(f, \id_B^{\MB}) \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}((A_1, B), (A_2, B))$. Therefore
				\begin{align*}
					\al(F)^f_B
					& = F(f, \id_B^{\MB}) \\
					& \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}(F(A_1, B), F(A_2, B)) \\
					& = \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}(F(A_1, \cdot)(B), F(A_2, \cdot)(B)).
				\end{align*}
				Since $B \in \Obj(\MB)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, $\al(F)^f_B \in \Hom_{\MA \times \MB}(F(A_1, \cdot)(B), F(A_2, \cdot)(B))$.
				\item Let $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$. Then 
				\begin{align*}
					F(A_2, \cdot)(g) \circ_{\MC} \al(F)^f_{B_1} 
					& = F(\id_{A_2}^{\MA}, g) \circ_{\MC} F(f, \id_{B_1}^{\MB}) \\
					& = F((\id_{A_2}^{\MA}, g) \circ_{\MA \times \MB} (f, \id_{B_1}^{\MB})) \\
					& = F(\id_{A_2}^{\MA} \circ_{\MA} f, g \circ_{\MB} \id_{B_1}^{\MB}) \\
					& = F(f, g) \\
					& = F(f \circ_{\MA} \circ_{\MA} \id_{A_1}^{\MA}, \id_{B_2}^{\MB} \circ_{\MB} g) \\
					& = F((f, \id_{B_2}^{\MB}) \circ_{\MA \times \MB} (\id_{A_1}^{\MA}, g)) \\
					& = F(f, \id_{B_2}^{\MB}) \circ_{\MC} F(\id_{A_1}^{\MA}, g) \\
					& = \al(F)^f_{B_2} \circ_{\MC} F(A_1, \cdot)(g),
				\end{align*} 
				i.e. the following diagram commutes:
				\[
				\begin{tikzcd}
					F(A_1, \cdot)(B_1)  \arrow[r, "{\al(F)^f_{B_1}}"] \arrow[d, "{F(A_1, \cdot)(g)}"'] & F(A_2, \cdot)(B_1) \arrow[d, "{F(A_2, \cdot)(g)}"] \\
					F(A_1, \cdot)(B_2) \arrow[r, "{\al(F)^f_{B_2}}"] &  F(A_2, \cdot)(B_2).
				\end{tikzcd}
				\]
				Since $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $B_1, B_2 \in \Obj(\MB)$ and $g \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$, $F(A_2, \cdot)(g) \circ_{\MC} \al(F)^f_{B_1} = \al(F)^f_{B_2} \circ_{\MC} F(A_1, \cdot)(g)$.
			\end{itemize}
			Thus $\al(F)^f:F(A_1, \cdot) \Rightarrow F(A_2, \cdot)$ is a natural transformation. Since $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $\al(F)^f:F(A_1, \cdot) \Rightarrow F(A_2, \cdot)$ is a natural transformation.
			\item Similar to \tcr{prev part (ref part)}.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0003}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories and $F :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item for each $A_1, A_2, A_3 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $f_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $f_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_2, A_3)$, $\al(F)^{f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}} = \al(F)^{f_{2,3}} \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \al(F)^{f_{1,2}} $
			\item for each $B_1, B_2, B_3 \in \Obj(\MB)$, $g_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_1, B_2)$ and $g_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MB}(B_2, B_3)$, $\be(F)^{g_{2,3} \circ_{\MB} g_{1,2}} = \be(F)^{g_{2,3}} \circ_{\MC^{\MA}} \be(F)^{g_{1,2}}$
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A_1, A_2, A_3 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $f_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $f_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_2, A_3)$. Then for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$,
			\begin{align*}
				(\al(F)^{f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}})_B
				& = F(f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}, \id_B^{\MB}) \quad \text{(by \rd{def:basics:contructs:currying:0001})} \\
				& = F(f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}, \id_B^{\MB} \circ_{\MB} \id_B^{\MB}) \\
				& = F((f_{2,3}, \id_B^{\MB}) \circ_{\MA \times \MB} (f_{1,2}, \id_B^{\MB})) \\
				& = F(f_{2,3}, \id_B^{\MB}) \circ_{\MC} F(f_{1,2}, \id_B^{\MB}) \\
				& = \al(F)^{f_{2,3}}_B \circ_{\MC} \al(F)^{f_{1,2}}_B \\
				& = (\al(F)^{f_{2,3}} \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \al(F)^{f_{1,2}})_B.
			\end{align*}
			Thus $\al(F)^{f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}} = \al(F)^{f_{2,3}} \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \al(F)^{f_{1,2}}$.
			\item \tcr{similar to prev part (ref prev part)}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0004}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC$ be categories and $F :\MA \times \MB \rightarrow \MC$. Then
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item For each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$, $\al(F)^{\id_A^{\MA}} = \id_{F(A, \cdot)}^{\MC^{\MB}}$.
			\item For each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, $\be(F)^{\id_B^{\MB}} = \id_{F(\cdot, B)}^{\MC^{\MA}}$.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item For each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, 
			\begin{align*}
				\al(F)^{\id_A^{\MA}}_B 
				& = F(\id_A^{\MA}, \id_B^{\MB}) \\
				& = F(\id_{(A,B)}^{\MA \times \MB}) \\
				& = \id_{F(A, B)}^{\MC} \\
				& = \id_{F(A, \cdot)(B)}^{\MC} \\
				& = (\id_{F(A, \cdot)})_B \quad \text{(by \rd{def:basics:nat_trans:cat_funct:0004})}.
			\end{align*}
			Since $B \in \Obj(\MB)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$, $\al(F)^{\id_A^{\MA}}_B = (\id_{F(A, \cdot)})_B$. Thus $\al(F)^{\id_A^{\MA}} = \id_{F(A, \cdot)}$.
			\item \tcr{Similar to prev part (ref prev part)}.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:currying:0005}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$. We define the \tbf{Curry functor induced by $F$}, denoted $\cur(F): \MA \rightarrow \MC^{\MB}$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\cur(F)(A) \defeq F(A, \cdot), \quad (A \in \Obj(\MA))$,
			\item $\cur(F)(f) \defeq \al(F)^f, \quad (f \in \Hom_{\MA})$,
		\end{itemize} 
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0006}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$. Then $\cur(F): \MA \rightarrow \MC^{\MB}$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0002} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\cur(F)(f)
				& = \al(F)^f \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(F(A_1, \cdot), F(A_2, \cdot)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(\cur(F)(A_1), \cur(F)(A_1)).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A_1, A_2, A_3 \in \Obj(\MA)$, $f_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ and $f_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_2, A_3)$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0003} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\cur(F)(f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2})
				& = \al(F)^{f_{2,3} \circ_{\MA} f_{1,2}} \\
				& = \al(F)^{f_{2,3}} \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \al(F)^{f_{1,2}} \\
				& = \cur(F)(f_{2,3}) \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \cur(F)(f_{1,2}).
			\end{align*} 
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\MA)$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0004} implies that,
			\begin{align*}
				\cur(F)(\id_A^{\MA})
				& = \al(F)^{\id_A^{\MA}} \\
				& = \id_{F(A, \cdot)}^{\MC^{\MB}} \\
				& = \id_{\cur(F)(A)}^{\MC^{\MB}}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $\cur(F):\MA \rightarrow \MC^{\MB}$ is a functor. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:currying:0007}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F,G \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F,G)$. We define the \tbf{Curry transformation induced by $\al$}, denoted $\cur(\al): \cur(F) \Rightarrow \cur(G)$ by 
		$$\cur(\al)_A \defeq \al_{(A, \cdot)}, \quad A \in \Obj(\MA).$$
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0008}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $F,G \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F,G)$. Then $\cur(\al): \cur(F) \Rightarrow \cur(G)$ is a natural transformation. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0010} implies that for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\cur(\al)_A
				& = \al_{(A, \cdot)} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(F(A, \cdot), G(A, \cdot)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(\cur(F)(A), \cur(G)(A)).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$. Since $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F,G)$, we have that
			\begin{align*}
				G(f, \id_B^{\MB}) \circ_{\MC} \al_{(A_1,B)}
				& = \al_{(A_2,B)} \circ_{\MC}  F(f, \id_{B}^{\MB}),
			\end{align*}
			i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				F(A_1, B)  \arrow[r, "{\al_{(A_1,B)} }"] \arrow[d, "{F(f, \id_B^{\MB})}"'] & G(A_1, B) \arrow[d, "{G(f, \id_B^{\MB})}"] \\
				F(A_2, B) \arrow[r, "{\al_{(A_2, B)}}"] &  G(A_2, B).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Therefore for each $B \in \Obj(\MB)$,
			\begin{align*}
				(\cur(G)(f) \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \cur(\al)_{A_1})_B
				& = \cur(G)(f)_B \circ_{\MC} (\cur(\al)_{A_1})_B \\
				& = G(f, \id_B^{\MB}) \circ_{\MC} \al_{(A_1,B)} \\
				& = \al_{(A_2,B)} \circ_{\MC}  F(f, \id_{B}^{\MB}) \\
				& = \cur(\al)_{A_1})_B \circ_{\MC} \cur(F)(f)_B \\
				& = (\cur(\al)_{A_1} \circ_{\MC} \cur(F)(f))_B.
			\end{align*}
			Hence $\cur(G)(f) \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \cur(\al)_{A_1} = \cur(\al)_{A_2} \circ_{\MC} \cur(F)(f)$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				\cur(F)(A_1)  \arrow[r, "{\cur(\al)_{A_1}}", Rightarrow] \arrow[d, "{\cur(F)(f)}"', Rightarrow] & \cur(G)(A_1) \arrow[d, Rightarrow, "{\cur(G)(f)}"] \\
				\cur(F)(A_2) \arrow[r, "{\cur(\al)_{A_2}}", Rightarrow] &  \cur(G)(A_2).
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			Since $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $A_1, A_2 \in \Obj(\MA)$ and $f \in \Hom_{\MA}(A_1, A_2)$, $\cur(G)(f) \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \cur(\al)_{A_1} = \cur(\al)_{A_2} \circ_{\MC} \cur(F)(f)$. 
		\end{itemize}
		Thus $\cur(\al):\cur(F) \Rightarrow \cur(G)$ is a natural transformation. 
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0009}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $F_1, F_2, F_3 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$, $\al_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F_1, F_2)$ and $\al_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F_2, F_3)$. Then $\cur(\al_{2,3} \circ_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}} \al_{1,2}) = \cur(\al_{2,3}) \circ_{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}} \cur(\al_{1,2})$.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0010.1} implies that for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$,
		\begin{align*}
			\cur(\al_{2,3} \circ_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}} \al_{1,2})_A
			& = (\al_{2,3} \circ_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}} \al_{1,2})_{(A, \cdot)} \\
			& = (\al_{2,3})_{(A, \cdot)} \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} (\al_{1,2})_{(A, \cdot)} \\
			& = \cur(\al_{2,3})_A \circ_{\MC^{\MB}} \cur(\al_{1,2})_A \\
			& = [\cur(\al_{2,3}) \circ_{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}} \cur(\al_{1,2})]_A.
		\end{align*}
		Therefore $\cur(\al_{2,3} \circ_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}} \al_{1,2}) = \cur(\al_{2,3}) \circ_{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}} \cur(\al_{1,2})$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0010}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $F \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$. Then $\cur(\id_F^{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}) = \id_{\cur(F)^{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}}}$. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0010.2} implies that for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$,
		\begin{align*}
			\cur(\id_F^{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}})_A
			& = (\id_F^{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}})_{(A, \cdot)} \\
			& = \id_{F(A, \cdot)}^{\MC^{\MB})} \\
			& = \id_{\cur(F)(A)}^{\MC^{\MB}} \\
			& = (\id_{\cur(F)}^{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}})_A.
		\end{align*}
		Hence $\cur(\id_F^{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}) = \id_{\cur(F)}^{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}}$.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:currying:0011}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. We define the \tbf{Curry functor from $\MC^{\MA \times \MB}$ to $(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$}, denoted $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}: \MC^{\MA \times \MB} \rightarrow (\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$ by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(F) \defeq \cur(F)$
			\item $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(\al) \defeq \cur(\al)$.
		\end{itemize}   
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0012}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}: \MC^{\MA \times \MB} \rightarrow (\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$ is a functor.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $F,G \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F, G)$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0008} implies that
			\begin{align*}
				\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(\al)
				& = \cur(\al) \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(\cur(F), \cur(G)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(F), \cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(G)).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $F_1, F_2, F_3 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$, $\al_{1,2} \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F_1, F_2)$ and $\al_{2,3} \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F_2, F_3)$. \rex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0009} implies that
			\begin{align*}
				\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(\al_{2,3} \circ_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}} \al_{1,2})
				 & = \cur((\al_{2,3} \circ_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}} \al_{1,2})) \\
				 & = \cur(\al_{2,3}) \circ_{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}} \cur(\al_{1,2}) \\
				 & = \cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(\al_{2,3}) \circ_{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}} \cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(\al_{1,2}).
			\end{align*}
			\item \rex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0010} implies that 
			\begin{align*}
				\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(\id_F^{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}) 
				& = \cur(\id_F^{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}) \\
				& = \id_{\cur(F)}^{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}} \\
				& = \id_{\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}(F)}^{(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Thus $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}: \MC^{\MA \times \MB} \rightarrow (\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$ is a functor.
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:basics:contructs:currying:0013}
		We define the \tbf{Currying natural transformation on $\Cat$}, denoted $\cur^{\Cat}: [(- \times -)_{\Cat}, -]_{\Cat} \Rightarrow [-, [-, -]_{\Cat}]_{\Cat}$, by  $(\cur^{\Cat})_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)} \defeq \cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}$
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:basics:contructs:currying:0014}
		We have that $\cur^{\Cat}:[(- \times -)_{\Cat}, -]_{\Cat} \Rightarrow [-, [-, -]_{\Cat}]_{\Cat}$ is a natural transformation.
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		\item \tcr{show it is in correct Hom set}
		\item \tcr{Show diagram commutes}
	\end{proof}

		\item define opposite functor $OP: \MC \rightarrow \op{\MC}$

	\begin{defn}
		
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		content...
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		content...
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. We define the \tbf{Currying functor from $(\MC)^{\MA \times \MB}$ to $(\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$}, denoted $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA,\MB, \MC)}: (\MC)^{\MA \times \MB} \rightarrow (\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$, by 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA,\MB, \MC)}(F) \defeq \cur(F), \quad (A \in \Obj(\MA))$
			\item $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA,\MB, \MC)}(\al)(A) \defeq \al_{(A, \cdot)}$.
		\end{itemize}
		\tcr{(need exercise showing that if $\MA, \MB$ are small, then $\MA \times \MB$ is small)}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MA, \MB, \MC \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA, \MB, \MC)}: \MC^{\MA \times \MB} \rightarrow (\MC^{\MB})^{\MA}$ is a functor. 
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $F,G \in \Obj(\MC^{\MA \times \MB})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MA \times \MB}}(F, G)$. Then for each $A \in \Obj(\MA)$,
			\begin{align*}
				\cur^{\Cat}_{\MA, \MB, \MC}(\al)(A)
				& = \al_{(A, \cdot)} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(F(A, \cdot), G(A, \cdot))  \quad \text{(by \tcr{ref prev ex})}\\
				& = \Hom_{\MC^{\MB}}(\cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA,\MB, \MC)}(F)(A), \cur^{\Cat}_{(\MA,\MB, \MC)}(G)(A)) 
			\end{align*}
			\item 
			\item 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
