	\newpage
	\chapter{Limits}
	
	\section{Cones and Cocones}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:cones_cocones:0001}
		Let $\MJ$, $\MC$ be categories and $D: \MJ \rightarrow \MC$. Then $D$ is said to be a \textbf{diagram of type $\MJ$ in $\MC$}.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		We are usually interested in the case that $\MJ$ is small. We will identify a diagram $D$ with its image \tcr{and we visualize a diagram by the generating morphisms in $\MJ$}. 
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{exmp} \tcr{create example reference}
		Define $\MJ$ by
		\begin{itemize}
			\item  $\Obj(\MJ) = \{1, 2, 3, 4\}$,
			\item for $i,j \in \Obj(\MJ)$, $\Hom_{\MJ}(i,j) = \{a_{ij}\}$.
		\end{itemize}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $D: \MJ \rightarrow \MC$. Without including the identity morphisms or compositions, we can visualize $D$ \tcr{by its set of generating morphisms (i.e. not including the identity morphisms)} as follows:
		\[
		\begin{tikzcd}
			&     1  \arrow[dl, "a_{1,3}"'] \arrow[r, "a_{1,2}"]        &  2 \arrow[dl, "a_{2,4}"] \\
			3 \arrow[r, "a_{3,4}"'] &        4   & \\
		\end{tikzcd}
		\overset{D}{\longrightarrow}
		\begin{tikzcd}
			&     D_1  \arrow[dl, "D_{1,3}"'] \arrow[r, "D_{1,2}"]        &  D_2 \arrow[dl, "D_{2,4}"] \\
			D_3 \arrow[r, "D_{3, 4}"'] &        D_4   & \\
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
	\end{exmp}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:cones_cocones:0003}
		Let $\MJ$, $\MC$ be categories. Suppose that $\MJ$ is small. Let $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item We define the \textbf{category of cones over $D$}, denoted $\Cone(D)$, by $\Cone(D) = (\Del^{\MJ} \doar D)$.
			\item We define the \textbf{category of cocones under $D$}, denoted $\Cocone(D)$, by $\Cocone(D) = (D \doar \Del^{\MJ})$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}\
		\begin{itemize}
			\item By defintion,
			\begin{align*}
				\Obj(\Cone(D)) 
				& = \{(X, \phi): X \in \Obj(\MC) \text{ and } \phi \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(\Del^{\MJ}(X), D) \} \\
				& = \{(X, \phi): X \in \Obj(\MC) \text{ and } \phi: \Del^{\MJ}_X \Rightarrow D\}
			\end{align*}
			and for $(X, \phi), (Y, \psi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$,
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\Cone(D)}((X, \phi),(Y, \psi)) 
				& = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y): \psi \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\al) = \phi \} \\
				& = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y): \psi \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \del^{\MJ}_{\al} = \phi \} \\
				& = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y): \text{for each $j \in \MJ$, $\psi_j \circ_{\MC} \al  = \phi_j$} \}.
			\end{align*}
			\tcr{make ex in subcategory section and rephrase this in terms of the commutative diagram on only the generating morphisms. This will enable us to more precisely cover limits like products and projective systems where the identity maorphisms are not typically included in the definition of a diagram, but rather only the set of generating morphisms}. Therefore, $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$ iff for each $i,j \in \Obj(\MJ)$ and $f_{i,j} \in \Hom_{\MJ}(i, j)$, the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				&  X \arrow[dl, "\phi_i"']  \arrow[dr, "\phi_j"] & \\
				D_i  \arrow[rr, "D_{f_{i,j}}"'] &&  D_j \\ 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]  
			and $\al \in \Hom_{\Cone(D)}((X, \phi), (Y, \psi))$ iff  for each $i,j \in \Obj(\MJ)$ and $(i,j) \in \Hom_{\MJ}(i, j)$ the following diagram commutes: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				& X \arrow[d, "\al"'] \arrow[bend right=30, swap]{ddl}{\phi_i} \arrow[bend left=30]{ddr}{\phi_j} \\
				&  Y \arrow[dl, "\psi_i"']  \arrow[dr, "\psi_j"] & \\
				D_i  \arrow[rr, "D_{i,j}"'] &&  D_j \\ 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item By defintion,
			\begin{align*}
				\Obj(\Cocone(D)) 
				& = \{(X, \phi): X \in \Obj(\MC) \text{ and } \phi \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}( D, \Del^{\MJ}(X)) \} \\
				& = \{(X, \phi): X \in \Obj(\MC) \text{ and } \phi: D \Rightarrow \Del^{\MJ}_X\}
			\end{align*}
			and for $(X, \phi), (Y, \psi) \in \Obj(\Cocone(D))$,
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\Cocone(D)}((X, \phi),(Y, \psi)) 
				& = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y): \Del^{\MJ}(\al) \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi = \psi \} \\
				& = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y): \del^{\MJ}_{\al} \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi = \psi \} \\
				& = \{\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, Y): \text{for each $j \in \MJ$, $\al \circ_{\MC} \phi_j = \psi_j$} \}.
			\end{align*}
			\tcr{make ex in subcategory section and rephrase this in terms of the commutative diagram on only the generating morphisms. This will enable us to more precisely cover limits like products and projective systems where the identity maorphisms are not typically included in the definition of a diagram, but rather only the set of generating morphisms}. Therefore, $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$ iff for each $i,j \in \Obj(\MJ)$ and $f_{i,j} \in \Hom_{\MJ}(i, j)$, the following diagram commutes:
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				D_i \arrow[dr, "\phi_i"'] \arrow[rr, "D_{f_{i,j}}"] &&  D_j \arrow[dl, "\phi_j"]  \\ 
				&  X  & 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]  
			and $\al \in \Hom_{\Cone(D)}((X, \phi), (Y, \psi))$ iff  for each $i,j \in \Obj(\MJ)$ and $(i,j) \in \Hom_{\MJ}(i, j)$ the following diagram commutes: 
			\[ 
			\begin{tikzcd}
				D_i \arrow[dr, "\phi_i"'] \arrow[rr, "D_{f_{i,j}}"] \arrow[bend right=30, swap]{ddr}{\psi_i}  & &  D_j \arrow[dl, "\phi_j"] \arrow[bend left=30]{ddl}{\psi_j} \\ 
				&  X  \arrow[d, "\al"'] & \\
				&  Y & 
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			
		\end{itemize}
	\end{note}
	
	
	
	\tcr{note that in the case of say a product of projective system, the category $\MJ$ does not include the identity morphisms in the Hom sets, to avoid having to specify the category with all morphisms, rephrase this definition in terms of the subcategory generated by a set of morphisms. This will need some exercises made in section on subcategories about natural transformations on a generated subcategory needing only to satisfy the composition rules in the def natl transf's on the generating morphisms of that category. maybe other similar exercises needed as well. For example in a product, when we write the diagram, we include the objects $X,Y$ but we never include the morphisms $\id_X, \id_Y$ in the diagram.}
	
	\begin{exmp} \tcr{ref example}
		Define $\MJ$ and $\MD$ \tcr{as in previous example}. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$. We can visualize $(X, \phi)$ as follows:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				&  &  X \arrow[ddd, "\phi_1"'] \arrow[ddddll, "\phi_3"']  \arrow[dddrrr, "\phi_2"], \arrow[ddddr, "\phi_4"] &       &    \\
				&       &     &       &    \\
				&       &     &       &    \\
				&       &  D_1  \arrow[dll, "D_{1,3}"'] \arrow[rrr, "D_{1,2}"]    &       & &  D2 \arrow[dll, "D_{2,4}"] \\
				D_3 \arrow[rrr, "D_{3,4}"'] &       &     &  D_4  &    \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cocone(D))$. We can visualize $(X, \phi)$ as follows:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				&  &  X \arrow[ddd, "\phi_1"'] \arrow[ddddll, "\phi_3"']  \arrow[dddrrr, "\phi_2"], \arrow[ddddr, "\phi_4"] &       &    \\
				&       &     &       &    \\
				&       &     &       &    \\
				&       &  D_1  \arrow[dll, "D_{1,3}"'] \arrow[rrr, "D_{1,2}"]    &       & &  D2 \arrow[dll, "D_{2,4}"] \\
				D_3 \arrow[rrr, "D_{3,4}"'] &       &     &  D_4  &    \\
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\tcr{FIX!!!!}
		\end{itemize}
	\end{exmp}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:limits:cones_cocones:0005}
		\tcr{show $\Cocone(D) \cong \op{\Cone(D)}$ (ref ex about comma categories and opposite categories)}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}
		
	\end{proof}
	
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:limits:cones_cocones:0006}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$.
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item For each $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$, 
				$$(X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_2)).$$
				\item For each $(X, \phi), (X', \phi') \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$ and $\eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_1)}((X, \phi), (X', \phi'))$, 
				$$\eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}((X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi), (X', \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi')).$$
			\end{enumerate} 
			\item Let $\be \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_2, D_1)$.
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item \tcr{FIX for cocones}
				\item 
			\end{enumerate} 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$. Then $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\phi \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(\Del^{\MJ}_X, D_1)$. Therefore $\al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(\Del^{\MJ}_X, D_2)$. Hence $(X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_2))$. 
				\item Let $(X, \phi), (X', \phi') \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$ and $\eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_1)}((X, \phi), (X', \phi'))$. Then $\eta \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, X')$ and $\phi' \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta) = \phi$. Therefore $\al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi' \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta) = \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi$. Hence $\eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}((X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi), (X', \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi'))$.
			\end{enumerate}
			\item \tcr{use duality}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:cones_cocones:0007}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$. We define the \tbf{cone functor induced by $\al$}, denoted $\Cn_{\al}: \Cone(D_1) \rightarrow \Cone(D_2)$, by 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Cn_{\al}(X, \phi) \defeq (X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi), \quad (X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$,
				\item $\Cn_{\al}(\eta) \defeq \eta, \quad \eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_1)}$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item \tcr{similar for cocone functor}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:limits:cones_cocones:0008}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$ and $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$. Then $\Cn_{\al}: \Cone(D_1) \rightarrow \Cone(D_2)$ is a functor.
			\item \tcr{similar for cocone functor}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item We note that \tcr{ref prev ex} implies that $\Cn_{\al}$ is well-defined. 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item \tcr{ref prev ex} implies that for each $(X, \phi), (X', \phi') \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$, and $\eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_1)}((X, \phi), (X', \phi'))$,
				\begin{align*}
					\Cn_{\al}(\eta)
					& = \eta \\
					& \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}((X, \al \circ{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi), (X', \al \circ{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi')) \\
					& = \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(X, \phi), \Cn_{\al}(X', \phi')).
				\end{align*}
				\item Let $(X, \phi), (Y, \psi), (Z, \chi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$ and $\mu \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_1)}((X, \phi), (Y, \psi))$ and $\nu \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_1)}((Y, \psi), (Z, \chi))$. Since $\Cone(D_1) = (\Del^{\MJ} \doar D_1)$ and $\Cone(D_2) = (\Del^{\MJ} \doar D_2)$,  \rd{def:basics:functors:comma_cat:0004} implies that 
				\begin{align*}
					\Cn_{\al}(\nu \circ_{\Cone(D_1)} \mu)
					& = \nu \circ_{\Cone(D_1)} \mu \\
					& = \nu \circ_{(\Del^{\MJ} \doar D_1)} \mu \\
					& = \nu \circ_{\MC} \mu \\
					& = \nu \circ_{(\Del^{\MJ} \doar D_2)} \mu \\
					& = \nu \circ_{\Cone(D_2)} \mu \\
					& = \Cn_{\al}(\nu) \circ_{\Cone(D_2)} \Cn_{\al}(\mu).
				\end{align*} 
				\item 
				By \rd{def:limits:cones_cocones:0003},  
				\begin{align*}
					\id_{(X, \phi)}^{\Cone(D_1)} 
					& = \id_{(X, \phi)}^{(\Del^{\MJ} \doar D_1)} \\
					& = \id_X^{\MC} \\
					& = \id_{(X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi)}^{(\Del^{\MJ} \doar D_2)} \\
					& = \id_{(X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi)}^{\Cone(D_2)}.
				\end{align*}
				Hence for each $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D_1))$,
				\begin{align*}
					\Cn_{\al}(\id_{(X, \phi)}^{\Cone(D_1)})
					& = \id_{(X, \phi)}^{\Cone(D_1)} \\
					& = \id_{(X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi)}^{\Cone(D_2)} \\
					& = \id_{\Cn_{\al}(X, \phi)}^{\Cone(D_2)}.
				\end{align*}
			\end{enumerate}
			Hence $\Cn_{\al}: \Cone(D_1) \rightarrow \Cone(D_2)$ is a functor.
			\item \tcr{use duality}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$. 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item We define the \tbf{Cone functor}, denoted $\Cone(\cdot):\MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \Cat$, by
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Cone(\cdot)(D) \defeq \Cone(D), \quad D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ 
				\item $\Cone(\cdot)(\al) \defeq \Cn_{\al}, \quad \al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}$.
			\end{itemize}
			\item \tcr{define cocone functor}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category, $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$. 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item We have that $\Cone(\cdot):\MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
			\item \tcr{show cocone functor is functor}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Set $C \defeq \Cone(\cdot)$.
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item Let $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$. Then 
				\begin{align*}
					C(\al)
					& = \Cn_{\al} \\
					& \in \Hom_{\Cat}(\Cone(D_1), \Cone(D_2)) \\
					& = \Hom_{\Cat}(C(D_1), C(D_2)).
				\end{align*}
				\item Let $D_1, D_2, D_3 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_2, D_3)$. Then for each $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$,
				\begin{align*}
					[C(\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al)](X, \phi)
					& = \Cn_{\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al} (X, \phi) \\
					& = (X, [\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al] \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi) \\
					& = (X, \be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} [\al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi]) \\
					& = \Cn_{\be}(X, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi) \\
					& = \Cn_{\be}(\Cn_{\al}(X, \phi)) \\
					& = C(\be)[C(\al)(X, \phi)] \\
					& = [C(\be) \circ_{\Cat} C(\al)](X, \phi)
				\end{align*} 
				Therefore $C(\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al) = C(\be) \circ_{\Cat} C(\al)$.
				\item Let $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$. Then for each $(X, \phi), (X', \phi') \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$ and $\eta \in \Hom_{\Cone(D)}((X, \phi), (X', \phi'))$,
				\begin{align*}
					C(\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}})(X, \phi)
					& = \Cn_{\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}}(X, \phi) \\
					& = (X, \id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}} \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi) \\
					& = (X, \phi) \\
					& = \id_{\Cone(D)}^{\Cat}(X, \phi) \\
					& = \id_{C(D)}^{\Cat}(X, \phi)
				\end{align*}
				and 
				\begin{align*}
					C(\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}})(\eta)
					& = \Cn_{\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}}(\eta) \\
					& = \eta \\
					& = \id_{\Cone(D)}^{\Cat}(\eta) \\
					& = \id_{C(D)}^{\Cat}(\eta).
				\end{align*}
				Thus $C(\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}) = \id_{C(D)}^{\Cat}$.
			\end{enumerate}
			Hence $\Cone(\cdot):\MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \Cat$ is a functor.
			\item \tcr{FINISH for cocones!!!!}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}



































	\newpage
	\section{Limits and Colimits}
	
	\subsection{Universal Morphisms}
	\tcr{make subsection instead of section and put it in section on limits after section on cones and cocones}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:limits_colimits:0001}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be a categories, $X \in \Obj(\MD)$, $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $A \in \Obj(\MC)$.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, F(A))$. Then $(A, f)$ is said to be a \textbf{universal morphism from $X$ to $F$} if for each $A' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, F(A'))$, there exists a unique $\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, A')$ such that $F(\al) \circ_{\MC} f = f'$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				X \arrow[r, "f"]  \arrow[dr, "f'"'] & F(A) \arrow[d, "F(\al)", dashed] \\
				& F(A')  
			\end{tikzcd}
			\hspace{.3cm}
			\begin{tikzcd}
				A  \arrow[d, "\al", dashed] \\
				A'  
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
			\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), X)$. Then $(A, f)$ is said to be a \textbf{universal morphism from $F$ to $X$} if for each $A' \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f' \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A'), X)$, there exists a unique $\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(A', A)$ such that $f \circ_{\MD} F(\al) = f'$, i.e. the following diagram commutes:
			\[
			\begin{tikzcd}
				X   & F(A) \arrow[l, "f"'] \\
				& F(A')  \arrow[ul, "f'"] \arrow[u, "F(\al)"', dashed]  
			\end{tikzcd}
			\hspace{.3cm}
			\begin{tikzcd}
				A \\
				A'  \arrow[u, "\al"', dashed]   
			\end{tikzcd}
			\]
		\end{itemize}
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{ex} \lex{ex:limits:limits_colimits:0002}
		Let $\MC, \MD$ be a categories, $X \in \Obj(\MD)$, $F: \MC \rightarrow \MD$ and $A \in \Obj(\MC)$.
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(X, F(A))$. Then $(A, f)$ is a universal morphism from $X$ to $F$ iff $(A, f)$ is $(X \doar F)$-initial. 
			\item Let $f \in \Hom_{\MD}(F(A), X)$. Then $(A, f)$ is a universal morphism from $F$ to $X$ iff $(A, f)$ is $(F \doar X)$-terminal.
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\item 
		\end{enumerate}
		\tcr{FINISH!!!}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{note}
		\tcr{make a comment on how if $(A, f)$ is universal from $X$ to $F$, then for each $(A', f')$, $f'$ is a post-processing of $f$ and $(A, f)$ is universal from $F$ to $X$, then for each $(A', f')$, $f'$ is a pre-processing of $f$}
	\end{note}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Limits and Colimits}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:limits_colimits:0003}
		Let $\MJ$, $\MC$ be categories. Suppose that $\MJ$ is small. Let $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$. Then $(X, \phi)$ is said to be a \textbf{$D$-limit}, denoted $(X, \phi) = \lim D$, if $(X, \phi)$ is a universal morphism from $\Del^{\MJ}$ to $D$.  
				\item We define the \tbf{limit set of $D$}, denoted $\limSet(D)$, by 
				$$\limSet D \defeq \{(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D)): \text{$\Obj(\Cone(D))$ is a $D$-limit}\}.$$
			\end{itemize}
			\item 
			\begin{itemize}
				\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cocone(D))$. Then $(X, \phi)$ is said to be a \textbf{$D$-colimit}, denoted $(X, \phi) = \colim D$, if $(X, \phi)$ is a universal morphism from $D$ to $\Del^{\MJ}$.  
				\item We define the \tbf{colimit set of $D$}, denoted $\colimSet(D)$, by 
				$$\colimSet D \defeq \{(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cocone(D)): \text{$\Obj(\Cocone(D))$ is a $D$-colimit}\}.$$
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
		\tcr{maybe define $\lim$ set, but maybe not, we want to be able to write $(X, \phi) = \lim D$, but we need some guarantee that anything we would possibly want to say is invariant under isomorphism, other wise different limits of $D$ may always be interchangeable, ask someone if we need to be careful here and define limit sets. For instance \href{https://ncatlab.org/nlab/show/commutativity+of+limits+and+colimits}{commutativity}}
	\end{defn}

	\begin{note}
		Let $\MJ$, $\MC$ be categories. Suppose that $\MJ$ is small. Let $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$. 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\text{$(X, \phi)$  is a limit of $D$} 
				& \iff \text{$(X, \phi)$ is $\Cone(D)$-terminal} \\
				& \iff \text{for each $(X', \phi') \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$, there exists a unique} \\
				& \hspace{1.3cm }\text{$\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X', X)$ such that for each $j \in \MJ$, $\phi_j \circ_{\MC} \al = \phi'_j$}
			\end{align*} 
			\item Let $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cocone(D))$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\text{$(X, \phi)$  is a colimit of $D$} 
				& \iff \text{$(X, \phi)$ is $\Cocone(D)$-initial} \\
				& \iff \text{for each $(X', \phi') \in \Obj(\Cocone(D))$, there exists a unique} \\
				& \hspace{1.3cm }\text{$\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, X')$ such that for each $j \in \MJ$, $\al \circ_{\MC} \phi_j = \phi'_j $}
			\end{align*} 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{note} 

	\begin{ex} \lex{lex:limits:limits_colimits:0004}
		\tcr{limits and colimits are unique up to isomorphism} 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item ?Let $(X, \phi) \in \limSet D$ and $Y \in \Obj(\MC)$, then $(Y, \psi) \in \limSet D$ iff there exists $\al \in \Iso_{\MC}(X,Y)$ such that $\psi \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \del^{\MJ}_{\al} = \phi$? 
			\item \tcr{colimits}
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{proof}\
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item 
			\item 
		\end{enumerate}
	\end{proof}
	
	\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:limits_colimits:0005}
		Let $\MJ$, $\MC$ be categories. Suppose that $\MJ$ is small. Let $L \in \prod\limits_{\Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \limSet(D)$. 
	\end{defn}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\section{Fundamental Examples}
	
	\subsection{Products and Coproducts}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MJ$ be a discrete category, $\MC$ a category, $D \in \MC^{\MJ}$ and $(X, \pi) \in \Cone(D)$. Then $(X, \pi)$ is said to be a \tbf{product of $D$}.
	\end{defn}
	
	\begin{note}
		We may think of a product of $D$ as a tuple $(X, )$
	\end{note}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{show that if $\b1$ is terminal, then $X \times \b1 \cong X$.   }
	\end{ex}
	
	\begin{ex}
		\tcr{show that if $\MC$ has products, then $\MC$ has a copy morphism (define a copy morphism) see page 32 in `elementary categories, elementary toposes` by McLarty}. 
	\end{ex}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Equalizers and Coequalizers}
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	
	\subsection{Projective and Inductive Limits}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let $\MJ$ be a \tcr{directed} poset, $\MC$ a category and $D \in \MC^{\MJ}$. Then $D$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC$-projective system}.  
	\end{defn}

	\begin{note}
		We may think of 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item a $\MC$-projective system as a tuple $((X_j)_{j \in J}, (\pi_{j,k})_{(j,k) \in \leq})$ where $(J, \leq)$ is a \tcr{directed} poset, $(X_j)_{j \in J} \subset \Obj(\MC)$ and $(\pi_{j,k})_{(j,k) \in \leq} \subset \Hom_{\MC}$ satisfy that for each $j,k,l \in J$, 
			\begin{enumerate}
				\item $j \leq k$ implies that $\pi_{j,k} \in \Hom_{\MC}(X_k, X_j)$,
				\item $\pi_{j,j} = \id_{X_j}$,
				\item $j \leq k$ and $k \leq l$ implies that $\pi_{j,k} \circ_{\MC} \pi_{k,l} = \pi_{j,l}$.
			\end{enumerate}
			\item a cone over $D$ as a tuple $(X, (\pi_j)_{j \in J})$ where $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $(\pi_j)_{j \in J} \subset \Hom_{\MC}$ satisfy that for each $j,k \in J$, $j \leq k$ implies that $\pi_{j,k} \circ_{\MC} \pi_k = \pi_j$. 
		\end{itemize}
	\end{note}
	
	\tcr{make some diagrams}
	
	\begin{ex}
		Let $\MC$ be a category and $(X_j)_{j \in \N} \subset \Obj(\MC)$. Define $(Y_n)_{n \in \N} \subset \Obj(\MC)$ and $(\pi_{n, k})_{n \leq k} \in \prod\limits_{n \leq k} \Hom_{\MC}(Y_k, Y_n)$ by $Y_n \defeq \prod\limits_{j=1}^n X_j$ and $\pi_{n,k}$.  Suppose that for each  $(\prod_{n \in \N}, (\pi_n)_{n \in \N})$ \tcr{arg1}. 
	\end{ex}

	\begin{defn}
		Let $(\MJ, \MC, D)$ be a $\MC$-projective system and $(X, \phi) \in \Obj(\Cone(D))$. Then $(X, \phi)$ is said to be a $\MC$-projective limit of $(\MJ, \MC, D)$ if $(X, \phi)$ is a limit of $D$. 
	\end{defn}

	
\begin{note}
	We may think of a projective limit if $(\MJ, \MC, D)$ as a cone $(X, (\pi_j)_{j \in J})$ over $D$ satisfying that for each cone $(Y, (\tau_j)_{j \in J})$ over $D$, there exists a unique $\al \in \Hom_{\MC}(Y, X)$ such that $\tau_j = \pi_j \circ_{\MC} \al$. 
\end{note}

\tcr{make some diagrams}
















































\newpage
\section{Completeness}

\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:completeness:0001}
	Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$. Then $\MC$ is said to 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item \tbf{have all $\MJ$-limits} if for each $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$, $\limSet D \neq \varnothing$. 
		\item \tbf{have all $\MJ$-colimits} if for each $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$, $\colimSet D \neq \varnothing$. 
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}

\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:completeness:0002}
	Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$.  
	\begin{itemize}
		\item 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Suppose that $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-limits. Let $L \in \prod\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \limSet D$. Then $L$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC^{\MJ}$-limit choice function}.
			\item We define $\limChoice(\MC^{\MJ}) \defeq \prod\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \limSet D$.
		\end{itemize}
		\item 
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Suppose that $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-colimits. Let $C \in \prod\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \colimSet D$. Then $C$ is said to be a \tbf{$\MC^{\MJ}$-colimit choice function}.
			\item We define $\colimChoice(\MC^{\MJ}) \defeq \prod\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \colimSet D$.
		\end{itemize}
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}


\begin{ex} \lex{ex:limits:completeness:0003}
	Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$.
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item Suppose that $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-limits. Let $L \in \limChoice(\MC^{\MJ})$. Then for each $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$, there exists $\eta^L_{\al} \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2})$ such that $\Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2}) = \{\eta^L_{\al}\}$. 
		\item \tcr{do somethign similar for colimtis}
	\end{enumerate}
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}\
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item Let $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$. Since $L_{D_2}$ is a $D_2$-limit, $L_{D_2}$ is $\Cone(D_2)$-terminal. Thus there exists $\eta^L_{\al} \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2})$ such that $\Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2}) = \{\eta^L_{\al}\}$. 
		\item \tcr{FINISH!!!!}
	\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:completeness:0004}
	Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$. 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item Suppose that $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-limits. Let $L \in \limChoice(\MC^{\MJ})$.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item For $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$, we define $\eta^L_{\al} \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2})$ as in \rex{ex:limits:completeness:0003}. 
			\item We define the \tbf{$L$-limit functor}, denoted $\lim\limits_L: \MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \MC$, by
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\lim\limits_L(D) \defeq \prj_{\Obj(\MC)}(L_D), \quad D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ 
				\item $\lim\limits_L(\al) \defeq \eta^L_{\al}, \quad \al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}$.
			\end{itemize}
		\end{itemize}
		\item \tcr{define something similar for colimits, might need to change notation from $\eta^L_{\al}$ to something else}
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}

\begin{ex} \lex{ex:limits:completeness:0005}
	Let $\MC$ be a category and $\MJ \in \Obj(\Cat)$. 
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item Suppose that $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-limits. Let $L \in \limChoice(\MC^{\MJ})$. Then $\lim\limits_L: \MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \MC$ is a functor.
		\item \tcr{do something similar for colimits}
	\end{enumerate}
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}\
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item 
		\begin{enumerate}
			\item Let $D_1, D_2 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ and $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$. Write $L_{D_1} = (X_1, \phi_1)$ and $L_{D_2} = (X_2, \phi_2)$. Then $\lim\limits_L(D_1) = X_1$ and $\lim\limits_L(D_2) = X_2$. By \rd{def:limits:cones_cocones:0003},  
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2}) 
				& = \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}((X_1, \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_1), (X_2, \phi_2)) \\
				& \subset \Hom_{\MC}(X_1, X_2).
			\end{align*}
			Therefore 
			\begin{align*}
				\lim\limits_L(\al)
				& = \eta^L_{\al} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2}) \\
				& \subset \Hom_{\MC}(X_1, X_2) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\lim\limits_L(D_1), \lim\limits_L(D_2)).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $D_1, D_2, D_3 \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$, $\al \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_1, D_2)$ and $\be \in \Hom_{\MC^{\MJ}}(D_2, D_3)$. By \rex{ex:limits:completeness:0003},
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\Hom_{\Cone(D_2)}(\Cn_{\al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_2}) = \{\eta^L_{\al}\}$, \item $\Hom_{\Cone(D_3)}(\Cn_{\be}(L_{D_2}), L_{D_3}) = \{\eta^L_{\be}\}$,
				\item $\Hom_{\Cone(D_3)}(\Cn_{\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_3}) = \{\eta^L_{\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al}\}$. 
			\end{itemize}
			By definition \rd{def:limits:cones_cocones:0003},
			\begin{itemize}
				\item $\eta^L_{\al} \in \Hom_{\MC}(X_1, X_2)$ and $\phi_2 \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\al}) = \al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_1$
				\item $\eta^L_{\be} \in \Hom_{\MC}(X_2, X_3)$ and $\phi_3 \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\be}) = \be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_2$.
				\item 
			\end{itemize}
			Therefore $\eta^L_{\be} \circ_{\MC} \eta^L_{\al} \in \Hom_{\MC}(X_1, X_3)$ and
			\begin{align*}
				\phi_3 \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\be} \circ_{\MC} \eta^L_{\al}) 
				& = \phi_3 \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} [\Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\be}) \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\al})] \\
				& = [\phi_3 \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\be})] \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\al}) \\
				& = [\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_2] \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\al}) \\
				& = \be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} [\phi_2 \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \Del^{\MJ}(\eta^L_{\al}) ] \\
				& = \be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} [\al \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_1] \\
				& = [\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al] \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_1.
			\end{align*}
			Hence 
			\begin{align*}
				\eta^L_{\be} \circ_{\MC} \eta^L_{\al} 
				& \in \Hom_{\Cone(D_3)}(X_1, (\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al) \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \phi_1, (X_3, \phi_3)) \\
				& = \Hom_{\Cone(D_3)}(\Cn_{\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al}(L_{D_1}), L_{D_3}) \\
				& = \{\eta^L_{\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al}\}.
			\end{align*} 
			Thus 
			\begin{align*}
				\lim\limits_L(\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al)
				& = \eta^L_{\be \circ_{\MC^{\MJ}} \al} \\
				& = \eta^L_{\be} \circ_{\MC} \eta^L_{\al} \\
				& = \lim\limits_L(\be) \circ_{\MC} \lim\limits_L(\al).
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$. Write $L_D = (X, \phi)$. \rex{} \tcr{ref prev ex} implies that $\Cone(\cdot): \MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \Cat$ and 
			\begin{align*}
				\Cn_{\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}} 
				& = \Cone(\cdot)(\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}) \\
				& = \id_{\Cone(D)}^{\Cat}.
			\end{align*} 
			Then  
			\begin{align*}
				\Cn_{\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}}(L_D) 
				& = \id_{\Cone(D)}^{\Cat}(L_D) \\
				& = L_D.
			\end{align*}
			Since $L_D$ is $\Cone(D)$-terminal,
			\begin{align*}
				\lim\limits_L(\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}})
				& = \eta^L_{\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}} \\
				& \in \Hom_{\Cone(D)}(\Cn_{\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}}}(L_D), L_D) \\
				& = \Hom_{\Cone(D)}(L_D, L_D) \\
				& = \{\id_{L_D}^{\Cone(D)}\}. 
			\end{align*}
			By \rd{} \tcr{ref cone def}, 
			\begin{align*}
				\id_{L_D}^{\Cone(D)} 
				& = \id_{L_D}^{(\Del^{\MJ} \doar D)} \\
				& = \id_{(X, \phi)}^{(\Del^{\MJ} \doar D)} \\
				& = \id_X^{\MC}.
			\end{align*}
			Therefore
			\begin{align*}
				\lim\limits_L(\id_D^{\MC^{\MJ}})
				& = \id_{L_D}^{\Cone(D)} \\
				& = \id_X^{\MC} \\
				& = \id_{\lim\limits_L(D)}^{\MC}.
			\end{align*}
		\end{enumerate}
		Hence $\lim\limits_L: \MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \MC$ is a functor. 
		\item \tcr{colimit functor}
	\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{ex}
	For a choice of $L$, we get a functor $\lim\limits_L$. Rephrasing this, for each object (a set $L \in \limChoice(\MC^{\MJ})$)  we get a an object (a functor $\lim\limits_L: \MC^{\MJ} \rightarrow \MC$). Maybe we can consider $\limChoice(\MC^{\MJ})$ as a category and consider an arrow $f: L \rightarrow M$ as a function $f: \bigcup\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \Cone(D) \rightarrow \bigcup\limits_{D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})} \Cone(D)$ such that $f \circ_{\bSet} L = M$, i.e. for each $D \in \Obj(\MC^{\MJ})$ $f(L_D) = M_D$, \tcr{idk, think about}
\end{ex}









\begin{defn} \ld{def:limits:completeness:0007}
	Let $\MC$ be a category. Then $\MC$ is said to be 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item \tbf{complete} if for each $J \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-limits.
		\item \tbf{cocomplete} if for each $J \in \Obj(\Cat)$, $\MC$ has all $\MJ$-colimits.
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}



















































\newpage
\chapter{Yoneda Lemma}

\section{Representable Functors}

\begin{ex} \lex{ex:yoneda:rep_funct:0001}
	Let $\MC$ be a category, $(A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$ and $(f_1, f_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2))$. Then for each $h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2)$, $f_2 \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} f_1 \in \Hom_{\MC}(B_1, B_2)$. 
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}
	By definition of $\op{\MC} \times \MC$, we have that
	\begin{itemize}
		\item 
		\begin{align*}
			A_1, B_1
			& \in \Obj(\op{\MC}) \\
			& = \Obj(\MC),
		\end{align*}
		\begin{align*}
			f_1 
			& \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A_1, B_1) \\
			& = \Hom_{\MC}(B_1, A_1),
		\end{align*}
		\item $A_2, B_2 \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $f_2 \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_2, B_2)$.
	\end{itemize}
	Therefore, for each $h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2)$, $f_2 \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} f_1 \in \Hom_{\MC}(B_1, B_2)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{note}
	If $\MC$ is locally small, then for each $(A_1, A_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2) \in \Obj(\bSet)$.
\end{note}

\begin{defn} \ld{def:yoneda:rep_funct:0002}
	Let $\MC$ be a locally small category. We define the \tbf{Hom-functor of $\MC$}, denoted $\Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, \cdot):\op{\MC} \times \MC \rightarrow \bSet$, by 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item $\Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, \cdot)(A_1, A_2) \defeq \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2), \quad (A_1, A_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$
		\item $\Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, \cdot)(f_1,f_2)(h) \defeq f_2 \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} f_1, \quad (f_1, f_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2)), h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2)$
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}

\begin{ex} \lex{ex:yoneda:rep_funct:0003}
	Let $\MC$ be a locally small category. Then $\Hom_{\MC}:\op{\MC} \times \MC \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor. 
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}
	Set $H \defeq \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, \cdot)$.
	\begin{enumerate}
	\item \tcr{The previous ex} implies that for each $(A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$ and $(f_1, f_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2))$, 
	\begin{align*}
		H(f_1, f_2) 
		& \in \Hom_{\bSet}(\Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2), \Hom_{\MC}(B_1, B_2)) \\
		& = \Hom_{\bSet}(H(A_1, A_2), H(B_1, B_2))
	\end{align*}
	\item Let $(A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2), (C_1, C_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$, $(f_1, f_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2))$ and $(g_1, g_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((B_1, B_2), (C_1, C_2))$. Then for each $h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2)$, we have that 
	\begin{align*}
		H((g_1, g_2) \circ_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}(f_1, f_2))(h)
		& = H(g_1 \circ_{\op{\MC}} f_1, g_2 \circ_{\MC} f_2)(h) \\
		& = H(f_1 \circ_{\MC} g_1, g_2 \circ_{\MC} f_2)(h) \\
		& = (g_2 \circ_{\MC} f_2) \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} (f_1 \circ_{\MC} g_1) \\
		& = g_2 \circ_{\MC} (f_2 \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} f_1) \circ_{\MC} g_1 \\
		& = g_2 \circ_{\MC} [H(f_1, f_2)(h)] \circ_{\MC} g_1 \\
		& = H(g_1, g_2)(H(f_1, f_2)(h)) \\
		& = H(g_1, g_2) \circ_{\bSet} H(f_1, f_2)(h).
	\end{align*}
	Thus $H((g_1, g_2) \circ_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}(f_1, f_2)) = H(g_1, g_2) \circ_{\bSet}  H(f_1, f_2)$. Since $(A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2), (C_1, C_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$, $(f_1, f_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2))$ and $(g_1, g_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((B_1, B_2), (C_1, C_2))$ are arbitrary, we have that for each $(A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2), (C_1, C_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$, $(f_1, f_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((A_1, A_2), (B_1, B_2))$ and $(g_1, g_2) \in \Hom_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}((B_1, B_2), (C_1, C_2))$, $H((g_1, g_2) \circ_{\op{\MC} \times \MC}(f_1, f_2)) = H(g_1, g_2) \circ_{\bSet} H(f_1, f_2)$. 
	\item Let $(A_1, A_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$. Then for each $h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2)$,
	\begin{align*}
		H(\id_{(A_1, A_2)}^{\op{\MC} \times \MC})(h)
		& = H(\id_{A_1}^{\op{\MC}}, \id_{A_2}^{\MC})(h) \\
		& = H(\id_{A_1}^{\MC}, \id_{A_2}^{\MC})(h) \\
		& = \id_{A_2}^{\MC} \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} \id_{A_1}^{\MC} \\
		& = h \\
		& = \id_{\Hom_{\MC}(A_1, A_2)}^{\bSet}(h) \\
		& = \id_{H(A_1, A_2)}^{\bSet}(h).
	\end{align*}
	Thus $H(\id_{(A_1, A_2)}^{\op{\MC} \times \MC}) = \id_{H(A_1, A_2)}^{\bSet}$. Since $(A_1, A_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $(A_1, A_2) \in \Obj(\op{\MC} \times \MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(\id_{(A_1, A_2)}^{\op{\MC} \times \MC}) = \id_{H(A_1, A_2)}^{\bSet}$.
	\end{enumerate}
	Hence $\Hom_{\MC}: \op{\MC} \times \MC \rightarrow \bSet$ is a functor. 
\end{proof}

\begin{note}
	If $\MC$ is locally small, \rex{ex:basics:contructs:products:0006} implies that for each $X \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(X, \cdot): \MC \rightarrow \bSet$ and $\Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X): \op{\MC} \rightarrow \bSet$ are functors.
\end{note}

\begin{ex} \lex{ex:yoneda:rep_funct:0004}
	Let $\MC$ be a category. Suppose that $\MC$ is locally small. Then 
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item for each $X \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$, $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot) = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X)$
		\item for each $X \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\Hom_{\MC}(X, \cdot) = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(\cdot, X)$
	\end{enumerate}
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}
	We note that \rex{} \tcr{(ref ex)} implies that $\op{(\op{\MC})} = \MC$. So $\op{(\op{\MC})} \times \op{\MC} = \MC\times \op{\MC}$.
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item Let $X \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$. Then $X \in \Obj(\MC)$.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item Let $A \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$. Then $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ and
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot)(A)
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(\cdot, \cdot)(X, A) \\
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, A) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(A, X) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, \cdot)(A, X) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X)(A). 
			\end{align*}
			\item Let $A,B \in \Obj(\op{\MC})$ and $f \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(A, B)$ and $h \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, A)$. Then $A,B \in \Obj(\MC)$, $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(B,A)$ and $h \in \Hom_{\MC}(A, X)$. Thus $(\id_X^{\MC}, f) \in \Hom_{\MC \times \op{\MC}}((X, A), (X, B))$ and
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot)(f)(h)
				& = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(\cdot, \cdot)(\id_X^{\MC}, f)(h) \\
				& = f \circ_{\op{\MC}} h \circ_{\op{\MC}} \id_X^{\MC} \\
				& = \id_X^{\MC} \circ_{\MC} h \circ_{\MC} f \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, \cdot)(f, \id_X^{\MC})(h) \\
				& = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X)(f)(h)
			\end{align*}
			Since $h \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, A)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $h \in \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, A)$, $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot)(f)(h) = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X)(f)(h)$. Thus $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot)(f) = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X)(f)$.
		\end{itemize}
		Hence $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot) = \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X)$.
		\item \tcr{FINISH!!!} (similar)
	\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{defn} \ld{def:yoneda:rep_funct:0005}
	Let $\MC$ be a category. Suppose that $\MC$ is locally small. Let $F: \MC \rightarrow \bSet$. 
	\begin{itemize}
		\item Let $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\phi : F \Rightarrow \Hom_{\MC}(X, \cdot)$. Then $(X, \phi)$ is said to be a \tbf{representation of $F$} if $\phi$ is a natural isomorphism.
		\item Then $F$ is said to be \tbf{representable} if there exists $X \in \Obj(\MC)$ and $\phi:F \Rightarrow \Hom_{\MC}(X, \cdot)$ such that $(X, \phi)$ is a representation of $F$. 
	\end{itemize}
\end{defn}

\begin{ex} \lex{ex:yoneda:rep_funct:0006}
	Let $\MC$ be a category. Suppose that $\MC$ is small. Let $X \in \Obj(\MC)$. Let $1 \in \Obj(\bSet)$. Suppose that $1$ is $\bSet$-terminal. Then
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item $X$ is $\MC$-initial iff $\Hom_{\MC}(X, \cdot) \cong_{\bSet^{\MC}} \Del^{\MC}_1$.
		\item $X$ is $\MC$-terminal iff $\Hom_{\op{\MC}}(\cdot, X) \cong_{\bSet^{\op{\MC}}} \Del^{\op{\MC}}_1$.
	\end{enumerate}
\end{ex}

\begin{proof}
	Define $F \in \bSet^{\MC}$ by $F \defeq \Hom_{\MC}(X, \cdot)$.
	\begin{enumerate}
		\item \rex{15020} implies that $\phi^{(F,1)} \in \Hom_{\bSet^{\MC}}(F, \Del^{\MC}_1)$. \rex{15015} implies that there exists $x \in 1$ such that $1 = \{x\}$.
		\begin{itemize}
			\item $(\implies)$: \\
			Suppose that $X$ is $\MC$-initial. Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Since $F(A) = \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$, \rex{15015.1} implies that $F(A)$ is $\bSet$-terminal. Since $1$ is $\bSet$-terminal, \rex{15014} implies that $F(A) \cong_{\bSet} 1$ and $\Hom_{\bSet}(F(A), 1) = \Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), 1)$. Therefore 
			\begin{align*}
				\phi^{(F,1)}_A 
				& \in \Hom_{\bSet}(F(A), 1) \\
				& = \Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), 1) \\
				& = \Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), \Del^{\MC}_1(A)).
			\end{align*}
			Since $A \in \Obj(\MC)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, $\phi^{(F,1)}_A \in \Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), \Del^{\MC}_1(A))$. Thus $\phi^{(F,1)}:F \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_1$ is a natural isomorphism. \rex{15011.5} then implies that $\phi^{(F,1)} \in \Iso_{\bSet^{\MC}}(F, \Del^{\MC}_1)$. Since $\Iso_{\bSet^{\MC}}(F, \Del^{\MC}_1) \neq \varnothing$, we have that $F \cong_{\bSet^{\MC}} \Del^{\MC}_1$.
			\item $(\impliedby)$: \\
			Suppose that $F \cong_{\bSet^{\MC}} \Del^{\MC}_1$. Then there exists $\phi \in \Iso_{\bSet^{\MC}}(F, \Del^{\MC}_1)$. \rex{15011.5} then implies that $\phi: F \Rightarrow \Del^{\MC}_1$ is a natural isomorphism. Let $A \in \Obj(\MC)$. Then 
			\begin{align*}
				\phi_A 
				& \in \Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), \Del^{\MC}_1(A)) \\
				& = \Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), 1).
			\end{align*}
			Since $\Iso_{\bSet}(F(A), 1) \neq \varnothing$ and $1$ is $\bSet$-terminal, we have that  
			\begin{align*}
				\Hom_{\MC}(X, A) 
				& = F(A) \\
				& \cong_{\bSet} 1 \\
				& \cong_{\bSet} \{\varnothing\}, \quad \text{(by \rex{15015})}.
			\end{align*}
			Thus there exists $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(X, A) = \{f\}$. Since $A \in \Obj(\MX)$ is arbitrary, we have that for each $A \in \Obj(\MC)$, there exists $f \in \Hom_{\MC}(X, A)$ such that $\Hom_{\MC}(X, A) = \{f\}$. Hence $X$ is $\MC$-initial.
		\end{itemize}
		\item We have that 
		\begin{align*}
			\text{$X$ is $\MC$-terminal}
			& \iff \text{$X$ is $\op{\MC}$-initial}, \quad \text{(by \rex{15012.1})} \\
			& \iff \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot) \cong_{\bSet^{\op{\MC}}} \Del^{\op{\MC}}_1, \quad \text{(by \tcr{(ref) prev part})} \\
			& \iff \Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X) \cong_{\bSet^{\op{\MC}}} \Del^{\op{\MC}}_1, \quad \text{(by \tcr{(ref) prev ex about $\Hom_{\MC}(\cdot, X) = \Hom_{\op{\MC}}(X, \cdot)$})}
		\end{align*}
	\end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{ex}
	Let $\MC$ be a category, $F:\MC \rightarrow \bSet$, $X \in \Obj(\bSet)$ and $(A, f) \in (X \doar F)$. Suppose that $\MC$ is locally small, $X$ is $\bSet$-terminal and $(A,f)$ is a universal morphism from $X$ to $F$. Then 
\end{ex}

	\appendix
	\chapter{App}
	
	\section{Reading Diagrams and associated digraphs of diagrams}
	
	\begin{defn}
		Let 
		\[ 
		\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
			C \arrow[r, "g"] \arrow[d, "h"'] & A \arrow[d, "f"] \\
			A \arrow[r, "f"'] & B\\
		\end{tikzcd}
		\implies
		\begin{tikzcd}[baseline= 7]
			C \arrow[bend right=60, swap]{r}{h} \arrow[bend right=-60]{r}{g} & A  \\
		\end{tikzcd}
		\]
		
		see an intro to the language of category theory by roman for description
	\end{defn}
	
	
	\begin{defn}
		A diagram is said to be \tbf{commutative} if for each path of length $\geq 2$, in the associated digraph gives the same morphism.  
	\end{defn}
